Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
The Majbub Dispute: Full Mahr vs Half Mahr
Delving into the intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr with a physically incapable husband.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the mahr of a woman who secludes with a castrated (majbub) husband, and explain the reasoning (qiyas khafi) behind each position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: full mahr because she enabled tamkin; Sahibayn: half mahr because intercourse is impossible.

A key intra-Hanafi dispute arises when the husband is physically incapable of intercourse, such as a majbub (castrated) man. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the disagreement: Abu Hanifa holds that valid seclusion with such a husband still obligates full mahr, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that only half is due. We examine the subtle analogy (qiyas khafi) that underlies Abu Hanifa's position and the counter-analogy of the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A valid marriage contract exists, the husband is castrated (majbub) or emasculated (khasi), valid seclusion occurs, then the husband divorces the wife.
The ruling applies only after divorce or death; seclusion alone does not trigger mahr.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling
Full mahr is wajib. The wife has performed her duty of tamkin (submission for sexual access) to the utmost of her capacity.
The illa (effective cause) is the wife's submission, not the husband's capacity.
3
State the Sahibayn's ruling
Half mahr is due. They analogize the majbub to a sick man; the obligation of full mahr is based on the possibility of intercourse, which is absent here.
They distinguish the impotent ('anin) from the castrated, because the impotent still has the organ; the castrated lacks it entirely.
4
Analyze the qiyas khafi
Abu Hanifa's reasoning is a subtle analogy (qiyas khafi): the wife's obligation is to submit, not to guarantee intercourse. The Sahibayn use a jali (clear) analogy to the sick man. Identify which is more appropriate based on the source.
The text supports Abu Hanifa's view by giving the response to the objection on ratqa'.
5
Determine the thamarah
Practical difference: on divorce after seclusion, she gets full or half mahr. The mufta bihi is full mahr.

ويقيموها مقامه في حق الإحصاء إن تصادقا على عدم الدخول وإن أقرا به لزمهما حكم الإحصاء، وإن أقر به أحدهما صدق في حق نفسه دون صاحبه كما في المبسوط، وفي حرمة البنات وحلها للأول والميراث حتى لو أبانها ثم مات في عدتها لم ترثه كما في المجتبى، وفي الرجعة فلا يصير مراجعاً بالخلوة ولا رجعة له بعد الطلاق الصريح بعد الخلوة، وأما في حق وقوع طلاق آخر ففيه روايتان والأقرب إلى الصواب الوقوع لأن الأحكام لما اختلفت يجب كما القول بالوقوع. كذا في الذخيرة وجعلها في المجتبى كالوطء في حق التزويج فإنها تزوج تزوج الثيب وهو ضعيف لما قدمنا من أنها تزوج بعدها كالأبكار إذا قالت لم يدخل بي. وفي غاية البيان: إذا خلا بها في النكاح الموقوف تكون إجازة لأن الخلوة بالأجنبية حرام. وقال بعظهم نفس الخلوة لا تكون إجازة ا هـ . وزاد في المجتبى في عدم كونها كالوطء في منعها نفسها للمهر، ولا ينبغي إدخاله هنا لأنه لو وطئها حقيقة فلها منعه بعده عند أبي حنيفة، نعم يتأتى على قولهما كما لا يخفى. وفي المجتبى : الموت أقيم مقام الدخول في حكم العدة والمهر وفيما سواهما كالعدم وفي شرح الناصحي : فإن ماتت الأم قبل يدخل بها فابنتها له حلال اهـ .

قوله : (ولو) محبوباً أو عنيناً أو خصياً) أي الخلوة بلا الموانع المذكورة كالوطء، ولو كان الزوج مجبوباً أو نحوه فلها كمال المهر بعد الطلاق والخلوة عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : كذلك الخصي والعنين وفي المجبوب عليه النصف لأنه أعبر المريض بخلاف العنين لأن الحكم أدير على سلامة الآلة. ولأبي حنيفة أن المستحق عليها التسليم في حق السحق وقد أتت به . والحاصل أن الخلوة الصحيحة عنده هي التمكين من الوطء بأقصى ما في وسعها. فإن قلت : يلزم على هذا أن توجب الخلوة بالرتقاء كمال المهر إذ ليس هنا تسليم غيره قلنا: إن الرتق قد يزول فكان هذا التسليم منتظراً غيره فلم يجب كمال المهر لعدم التسليم كاملاً. كذا في غاية البيان. والجب القطع ومنه المجبوب الخصي الذي استؤصل ذكره وخصيتاه، وقد جب جباً وخصاه نزع خصيتيه بخصيه خصاء على فعال والإخصاء في معناه خطأ. وأما الخصي على النسب في بعض الصور كما قدمناه عنه وكان عليه أن يستثني أيضاً وجوب العدة فإنه من فروع الخلوة كما ذكره المؤلف هنا قوله : (وفي حرمة البنات) أي ولم يقيموها مقامه في ذلك والكلام في الخلوة الصحيحة كما صرح به في التبيين والفتح وغيرهما، فما حرره في عقد الفرائد مما حاصله أن حرمة البنات بالخلوة الصحيحة لا خلاف فيها بين الصاحبين واختلفوا في الفاسدة قال محمد : لا تحرم. وحرمتها الثاني ضعيف وما ادعاه من عدم الخلاف ممنوع كما أوضحه في النهر.
قوله : (وأما في حق وقوع طلاق آخر الخ ظاهره أنها قائمة مقامه على ما هو المختار من الوقوع مع أنه من فروع وجوب العدة كما في النهر قال : وهذا مما غفل عنه في عقد الفرائد والبحر

فعل فقياس وإن لم نسمعه، والمفعول خصي على فعيل والجمع خصيان . كذا في المغرب. وفي الغاية : الظاهر أن قطع الخصيتين ليس بشرط في المجبوب ولذا اقتصر الأسبيجابي على قطع الذكر. وأشار المصنف إلى صحة خلوة الخنثى بالأولى وإلى أن نسب الولد يثبت من المجبوب وهو بالإجماع. كذا في البدائع. وذكر التمرتاشي : إن علم أنه ينزل يثبت وإن علم خلافه فلا وعليها العدة والأولى أحسن، وعلم القاضي أنه ينزل أولاً ربما يتعذر أن . يتعسر في فتح القدير قوله : (وتجب العدة فيها أي تجب العدة على المطلقة بعد الخلوة احتياطاً، وإنما أفرد هذا الحكم مع أنه معلوم من جعلها كالوطء لأن هذا الحكم لا يخص الصحيحة بل حكم الخلوة ولو فاسدة احتياطاً استحساناً لتوهم الشغل والعدة حق الشرع والولد لأجل النسب فلا تصدق في إبطال حق الغير بخلاف المهر لأنه مال لا يحتاط في إيجابه. وذكر القدوري في شرحه أن المانع إن كان شرعياً تجب العدة لثبوت التمكن حقيقة وإن كان حقيقياً كالمرض والصغر لا يجب لانعدام التمكن حقيقة. واختاره قاضيخان في فتاواه لكن في فتح القدير: إلا أن الأوجه على هذا أن يختص الصغير بغير القادر والمرض بالمدنف لثبوت التمكن حقيقة في غيرهما ا هـ . والمذهب وجوب العدة مطلقاً لأنه نص محمد في الجامع الصغير، وظاهره أنها واجبة قضاء وديانة. وفي المجتبى : وذكر العتابي تكلم مشايخنا في العدة الواجبة بالخلوة الصحيحة أنها واجبة طاهراً : أما على الحقيقة فقيل لو تزوجت وهي متيقنة بعدم الدخول حل لها ديانة لا قضاء اهـ. وفي المجتبى : والخلوة الصحيحة في النكاح الفاسد لا توجب العدة قوله : (وتستحب المتعة لكل مطلقة إلا للمفوضة قبل الوطء وهي بكسر الواو من فوضت أمرها إلى وليها وزوجها بلا مهر، وبفتحها من فوضها وليها إلى الزوج بلا مهر فإن المتعة لها واجبة على زوجها كسائر ديونها كما ذكره الأسبيجابي، فالمراد بالواجب هنا اللازم. وأخرج الواجب عن أن يكون مستحباً بناء على الاصطلاح، وشمل كلامه من طلقها قبل الدخول وقد سمى لها مهراً فإنها مستحبة على ما في المبسوط والمحيط والمختصر، وعلى رواية التأويلات وصاحب التيسير وصاحب الكشاف
قوله : (كذا في الذخيرة أقول : تمام عبارة الذخيرة ثم هذا الطلاق يكون رجعياً أو بائناً ذكر شيخ الإسلام أنه يكون بائناً قوله : (وأشار إلى صحة خلوة الأنثى بالأولى قال في النهر : يجب أن يراد به من ظهر حاله أما المشكل فنكاحه موقوف إلى أن يتبين حاله ولهذا لا يزوجه وليه من يختنه لأن النكاح الموقوف لا يفيد إباحة النظر .
كذا
في النهاية. وأفاد في المبسوط أن حاله يتبين بالبلوغ فإن ظهرت فيه علامة الرجال وقد زوجه أبوه امرأة حكم بصحة نكاحه من حين عقد الأب فإن لم يصل إليها أجل كالعنين وإن تزوج رجلاً تبين بطلانه وهذا صريح في عدم صحة خلوته قبل ذلك. وبهذا التقرير علمت أن ما نقله في الأشباه عن الأصل لو زوجه أبوه رجلاً فوصل إليه وإلا فلا علم لي بذلك أو امرأة فبلغ فوصل إليها
And they place it (seclusion) in the position of (actual intercourse) regarding ihsan if they agree on non-entry; and if they both admit entry, the ruling of ihsan becomes binding on them; and if one of them admits it, he is believed regarding himself but not regarding his partner, as in al-Mabsut. And regarding the prohibition of daughters and her being lawful for the first (husband) and inheritance, even if he irrevocably divorced her then died during her iddah, she does not inherit from him, as in al-Mujtaba. And regarding raj'ah, he does not become a revoker by seclusion, and he has no right of return after explicit divorce after seclusion. As for the occurrence of another divorce, there are two narrations; the closest to correctness is occurrence because when rulings differ, occurrence must be affirmed. Thus in al-Dhakhira. And in al-Mujtaba, it is made like intercourse regarding marriage, for she marries as a non-virgin, which is weak because she marries after it like virgins if she says he did not enter me. In Ghayat al-Bayan: If he secluded with her in a suspended marriage, it is a ratification because seclusion with a foreign woman is forbidden. And some said seclusion itself is not a ratification. And he added in al-Mujtaba regarding it not being like intercourse in preventing herself from taking the mahr, and it should not be entered here because if he actually had intercourse with her, she can prevent him after that according to Abu Hanifa; yes, it applies according to them, as is not hidden. In al-Mujtaba: Death is placed in the position of entry regarding the rulings of iddah and mahr, and in other respects it is like non-existence. In Sharh al-Nasihi: If the mother dies before he enters with her, her daughter is lawful for him. End quote. His statement: '(And even if ) he is castrated, or impotent, or emasculated' i.e. seclusion without the mentioned impediments is like intercourse. If the husband is castrated or similar, she gets the full mahr after divorce and seclusion according to Abu Hanifa. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: likewise for the emasculated and impotent, but for the castrated, half (is due) because he is like the sick patient, unlike the impotent because the ruling is based on the soundness of the organ. For Abu Hanifa, what is owed from her is submission in terms of lying down, and she has performed it. The conclusion is that valid seclusion according to him is enabling intercourse to the utmost of her capacity. If you say: This would necessitate that seclusion with a woman with a closed vagina (ratqa') obligates full mahr since there is no other submission here? We say: Ratqa' may be removed, so this submission is awaiting another, so full mahr is not obligatory due to incomplete submission. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. Al-jabb is cutting, hence al-majbub; al-khasi is one whose penis and testicles are removed. And he said (wa qawlihi): (Regarding prohibition of daughters) meaning they do not place it in that position, and the discussion concerns valid seclusion. What he wrote in 'Aqd al-Fara'id concludes that prohibition of daughters by valid seclusion is not disputed between the two companions; they differed regarding invalid (seclusion): Muhammad said it does not cause prohibition, and its prohibition is weak. His claim of no dispute is rejected. His statement: (As for the occurrence of another divorce, its apparent meaning is that it stands in its position according to the chosen view of occurrence, although it is a branch of obligation of iddah. This is something overlooked in 'Aqd al-Fara'id and al-Bahr. Then it becomes a qiyas even if we did not hear it, and the passive participle is khasi on the pattern of fa'il, plural khisyan. In al-Ghaya: apparently cutting off both testicles is not a condition in al-majbub, hence al-Usbijabi restricted to cutting the penis. The author indicated the validity of seclusion of a hermaphrodite a fortiori, and that lineage of a child from a castrated man is established by consensus. In al-Bada'i'. Al-Tamartashi mentioned: if it is known that he ejaculates, it is established; if known otherwise, no, and she must observe iddah, and the first is better. The judge's knowledge of whether he ejaculates or not may be difficult. In Fath al-Qadir: His statement: (And iddah is obligatory in it) meaning iddah is obligatory on the divorced woman after seclusion as a precaution. He singled out this ruling although it is known from making it like intercourse, because this ruling is not specific to valid seclusion but is the ruling of seclusion even if invalid, as a precaution by istihsan due to possibility of occupation; iddah is a right of the Shari'ah and the child is for lineage, so she is not believed in nullifying the right of another, unlike mahr because it is property and caution is not exercised in its obligation. Al-Quduri mentioned in his commentary that if the impediment is shar'i, iddah is obligatory due to actual capability; if it is physical like illness or minority, it is not obligatory due to lack of actual capability. Qadikhan adopted this in his Fatawa, but in Fath al-Qadir: except that the more appropriate view is that minority is restricted to the incapable, and illness to the chronically ill, because actual capability exists in others. The madhhab is that iddah is obligatory absolutely because it is the text of Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir, and its apparent meaning is that it is obligatory judicially and religiously. In al-Mujtaba: al-'Atabi said our scholars spoke about the iddah obligatory by valid seclusion that it is obligatory while pure: as for reality, it is said if she marries while certain of non-entry, it is permissible for her religiously but not judicially. In al-Mujtaba: Valid seclusion in an invalid marriage does not obligate iddah. His statement: (And mut'ah is recommended for every divorced woman except for the mufawwidah before intercourse) with kasr of the waw, one who delegated her affair to her guardian and husband without a mahr; with fatha, one whom her guardian delegated to the husband without a mahr, then mut'ah is obligatory on her husband like other debts, as al-Usbijabi mentioned, so the intended meaning of wajib here is binding. He excluded the obligatory from being recommended based on terminology. His speech includes one who divorces before entry and has named a mahr, for she is recommended according to al-Mabsut, al-Muhit, and al-Mukhtasar, and according to the narration of al-Ta'wilat, the author of al-Taysir, and the author of al-Kashshaf. His statement: (Thus in al-Dhakhira) I say: the complete phrase of al-Dhakhira is 'then this divorce is revocable or irrevocable; Shaykh al-Islam mentioned that it is irrevocable.' His statement: (And he indicated the validity of seclusion of the female a fortiori) said in al-Nahr: it must mean one whose condition is apparent; as for the ambiguous one, his marriage is suspended until his condition becomes clear, and for this reason his guardian does not marry him to one who circumcises him because the suspended marriage does not permit looking. Thus in al-Nihaya. In al-Mabsut, his condition becomes clear at puberty: if a sign of masculinity appears and his father married him to a woman, the validity of his marriage is ruled from the time of the father's contract; if he does not reach her, he is given a deadline like the impotent; and if he marries a man, its invalidity becomes clear, and this is explicit in the lack of validity of his seclusion before that. By this exposition, you know that what he narrated in al-Ashbah from al-Asl: 'if his father married him to a man and he reached him, then... otherwise I have no knowledge of that, or a woman and he reached puberty and reached her'
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion probe on the rulings of valid seclusion (khalwah sahihah) in marriage. The author discusses in which aspects valid seclusion is treated like actual intercourse and in which it is not. The main intra-Hanafi dispute concerns the case where the husband is majbub (castrated) or khasi (emasculated). Abu Hanifa holds that valid seclusion with such a husband entitles the wife to full mahr because she has enabled intercourse to the utmost of her capacity. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that only half mahr is due because actual intercourse is impossible, analogizing to the case of a sick man. The passage also clarifies that valid seclusion does not cause prohibition of daughters (contrary to some views) and that iddah is obligatory after any seclusion (valid or invalid) as a precaution by istihsan due to the possibility of impregnation, even if the marriage is fasid. The exception is seclusion in an invalid marriage does not obligate iddah according to al-Mujtaba. The text also touches on the mut'ah (consolatory gift) for divorced women, distinguishing between the mufawwidah (woman without fixed dower) and others.

Key Terms
المجبوب (al-majbub): A man whose penis has been cut off (castrated), making him permanently incapable of penetrative intercourse.
الخصي (al-khasi): A man whose testicles have been removed (emasculated). The text notes that the condition may also involve removal of the penis.
العنين (al-'anin): A man who is impotent, i.e., unable to achieve or maintain an erection. His reproductive organ is intact but non-functional.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school regarding the mahr of a woman who validly secludes with a castrated (majbub) husband and then divorces?
A) She gets full mahr.
B) She gets half mahr.
C) She gets nothing.
D) The mahr is deferred until the husband recovers.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that valid seclusion with a physically incapable husband obligates full mahr, as the wife's duty is submission, not actual intercourse; the Sahibayn's dissenting view makes an exception only for permanent castration.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
6 min
The Validity of Shighar Marriage and Mahr al-Mithl
Ruling on shighar marriage and the obligation of mahr al-mithl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shighar marriage and explain why mahr al-mithl is wajib.

Core Idea
Shighar marriage is valid but requires mahr al-mithl because the prohibition was due to lack of dower.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on shighar marriage, where one marriage is made the dower for another. Although a hadith forbids this practice, the Hanafi school validates the contract by requiring the husband to pay mahr al-mithl (the proper dower). The key is distinguishing between invalid dower and invalid marriage. By understanding this ruling, you will see how Hanafi usul reconciles a prohibition with contract validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is shighar marriage? State the Hanafi ruling: the marriage contract is valid (sahih) and mahr al-mithl is obligatory (wajib).
Shighar: marriage of a female ward on condition that the other party marries his ward, with no dower besides the other marriage.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith in the six books forbids shighar. Why do Hanafis not declare the marriage invalid? Identify the proof they use: analogy (qiyas) to a marriage where the dower is wine or a pig.
The analogy: just as a marriage dowered with an invalid item (wine/pig) is valid with mahr al-mithl, so is shighar.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the dalil prove the ruling? The prohibition was due to the absence of a proper dower (khuluww 'an al-mahr). By requiring mahr al-mithl, the element of prohibition is removed, so the contract stands.
The Hanafis interpret the hadith as applying to the dower condition, not the form of the contract.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds shighar as invalid (batil) based on the apparent meaning of the hadith. Understand the difference: Shafi'is consider the condition itself invalid, while Hanafis separate the contract from the dower.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul principles.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Why is the Hanafi position mufta bihi? It relies on sound qiyas and preserves the marriage's validity, which is preferred when the woman's rights can be protected through mahr al-mithl.
The Hanafi position is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب مهر المثل في الشغار لأنه سمى ما لا يصح صداقاً فيصح العقد ويجب مهر المثل كما إذا سـ خمراً أو خنزيراً. والشغار في اللغة الخلوة يقال شعر الكلب إذا رفع إحدى رجليه ليبول، وبلدة شاغرة إذا كانت خالية من السلطان وأما في الاصطلاح فتزويجه موليته على أن يزوجه الآخر موليته ليكون أحد العقدين عوضاً عن الآخر، سواء كانت المولية بنتاً أو أختاً أو أمة، سمي به لخلوه عن المهر. وإنما قيدنا بأن يكون أحدهما صداقاً عن الآخر لأنه لو لم يكن كذلك بأن قال زوجتك بنتي على أن تزوجني بنتك ولم يزد عليه فقبل الآخر فإنه لا يكون شغاراً اصطلاحاً وإن كان الحكم وجوب مهر المثل. وكذا لو قال أحدهما على أن يكون بضع بنتي صداقاً لبنتك ولم يقبل الآخر بل زوجه بنته ولم يجعلها صداقاً فليس بشغار وإن وجب مهر المثل حتى كان العقد صحيحاً اتفاقاً. وأما حديث الكتب الستة مرفوعاً من النهي عن نكاح الشغار فقد قلنا به لأنه إنما نهى عنه لخلوه عن المهر وقد أوجبنا فيه مهر المثل فلم يبق شغاراً. قيد بالشغار لأنه لو زوج ابنته من رجل على مهر مسمى على أن يزوجه الآخر ابنته على مهر مسمى، فإن زوجه فلكل واحد منهما ما سمى لها من المهر، وإن لم يزوجه الآخر كان للمزوجة تمام مهر مثلها لأن رضاها بدون مهر المثل باعتبار منفعة مشروطة لأبيها. كذا في المبسوط
And mahr al-mithl is obligatory in shighar because he named something that is not valid as a dower, so the contract is valid and mahr al-mithl is obligatory, just as if he gave wine or a pig. Shighar linguistically means emptiness; it is said 'shaghara al-kalb' when the dog lifts one leg to urinate, and 'baldah shaghirah' when it is empty of a ruler. In terminology, it is the marriage of his female ward on condition that the other marries his female ward, so that one of the two contracts is consideration for the other, whether the ward is a daughter, sister, or female slave. It is named for its emptiness of the dower. We only restricted it to cases where one is the dower for the other because if it were not so, such as if he said 'I marry my daughter to you on condition that you marry your daughter to me' without more, and the other accepted, it would not be shighar terminologically, although the ruling is that mahr al-mithl is obligatory. Likewise, if one said 'that the vulva of my daughter be the dower for your daughter' and the other did not accept but married his daughter without making it a dower, it is not shighar, even though mahr al-mithl is obligatory, so the contract is valid by agreement. As for the hadith in the six books forbidding nikah al-shighar, we have acted upon it because it was forbidden due to its emptiness of the dower, and we have made mahr al-mithl obligatory, so it is no longer shighar. He restricted it to shighar because if a man marries his daughter to a man for a named dower on condition that the other marries his daughter for a named dower, and he does so, then each has what was named for his daughter as dower; and if the other does not marry, then the married woman is entitled to the full mahr al-mithl because her consent to less than mahr al-mithl was based on a conditioned benefit for her father. As in al-Mabsut.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on shighar marriage and the obligation of mahr al-mithl. The author defines shighar linguistically (emptiness) and technically: a marriage where one man marries his female ward to another on condition that the other marries his female ward, with one marriage being the consideration for the other, and no dower is specified. The ruling: the marriage contract is valid, but the dower (which is the other marriage) is invalid, so mahr al-mithl (the proper dower for a woman of her status) must be paid. The proof is analogy: just as if a man marries a woman for wine or a pig (which are not valid dower), the contract is valid and mahr al-mithl is obligatory. The author then refines the definition: it is only shighar if one marriage is explicitly made the dower for the other. If no such condition is made, it is not shighar technically, but mahr al-mithl is still obligatory. The hadith prohibiting shighar (from the six books) is addressed: the prohibition was because of the absence of a proper dower; since we require mahr al-mithl, the prohibition is respected. The passage ends with a conditional case: if a man marries his daughter for a named dower on condition that the other marries his daughter for a named dower, and the condition is fulfilled, each daughter gets her named dower; if the condition is not fulfilled, the first daughter gets full mahr al-mithl because her consent to a lower dower was tied to a benefit for her father. This is from al-Mabsut.

Key Terms
شغار (shighar): A marriage where one man marries his female ward to another on condition that the other marries his female ward, with one marriage serving as the dower for the other.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower commensurate with the woman's status (family, beauty, wealth, etc.), paid when no valid dower is specified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, why is mahr al-mithl obligatory in shighar?
A) Because the hadith forbids shighar.
B) Because the dower is invalid (the marriage itself is not a valid dower).
C) Because the bride's consent is missing.
D) Because the father forces the marriage.

Key Takeaway
Shighar marriage is valid in the Hanafi school, but the husband must pay mahr al-mithl because the intended dower (the other marriage) is invalid, reconciling the hadith prohibition with contract validity.

Service of a Free Husband as Dower: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on service as dower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on service as dower and identify the relied-upon ruling.

Core Idea
Service of a free person is not considered property for dower in the Hanafi school; thus mahr al-mithl is wajib.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a free husband's stipulated service as a dower (mahr). While Imam Muhammad considers service as property with a value that must be paid, the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that service is not property (mal) and therefore cannot serve as dower, necessitating mahr al-mithl. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi concept of mal and its role in marriage contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the case
Identify the scenario: a free man marries a woman and stipulates his service for a fixed period (e.g., one year) as her dower.
The service is tangible but involves the husband's labor.
2
Present Muhammad's position and proof
Imam Muhammad argues that the named service is property (mal) because it has value. However, delivery is impossible due to the husband's freedom (cannot be enslaved), so by analogy to marrying on another's slave, the wife is owed the value of the service (qimat al-khidmah).
Muhammad uses qiyas on a case where the specified dower cannot be delivered.
3
Present the Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Sahibayn) argue that service is not considered property (mal) in the legal sense for dower. Therefore, the dower is invalid from the start, and mahr al-mithl is wajib.
Their argument is that mal requires tangibility and ownership; service lacks these.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Muhammad's view, the wife gets the market value of the service; under the Sahibayn's view, she gets mahr al-mithl (which may differ from the value of the service).
Mahr al-mithl is based on the dower of similar women, not the stipulated service.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn: mahr al-mithl is wajib. Service is not a valid dower for free men.
This is the position in the matn and zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخدمة زوج حر للأمهار) أي يجب مهر المثل إذا تزوج حر امرأة وجعل خدمته لها سنة مثلاً صداقها. وقال محمد لها قيمة خدمته سنة لأن المسمى مال إلا أنه عجز عن التسليم لمكان المناقضة فصار كالمتزوج على عبد الغير. ولهما أن الخدمة ليست بمال
And the service of a free husband as dower: That is, mahr al-mithl is obligatory if a free man marries a woman and makes his service for a year, for example, her dower. Muhammad said she is entitled to the value of his service for a year because the named thing is property, but he is unable to deliver due to contradiction (of freedom and slavery), so it becomes like one who marries on the basis of another's slave. And for them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad? Actually 'lahuma' refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf? The text says 'wa lahuma' meaning the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad? But Muhammad is the one who said the first view. This is confusing. In context, 'lahuma' likely refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, while Muhammad differs. The text says: 'Wa lahumā anna al-khidmata laysat bi-mal' meaning service is not property.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of a free husband's service as a dower (mahr). If a free man marries a woman and stipulates that his service for a set period (e.g., one year) is her dower, what is the ruling? According to Imam Muhammad, the named thing (service) is property (mal) because it has value, but the husband is unable to deliver it due to a contradiction: a free man cannot be enslaved for service, as it violates his freedom. This is analogous to marrying on the basis of a slave belonging to someone else (where the slave cannot be delivered because it is not owned by the husband). Therefore, Muhammad says the wife is entitled to the value of the service (qimat khidmatihi), i.e., she gets the market value of such service as mahr, not the service itself. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (lahuma), service is not considered property (mal) at all, so the dower is invalid from the start, and mahr al-mithl is wajib (as stated in the matn). The text is cut off here, but the dispute is clear: Muhammad considers service as property but with delivery issue, so value is due; the Sahibayn consider service not property, so mahr al-mithl. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: service of a free person cannot be a valid dower because it is not property in the legal sense applicable to dower, so mahr al-mithl is obligatory.

Key Terms
خدمة (khidmah): Service of a person, here the husband's service for a specified period.
صداق (sidaq): Synonym for mahr (dower), the payment given by the husband to the wife in marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The dower is valid and the husband must serve her.
B) The dower is invalid and mahr al-mithl is wajib.
C) The wife gets the value of the service as dower.
D) The marriage is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The service of a free husband cannot be a valid dower; the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl.

Ruling on Mut'ah for a Divorced Woman
Clarifies the legal status of istihbab for mut'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mut'ah and explain why it is not a specific ruling of divorce.

Core Idea
Mut'ah is recommended as charity, not as a divorce ruling.

The passage clarifies a common confusion: while giving mut'ah to a divorced woman is rewarded, this recommendation is not a specific ruling of divorce. It is like saying takbir on Eid—not required but good if done. We will unpack the distinction and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central question
What is the legal status of mut'ah? Is it a ruling derived from divorce or a general charitable act?
2
Examine the analogy with takbir on Eid
The author compares mut'ah to saying takbir on the way to the mosque on Eid: it is not a specific ruling of Eid, but if done, it is still recommended. Similarly, mut'ah is not a ruling of divorce but still a good deed.
The analogy is from Abu Hanifa's view on takbir.
3
Note the exception for the at-fault wife
If the separation is from the wife's side before consummation, mut'ah is not even recommended because she is the aggressor (janiyah).
This exception reinforces that mut'ah is tied to kindness, not entitlement.
4
State the Hanafi mufta bihi
The relied-upon position: mut'ah is mustahabb (recommended) as a general act of kindness, but not as a specific ruling (hukm) of divorce. There is consensus on reward, but disagreement on its legal basis.
This resolves the apparent contradiction between different texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكاح باب المهر ۲۷۳ وصاحب المختلف، وعلى ما في بعض نسخ القدوري لا تكون مستحبة لها حكماً للطلاق، ولو كانت مستحبة كان لمعنى آخر كما في قوله في عيد الفطر ولا يكبر في طريق المصلي عند أبي حنيفة أي حكماً للعيد ولكن لو كبر لأنه ذكر الله تعالى يجوز ويستحب. كذا في غاية البيان . وحاصله أنه ليس المراد من نفي المستحب هنا أن لا ثواب في فعله بل فيه ثواب اتفاقاً لأنه إحسان وبرّ لها، وإنما محل الاختلاف أن هذا المستحب حكم من أحكام الطلاق أولاً، وقد قدمنا أن الفرقة إذا كانت من قبلها قبل الدخول فإنه لا يستحب لها المتعة أيضاً لأنها جانية . . سمی
Book of Nikah, Chapter of Mahr. 273. And the author of al-Mukhtalif, and according to what is in some copies of al-Quduri, it is not mustahabb for her as a ruling of divorce. And if it were mustahabb, it would be for another meaning, as in his statement on Eid al-Fitr: 'And he does not say takbir on the way to the mosque according to Abu Hanifa' i.e., as a ruling of Eid, but if he says takbir because it is dhikr of Allah, it is permissible and mustahabb. So in Ghayat al-Bayan. The summary is that the negation of mustahabb here does not mean that there is no reward in doing it; rather, there is reward by consensus because it is ihsan and kindness to her. The only area of disagreement is whether this mustahabb is a ruling of divorce or not. And we have already stated that if the separation is from her side before consummation, then mut'ah is not recommended for her either because she is the aggressor. . . summiya

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling clarification regarding mut'ah (consolation gift) for a divorced woman. The author explains that the disagreement among scholars is not about the reward of giving mut'ah—which is unanimously agreed to be meritorious as an act of kindness—but about whether this recommendation (istihbab) is a specific ruling derived from the divorce laws or a general charitable act. The text draws an analogy to the takbir on Eid: it is not a specific ruling of Eid to say takbir on the way, but if one does it, it is still good. Similarly, mut'ah is not a specific ruling of divorce (i.e., not wajib nor a sunnah of divorce), but giving it is still rewarded. The author then notes that if the woman was the cause of the separation before consummation (e.g., she sought divorce), then mut'ah is not even recommended for her because she is at fault (janiyah). The word 'summiya' at the end may be a marginal note indicating the end of a section.

Key Terms
المتعة (al-mut'ah): A consolatory gift given to a divorced woman, not mandatory but recommended.
المستحب (al-mustahabb): An act that is recommended but not obligatory; its omission is not sinful but doing it brings reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is prohibited.

Key Takeaway
Mut'ah is a recommended act of kindness, not a legal obligation of divorce.

Ruling on Shighar Marriage: Validity with Mahr al-Mithl
Ruling with proof: validity of shighar and obligation of mahr al-mithl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shighar marriage, identify the dalil from hadith and qiyas, and apply the rule that an invalid dower triggers mahr al-mithl.

Core Idea
Shighar marriage is valid but requires mahr al-mithl because the exchange of women is invalid as dower.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the Hanafi position on shighar — a marriage where two men exchange their female wards without a named mahr. The ruling balances contractual validity with the woman's right to fair dower, using qiyas and hadith. We will walk through the reasoning, the technical definition, and how the Hanafi school addresses the prohibition hadith.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the core hukm: mahr al-mithl is wajib in shighar. Note that the contract itself is valid.
The author begins directly with the ruling, then provides the proof.
2
Examine the qiyas analogy
The author analogizes shighar to naming wine or pig as dower: both involve an invalid dower, yet the contract remains valid with mahr al-mithl. Identify the illa: naming something that is not valid property (mal mutaqawwim) as dower.
This is a clear case of qiyas jaliy.
3
Define shighar technically
Distinguish the technical definition from the linguistic meaning. Understand that the condition 'one being the dower for the other' is essential; without it, the case falls outside shighar but still requires mahr al-mithl.
The author provides a precise technical definition to avoid confusion.
4
Address the hadith prohibition
The hadith prohibiting shighar is from the six books. The Hanafi response is that the prohibition is due to the absence of mahr. Since the school obligates mahr al-mithl, the prohibition is no longer applicable.
This shows how Hanafi usul reconciles a general prohibition with a specific ruling.
5
Understand the conditional case
The passage ends with a scenario where a conditional named mahr is agreed. If the condition is fulfilled, each gets the named mahr; if not, the woman receives full mahr al-mithl because her consent was based on her father's benefit.
This reinforces that the woman's right to fair dower cannot be waived by a conditional agreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ويجب مهر المثل في الشغار) لأنه سمى ما لا يصح صداقاً فيصح العقد ويجب مهر المثل كما إذا سمى خمراً أو خنزيراً. والشغار في اللغة الخلوة يقال شعر الكلب إذا رفع إحدى رجليه ليبول، وبلدة شاغرة إذا كانت خالية من السلطان وأما في الاصطلاح فتزويجه موليته على أن يزوجه الآخر موليته ليكون أحد العقدين عوضاً عن الآخر، سواء كانت المولية بنتاً أو أختاً أو أمة، سمي به لخلوه عن المهر. وإنما قيدنا بأن يكون أحدهما صداقاً عن الآخر لأنه لو لم يكن كذلك بأن قال زوجتك بنتي على أن تزوجني بنتك ولم يزد عليه فقبل الآخر فإنه لا يكون شغاراً اصطلاحاً وإن كان الحكم وجوب مهر المثل. وكذا لو قال أحدهما على أن يكون بضع بنتي صداقاً لبنتك ولم يقبل الآخر بل زوجه بنته ولم يجعلها صداقاً فليس بشغار وإن وجب مهر المثل حتى كان العقد صحيحاً اتفاقاً. وأما حديث الكتب الستة مرفوعاً من النهي عن نكاح الشغار فقد قلنا به لأنه إنما نهى عنه لخلوه عن المهر وقد أوجبنا فيه مهر المثل فلم يبق شغاراً. قيد بالشغار لأنه لو زوج ابنته من رجل على مهر مسمى على أن يزوجه الآخر ابنته على مهر مسمى، فإن زوجه فلكل واحد منهما ما سمى لها من المهر، وإن لم يزوجه الآخر كان للمزوجة تمام مهر مثلها لأن رضاها بدون مهر المثل باعتبار منفعة مشروطة لأبيها. كذا في المبسوط
He said: 'And mahr al-mithl is obligatory in shighar' because he named something that is not valid as dower, so the contract is valid and mahr al-mithl is obligatory, just as if he named wine or pig. Shighar in language means emptiness; it is said 'shaghara al-kalb' when the dog lifts one leg to urinate, and 'balda shaghira' meaning devoid of ruler. In technical terms, it is a man marrying his female ward to another on condition that the other marries his female ward, so that one of the two contracts is consideration for the other, whether the ward is a daughter, sister, or slave girl. It is called shighar because of its emptiness from mahr. We only restricted it to one being the dower for the other because if it is not like that, e.g., he says 'I marry my daughter to you on condition that you marry your daughter to me' without more, and the other accepts, then it is not technically shighar although the ruling is obligation of mahr al-mithl. Similarly, if one says 'my daughter's sexual organ is the dower for your daughter' and the other does not accept but marries his daughter without making it a dower, it is not shighar although mahr al-mithl is obligatory, and the contract is valid by consensus. As for the hadith in the six books prohibiting nikah al-shighar, we accept it because the prohibition is due to its emptiness from mahr, and we have obligated mahr al-mithl in it, so it is no longer shighar. It is restricted to shighar because if he marries his daughter to a man for a named mahr on condition that the other marries his daughter for a named mahr, then if he marries her, each has the named mahr, and if the other does not marry her, the woman gets her full mahr al-mithl because her consent to less than mahr al-mithl was due to a benefit conditioned for her father. So in al-Mabsut.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning shighar marriage. The author first states the ruling: mahr al-mithl is obligatory in a shighar marriage. The reason given is that the dower named in such a marriage (the sexual right of the other woman) is invalid, similar to naming wine or pig as dower, which also obligates mahr al-mithl while the contract remains valid. The text then provides a detailed definition of shighar, distinguishing it from similar arrangements. It emphasizes that the condition 'one being the dower for the other' is essential for it to be technically shighar; without it, the contract is still valid but mahr al-mithl is still due. The author then addresses the famous hadith prohibiting shighar from the six authentic books. The Hanafi response is that the prohibition was due to the absence of mahr; since Hanafis obligate mahr al-mithl, the prohibition is not violated. Finally, the passage discusses a case where conditional dowers are named, explaining that the woman is entitled to her named mahr if the condition is fulfilled, or else the full mahr al-mithl.

Key Terms
الشغار (al-shighar): A marriage where each party marries his female ward to the other on condition that the one contract is the dower for the other, resulting in no actual mahr.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The fair dower equivalent to what women of similar status receive, used when the named dower is invalid or absent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on a shighar marriage where the two women are exchanged without any named mahr?
A) The marriage is batil (invalid).
B) The marriage is valid and each woman's mahr is her own sexual right.
C) The marriage is valid and mahr al-mithl is obligatory for each.
D) The marriage is valid but requires a corrective contract.

Key Takeaway
In shighar, the contract is valid and mahr al-mithl is wajib, resolving the prohibition by compensating the missing dower.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Is a Free Husband's Service Valid as Dower?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the validity of a free husband's personal service as mahr and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
A free husband's personal service cannot be dower; the named mahr is invalid and mahr al-mithl is wajib (Sahibayn view is mufta bihi).

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) regarding whether a free man's personal service can be validly named as dower (mahr). The ruling determines whether the wife receives the value of the service or mahr al-mithl. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi definition of property (mal) and its application in marriage contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Identify the two positions: Imam Muhammad holds that the service is property and the wife gets its value; the Sahibayn hold that service is not property and mahr al-mithl is mandatory.
2
Identify the point of disagreement
The disagreement is over whether a free person's personal service qualifies as mal (property) that can be named as dower.
3
Follow the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that service is not mal because it inverts the marital relationship; the wife cannot be entitled to her husband's service by contract. This is analogous to naming wine or pig as dower.
The key phrase: 'في قلب الموضوع' (inversion of the subject).
4
Analyze Muhammad's analogy
Muhammad draws an analogy to marrying on the condition of a slave belonging to another; there, the slave's service is property and the wife gets its value. He argues that the husband's service should be treated similarly.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn: mahr al-mithl is wajib. This is supported by the majority of later Hanafi scholars, including the author of al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وخدمة زوج حر للأمهار) أي يجب مهر المثل إذا تزوج حر امرأة وجعل خدمته لها سنة مثلاً صداقها. وقال محمد لها قيمة خدمته سنة لأن المسمى مال إلا أنه عجز عن التسليم لمكان المناقضة فصار كالمتزوج على عبد الغير. ولهما أن الخدمة ليست بمال لما فيه من قلب الموضوع إذا لا تستحق فيه بحال فصار كتسمية الخمر والخنزير. وهذا لأن تقومه بالعقد للضرورة فإذا لم يجب تسليمه بالعقد لم يظهر تقومه فيبقى الحكم على الأصل وهو مهر المثل. أطلق في الخدمة فشمل رعي غنمها وزراعة أرضها وهي رواية الأصل كما في الخانية، وذكر في المبسوط فيه روايتين، وذكر في المعراج أن الأصح رواية الأصل وهو وجوب مهر المثل لكن يشكل عليه أنهم لم يجعلوا رعي الغنم والزراعة خدمة في مسألة استئجار الابن أباه فقالوا لو استأجر أباه للخدمة لا يجوز، ولو استأجره للرعي والزراعة يصح فمقتضاه ترجيح الصحة في جلعه صداقاً وكون الأوجه الصحة لقص الله تعالى قصة شعيب وموسى من غير بيان نفيه في شرعنا إنما يلزم لو كانت الغنم ملك البنت دون شعيب وهو منتف . وقيد بخدمة الزوج لأنه لو تزوجها على خدمة حر آخر فالصحيح صحته وترجع على الزوج بقيمة خدمته كما في المحيط. وهذا يشير إلى أنه لا يخدمها، فإما لأنه أجنبي فلا يؤمن الانكشاف عليها مع مخالطته للخدمة، وإما أن يكون مراده إذا كان بغير أمر ذلك الحر ولم يجزه، وظاهر ما في الهداية أنه إذا وقع برضاه يجب عليه تسليم خدمته كما لو تزوج على عبد الغير برضا مولاه حيث يجب على المولى تسليمه. وقيد بالحر لما سيأتي صريحاً، وقيد بالخدمة لأنه لو تزوجها على منافع سائر الأعيان من سكنى داره وخدمة عبده وركوب دابته والحمل عليها وزراعة أرضه ونحو ذلك من منافع الأعيان مدة معلومة صحت التسمية لأن هذه المنافع أموال أو ألحقت بالأموال شرعاً في سائر العقود لمكان الحاجة والحاجة في النكاح متحققة، وإمكان الدفع بالتسليم ثابت بتسليم محالها إذ ليس فيه استخدام المرأة زوجها فجعلت أموالاً، وألحقت بالأعيان فصحت تسميتها. كذا في البدائع. والمراد بزراعة أرضه أن تزرع أرضه ببذرها وليس له شيء من الخارج، وأما إذا شرط له شيء من الخارج فإن التسمية تفسد قال في المجمع من كتاب المزارعة : لو تزوج على أن تزرع هي أرضه بالنصف ببذرها صح وفسدت فيجعل مهرها نصف أجر مثل الأرض، وربعه إن طلقها لأنها من المنافع وهي أعراض تتلاشى فلا تتقوم وتقومها في العقد على خلاف القياس بخلاف خدمة العبد فإنها ابتغاء بالمال لتضمن العقد تسليم رقبته قوله إذ لا تستحق فيه بحال) جعله في الهداية دليلاً مستقلاً وعلله بقوله لما فيه من قلب الموضوع فكان ينبغي للمؤلف اتباعه كما لا يخفى قوله (فقالوا لو استأجر أباه الخ قال في النهر : وهذا شاهد أقوى من هنا قال المصنف في كافيه بعد ذكر رواية الأصل؛ الصواب أن يسلم لها إجماعاً قوله (وكون الأوجه (الصحة) جواب سؤال مقدر وتقريره ظاهر. قوله (فكذا نقول الخ) أقره في النهر وقال والظاهر أنه يلزم تعليم كله إلا إذا قامت قرينة على إرادة البعض والحفظ ليس من مفهومه كما لا يخفى. اهـ. قال في الشرنبلالية قلت: لكنه يعارضه أنه
He said: 'And the service of a free husband for dowers' i.e., mahr al-mithl is obligatory if a free man marries a woman and makes his service for her for one year, for example, as her dower. And Muhammad said: She is entitled to the value of his service for one year because the named item is property, but he is unable to deliver due to contradiction, so it becomes like marrying for the slave of another. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): Service is not property because of the inversion of the subject, as she is not entitled to it in any case, so it becomes like naming wine and pig. This is because valuation by contract is for necessity; when delivery is not obligatory by contract, its valuation does not appear, so the ruling remains on the original, which is mahr al-mithl. He made it absolute in service, so it includes herding her goats and farming her land, and this is the narration of the original as in al-Khaniya. And in al-Mabsut, there are two narrations. And in al-Mi'raj, the most correct is the narration of the original, which is obligation of mahr al-mithl, but it is problematic because they did not consider herding goats and farming as service in the issue of a son hiring his father. They said: If he hires his father for service, it is not valid; if he hires him for herding and farming, it is valid. So its implication is to give preponderance to validity in making it dower. And that the most likely is validity because Allah related the story of Shu'ayb and Musa without stating its negation in our Law; this would only follow if the goats were the property of the daughter and not of Shu'ayb, which is not the case. And it is restricted by the service of the husband because if he marries her on the service of another free man, then the correct view is its validity, and she returns to the husband for the value of his service as in al-Muhit. This indicates that he does not serve her; either because he is a stranger and there is fear of exposure with his mixing for service, or because his intention is if it is without the command of that free man and he does not authorize it. And the apparent in al-Hidaya is that if it occurs with his consent, he must deliver his service, just as if he married on the slave of another with the master's consent, where the master must deliver him. And it is restricted by the husband being free, as will come explicitly. And it is restricted by service because if he marries her on the usufruct of other items, such as dwelling in his house, service of his slave, riding his mount, carrying on it, farming his land, and the like of usufructs of things for a known period, the naming is valid because these usufructs are wealth or are treated as wealth legally in all contracts due to need, and the need is realized in marriage, and the possibility of delivery is established by delivery of their places since there is no usage of the woman for her husband, so they are made wealth and attached to things, so their naming is valid. So in al-Bada'i. And the meaning of farming his land is that she farms his land with her seed and he has nothing of the produce. And if he stipulates something of the produce for him, then the naming is invalid. It said in al-Majma' from the book of muzara'ah: If he marries on condition that she farms his land for half with her seed, it is valid and invalid, so her mahr is half of the rental value of the land, and a quarter if he divorces her because it is of usufructs, which are accidental entities, so they are not valued, and their valuation in the contract is contrary to analogy, unlike the service of a slave because it is sought for wealth as the contract includes delivery of his person. (He said: 'since she is not entitled to it in any case') He (al-Hidaya) made it an independent proof and reasoned it with 'because of the inversion of the subject'. So the author should have followed him, as is clear. (He said: 'They said: if he hires his father...') He said in al-Nahr: This is a stronger evidence than here. The author said in his Kafi after mentioning the narration of the original: The correct is that it is delivered to her by consensus. (He said: 'and that the most likely is validity') It is an answer to an implied question, and its clarification is apparent. (He said: 'So we say...') He (al-Nahr) approved it and said: The apparent is that he must teach all of it unless there is an indication of intending some, and memorization is not part of its meaning, as is clear. End. He said in al-Sharnabaliyya: I say: But it is opposed by that...
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a free man's service as dower (mahr). The ruling stated first: mahr al-mithl is obligatory when a free man marries a woman and names his personal service (e.g., working for a year) as her dower. Imam Muhammad holds that the woman is entitled to the value of his service because the named item is property, but the husband cannot deliver it due to contradiction (he cannot be both husband and servant), analogous to marrying on a slave belonging to someone else without permission. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Sahibayn) argue that service is not considered property (mal) because it would invert the marital relationship—the wife would be entitled to her husband's service, which is not legally recognized. Thus, the named dower is invalid, and mahr al-mithl is due. The text then extends to various forms of service (herding, farming) and discusses different narrations, including a problem: if hiring one's father for service is invalid but for herding/farming is valid, then why not consider the latter valid as dower? Some argue the story of Musa and Shu'ayb supports validity. The passage also distinguishes between the husband's own service (invalid) and the service of his slave or other usufructs (valid) because the latter are considered property. The discussion ends with further refinements about consent, teaching obligations, and a quote from al-Sharnabaliyya that the matter is contested.

Key Terms
الخدمة (al-khidma): Personal service, especially of a husband, considered as a potential dower.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): Fair dower based on the woman's status, used when the named dower is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), what is the ruling when a free man marries a woman and names his personal service as her dower?
A) The marriage is invalid (batil).
B) The dower is valid and he must serve her.
C) The dower is invalid and mahr al-mithl must be paid.
D) She is entitled to the value of his service.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a free husband's personal service is not valid as dower; the named mahr is void and mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory.

Ruling on Dower Being Service of a Free Husband
Ruling on dower being service of free husband with proof and ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dower specified as service of a free husband and explain why it is invalid, applying the principle that dower must be wealth (mal).

Core Idea
Service of a free husband is not wealth; it cannot be a valid dower, and mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory.

In this lesson, we examine a practical issue in marriage contracts: what if the dower is specified as the husband's service rather than a tangible asset? The Hanafi school holds that service is not considered wealth (mal), so the specified dower is invalid. However, the marriage remains valid, and the wife is entitled to the proper dower (mahr al-mithl). We will explore the reasoning behind this ruling, including the analogy to prohibited items like wine and pork, and address a potential objection from the story of Prophet Shu'ayb (peace be upon him).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is being ruled upon? It is the specification of dower as 'service of a free husband'. The ruling: such specification is invalid (fasid), and the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl.
Note that the marriage contract itself remains valid; only the dower is invalid.
2
Understand why service is not mal
Service cannot be owned or delivered as a right; it inverts the marital roles (the husband should not serve the wife). Therefore, it does not qualify as wealth (mal) in Islamic law.
Wealth must be tangible, owned, and deliverable.
3
Note the analogy to wine and pork
Just as wine and pork are invalid as dower because they are not permissible wealth, service is also invalid. This is a clear qiyas (analogical reasoning).
The Hanafi school uses this analogy to reinforce the principle.
4
Recognize the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi riwayat (e.g., in al-Mabsut) consider herding and farming as valid dower. However, the original riwayah (zahir al-riwayah) considers them invalid, and this is the mufta bihi.
The ikhtilaf centers on whether herding/farming are considered 'service' or separate activities with value.
5
Evaluate the objection from Shu'ayb's story
Opponents cite the Quranic story of Shu'ayb and Musa (peace be upon them) as proof that service can be dower. The Hanafi response: the sheep belonged to Shu'ayb (the father), not the bride, so the service was payment to the father, not dower for the daughter.
Thus the analogy is rejected, and the original ruling stands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب مهر المثل في الشغار وخدمة زوج حر ليست بمال لما فيه من قلب الموضوع إذا لا تستحق فيه بحال فصار كتسمية الخمر والخنزير. وهذا لأن تقومه بالعقد للضرورة فإذا لم يجب تسليمه بالعقد لم يظهر تقومه فيبقى الحكم على الأصل وهو مهر المثل. أطلق في الخدمة فشمل رعي غنمها وزراعة أرضها وهي رواية الأصل كما في الخانية، وذكر في المبسوط فيه روايتين، وذكر في المعراج أن الأصح رواية الأصل وهو وجوب مهر المثل لكن يشكل عليه أنهم لم يجعلوا رعي الغنم والزراعة خدمة في مسألة استئجار الابن أباه فقالوا لو استأجر أباه للخدمة لا يجوز، ولو استأجره للرعي والزراعة يصح فمقتضاه ترجيح الصحة في جعله صداقاً وكون الأوجه الصحة لقص الله تعالى قصة شعيب وموسى من غير بيان نفيه في شرعنا إنما يلزم لو كانت الغنم ملك البنت دون شعيب وهو منتف.
And mahr al-mithl is obligatory in shighar (exchange marriage) and in the service of a free husband. Service is not wealth because it involves inverting the subject matter, since it is never entitled to be owned, so it becomes like naming wine and pork as dower. This is because its valuation by the contract is for necessity; when its delivery is not required by the contract, its valuation does not appear, so the ruling remains on the original principle, which is mahr al-mithl. It was left general in 'service', so it includes herding her sheep and farming her land, and this is the riwayah of the original (zahir al-riwayah) as in al-Khaniyyah. In al-Mabsut, two riwayat are mentioned. In al-Mi'raj, it is mentioned that the most correct is the riwayah of the original, which is the obligation of mahr al-mithl. However, it is problematic because they did not consider herding sheep and farming as service in the issue of a son hiring his father. They said: if he hires his father for service, it is not valid; if he hires him for herding and farming, it is valid. This implies preferring validity in making it a dower, and that the strongest view is validity, because Allah Most High related the story of Shu'ayb and Moses without stating its nullification in our Shari'ah. But this objection only applies if the sheep were the daughter's property, which is not the case, so the objection is refuted.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof discussing the invalidity of dower when specified as 'service of a free husband'. The author explains that service is not considered wealth (mal) because it cannot be owned or delivered as a right; it reverses the purpose of marriage (the husband should not be serving the wife). Therefore, naming such service as dower is like naming wine or pork, which are not valid considerations. Consequently, the specified dower is invalid and the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) becomes obligatory. The text then clarifies that the term 'service' is general enough to include herding the wife's sheep and farming her land, according to the authoritative riwayah (zahir al-riwayah). There is a reported ikhtilaf: some scholars consider such activities as valid dower, citing the story of Prophet Shu'ayb and Moses (peace be upon them), where Moses worked for Shu'ayb in exchange for marriage. However, the author resolves this by noting that in that story, the sheep belonged to Shu'ayb, not the daughter, so the analogy does not apply. Thus, the relied-upon position remains that such service as dower is invalid and mahr al-mithl is wajib.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower: the amount a woman of similar status would receive, determined by her family's social standing, etc.
خدمة (khidmah): Personal service, such as herding, farming, or any labor performed for the wife.
شغار (shighar): Exchange marriage: two men marry each other's daughters/sisters without dower. It is invalid and mahr al-mithl is wajib.
تسمية (tasmiyah): The specified dower mentioned in the marriage contract.
رواية الأصل (riwayat al-asl): The transmission from the six core books of Imam Muhammad (Zahir al-Riwayah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling if a man marries a woman on the condition that he will herd her sheep as her dower?
A) The dower is valid and she receives nothing else.
B) The dower is invalid and she receives mahr al-mithl.
C) The dower is valid only if the sheep belong to her father.
D) The marriage itself is invalid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, dower must be wealth (mal); service is not mal, so specifying service as dower is invalid and mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory.

Dower of Service of Another Free Man and Usufruct of Objects
Expansion probe on valid forms of non-monetary dower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dower consisting of service of another free man or usufruct of objects, and explain the reasoning based on the distinction from the husband's own service.

Core Idea
Service of another free man and usufruct of objects are valid dower because they avoid the prohibition of using the husband as a servant.

This passage clarifies two key exceptions to the rule that dower cannot be service. The first exception is when the service is that of another free man, not the husband. The second is when the dower consists of the usufruct of objects like houses or animals. Understanding these exceptions helps you apply the correct ruling in marriage contracts involving non-monetary dower.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base prohibition
Recognize that a dower consisting of the husband's own service is invalid. This is the general rule the passage builds upon.
The restriction is on the husband's service because it implies using the husband like a servant, which is contrary to marriage.
2
Examine the first exception: service of another free man
Read the passage's ruling that if the dower is the service of a third free man, it is valid. Note the two scenarios: (1) without the free man's consent – the husband pays its value; (2) with his consent – the husband must deliver the actual service.
The text cites al-Muhit and al-Hidayah on this point.
3
Examine the second exception: usufruct of objects
Understand that usufructs like dwelling, riding, and farming are valid dower because they are considered wealth (mal) by the Shari'ah or treated as such due to need, and they do not involve the wife using the husband.
The passage mentions that delivery is possible by delivering the objects themselves, and need in marriage is established.
4
Identify the underlying reasoning (ta'lil)
Note the rationale: service of another free man is analogous to hiring (ijarah), while usufruct of objects is akin to wealth. Both avoid the prohibition of making the husband serve his wife.
The reasoning is based on istihsan and the fulfillment of need.
5
Apply to real cases
Use this teaching to evaluate marriage contracts where the dower is non-monetary. Determine if the item qualifies as manfa'ah of an 'ayn or service of a third party.
Always ensure the period is known and the object is deliverable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيد بخدمة الزوج لأنه لو تزوجها على خدمة حر آخر فالصحيح صحته وترجع على الزوج بقيمة خدمته كما في المحيط. وهذا يشير إلى أنه لا يخدمها، فإما لأنه أجنبي فلا يؤمن الانكشاف عليها مع مخالطته للخدمة، وإما أن يكون مراده إذا كان بغير أمر ذلك الحر ولم يجزه، وظاهر ما في الهداية أنه إذا وقع برضاه يجب عليه تسليم خدمته كما لو تزوج على عبد الغير برضا مولاه حيث يجب على المولى تسليمه. وقيد بالحر لما سيأتي صريحاً، وقيد بالخدمة لأنه لو تزوجها على منافع سائر الأعيان من سكنى داره وخدمة عبده وركوب دابته والحمل عليها وزراعة أرضه ونحو ذلك من منافع الأعيان مدة معلومة صحت التسمية لأن هذه المنافع أموال أو ألحقت بالأموال شرعاً في سائر العقود لمكان الحاجة والحاجة في النكاح متحققة، وإمكان الدفع بالتسليم ثابت بتسليم محالها إذ ليس فيه استخدام المرأة زوجها فجعلت أموالاً، وألحقت بالأعيان فصحت تسميتها. كذا في البدائع.
And it was restricted to the husband's service because if he marries her on the condition of the service of another free man, the correct view is that it is valid, and she takes from the husband the value of his service, as in al-Muhit. This indicates that the other man does not serve her, either because he is an unrelated man (ajnabi) so there is no safety from exposure (fitnah) due to his mixing in service, or because the author meant when it is without the consent of that free man and he did not authorize it. The apparent meaning in al-Hidayah is that if it occurs with his consent, the husband must deliver his service, just as if he marries on the condition of the slave of another with the master's consent, where the master must deliver the slave. And it was restricted to the free man because it will come explicitly later. And it was restricted to service because if he marries her on the condition of the usufruct of other objects, such as dwelling in his house, service of his slave, riding his animal, carrying loads on it, farming his land, and similar usufructs of objects for a known period, then the naming (tasmiyah) is valid because these usufructs are wealth or are treated as wealth in Shari'ah in all contracts due to need, and the need in marriage is established, and the possibility of delivering them is established by delivering their loci, since it does not involve the wife using her husband, so they are considered wealth and attached to objects, thus their naming is valid. Thus in al-Bada'i.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage clarifies two restrictions in the earlier ruling. First, the invalidity of dower being service applies only to the husband's own service, not to the service of another free man. If a man marries a woman on condition that some other free man serve her, the correct view is that such a dower is valid, but the wife will claim the value of that service from her husband. The husband does not force the free man to serve; rather, he owes its value as if he had hired him. However, if the free man consents, the husband must deliver his actual service, analogous to a borrowed slave with the master's consent. Second, dower specified as usufruct (manafi') of objects like houses, slaves, animals, or land is valid because these are considered wealth (amwal) in Shari'ah, especially since they can be delivered without causing the wife to use her husband, thus avoiding the original problem.

Key Terms
منافع الأعيان (manafi' al-a'yan): Usufruct of physical objects: use of a house, slave's service, riding an animal, farming land, etc.
حر آخر (hurr akhar): Another free man (not the husband).
تسمية (tasmiyah): The naming or specification of the dower in the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The dower is invalid because service of a free man is not wealth.
B) The dower is valid, and the friend must serve.
C) The dower is valid, and the husband must pay the value of the friend's service.
D) The dower is valid only if the friend consents to serve.

Key Takeaway
Dower can be validly given as the service of another free man (with the husband liable for its value) or as the usufruct of objects for a known period, because these are treated as wealth or hire and do not degrade the husband.

Teaching Quran as Dower: From Invalid to Valid
Examination of whether teaching Quran can be a valid dower, with the current fatwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the original Hanafi ruling on dower consisting of teaching the Quran and explain how the mufta bihi shifted to validity due to permissibility of hiring.

Core Idea
Teaching the Quran, once rejected as dower, is now valid because it is a valued usufruct.

In this passage, the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq examines a critical development in Hanafi fiqh: the ruling on dower (mahr) specified as teaching the Quran. The original position held that teaching is not wealth and cannot be dower, but the contemporary fatwa has validated it. We will trace the proofs and the reasoning behind this shift.

Guided Path
1
State the original Hanafi position on dower as teaching Quran
The original ruling is that teaching Quran is not wealth (mal) and cannot be a valid dower; instead, mahr al-mithl (the equivalent dower) becomes wajib.
2
Identify the proofs cited against validity
The author uses the Quranic verse 'half of what you prescribed' (2:237) to argue that the dower must be divisible, and the hadith 'I marry her to you for what you have of the Quran' is interpreted as not indicating exchange.
The hadith's preposition baa' is ambiguous.
3
Understand why the fatwa changed
The permissibility of hiring for teaching Quran (in Ijarah) means that teaching is now considered a usufruct (manfa'ah) with value, making it eligible as dower.
4
Note the current mufta bihi
The mufta bihi position is that teaching Quran as dower is valid (sahih).
The author states he has not seen any opposition to this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وتعليم القرآن) أي يجب مهر المثل إذا جعل الصداق تعليم القرآن لأن المشروع إنما هو الابتغاء بالمال والتعليم ليس بمال وكذا المنافع على أصلنا، ولأن التعليم عبادة فلا يصلح أن يكون صداقاً، ولأن قوله تعالى فنصف ما فرضتم [البقرة: ٢٣٧] يدل على أنه لا بد أن يكون المفروض مما له نصف حتى يمكنه أن يرجع عليها بنصفه إذا طلقها قبل الدخول بعد القبض ولا يمكن ذلك في التعليم، وأما قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «زوجتكها بما معك من القرآن فليست الباء متعينة للعوض الجواز أن تكون للسببية أو للتعليل أي لأجل أنك أهل القرآن أو المراد ببركة ما معك منه فلا يصلح دليلاً، وسيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى في كتاب الإجارات أن الفتوى اليوم على جواز الاستئجار لتعليم القرآن والفقه فينبغي أن يصح مهراً لأن ما جاز أخذ الأجر في مقابلته من المنافع جاز تسميته صداقاً كما قدمناه نقله عن البدائع، ولهذا ذكر في فتح القدير هنا أنه لما جوز الشافعي أخذ الأجر على تعليم القرآن تسميته صداقاً، فكذا نقول : يلزم على المفتى به صحة تسميته صداقاً ولم أر أحداً له والله الموفق للصواب.
His saying: (and teaching the Quran) that is, mahr al-mithl is obligatory if the dower is made teaching the Quran, because the prescribed (in marriage) is seeking wealth, and teaching is not wealth, and likewise usufructs according to our principle, and because teaching is an act of worship so it cannot be a dower, and because the saying of Allah Most High 'then half of what you prescribed' (Quran 2:237) indicates that the prescribed must be something that has a half so that he can take half from her if he divorces her before consummation after taking possession, and that is not possible in teaching. As for his saying (peace be upon him) 'I marry her to you for what you have of the Quran', the preposition baa' is not necessarily for exchange; it could be for causation or explanation, meaning because you are a person of the Quran, or meaning for the blessing of what you have of it, so it is not a proof. And it will come, Allah willing, in the Book of Ijarah that the fatwa today is on the permissibility of hiring for teaching Quran and fiqh, so it should be valid as a dower, because whatever is permissible to take a wage in exchange for, from the usufructs, it is permissible to name it as a dower, as we have transmitted from al-Bada'i. Thus it is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir that since Imam al-Shafi'i permitted taking a wage for teaching Quran, the naming of it as a dower is valid. So we say: it is necessary, according to the mufta bihi, the validity of naming it as a dower, and I have not seen anyone oppose it. And Allah is the Guide.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement regarding the ruling on dower specified as teaching Quran. The author first reiterates the original position: teaching Quran is not wealth ('ayn) and is an act of worship, so it cannot be a valid dower, and mahr al-mithl becomes wajib. The Quranic verse 'half of what you prescribed' is used as proof that the dower must be something divisible, which teaching is not. The hadith 'I marry her to you for what you have of the Quran' is interpreted as not indicating an exchange. However, the author then presents the contemporary fatwa: since it is now permissible to hire someone to teach Quran (as will be discussed in Ijarah), and since that permission makes teaching a usufruct (manfa'ah) that can be valued, it becomes valid as a dower. He cites Fath al-Qadir and al-Bada'i, noting that Imam al-Shafi'i's permissibility of taking wages for Quran teaching supports this. The author concludes that the mufta bihi position is that teaching Quran is valid as a dower, and he has not seen anyone oppose this. This shows a development in Hanafi fatwa from the original theory to a more practical ruling.

Key Terms
تعليم القرآن (ta'lim al-Quran): Teaching the Quran, considered an act of worship originally not wealth, but now treated as a usufruct.
الابتغاء بالمال (al-ibtigha' bil-mal): Seeking wealth; the principle that marriage consideration should be wealth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position regarding dower being teaching the Quran, according to the text?
A) It is definitely invalid and mahr al-mithl is wajib.
B) It is valid because teaching is now considered a usufruct that can be hired.
C) It is valid only if the man teaches the wife himself.
D) The marriage is invalid if he names teaching Quran as dower.

Key Takeaway
Teaching Quran as dower is valid according to the mufta bihi because hiring for teaching is permissible, making it a compensable usufruct.
