Dower of a Slave-Girl with Attached Conditions
Ruling on conditional slave-girl dower with value comparison.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a dower includes a slave-girl with conditions (service or unborn child) and determine whether the wife receives the slave-girl or mahr al-mithl.

Core Idea
A dower can be a slave-girl, but if her value exceeds mahr al-mithl, the wife only gets mahr al-mithl unless the husband voluntarily gives her.

This lesson examines the validity of a dower that consists of a slave-girl (jariyah) with additional conditions—such as the husband's right to her services or ownership of her unborn child. The ruling hinges on comparing the slave-girl's value to the wife's mahr al-mithl. Understanding this nuance prevents misapplication in modern marital contracts involving conditional gifts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dower and its conditions
The dower is a slave-girl with a condition that her service or her unborn child belongs to the husband. Recognize that these conditions are attached to the dower itself.
The condition does not make the dower void; it affects what the wife ultimately receives.
2
Determine mahr al-mithl
Find the standard dower for a woman of her status, considering her family, beauty, and social standing.
Mahr al-mithl is the benchmark for fairness.
3
Compare the slave-girl's value to mahr al-mithl
If mahr al-mithl is equal to or greater than the slave-girl's value, the wife receives the slave-girl along with the attached benefits. If mahr al-mithl is less, she receives only mahr al-mithl.
The condition does not change the comparison; it is part of the dower's value.
4
Consider voluntary surrender
Even if mahr al-mithl is less, the husband may choose to give the slave-girl to the wife voluntarily, making the dower effective.
This is his right, not an obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخانية : ولو تزوج امرأة على جارية على أن له خدمتها ما عاش أو ما في بطنها له كانت الجارية وخدمتها وما في بطنها للمرأة إن كان مهر مثلها مثل قيمة الخادم أو أكثر، وإن كان مهر مثلها أقل من قيمة الخادم كان لها مهر المثل إلا أن يسلم الزوج الخادم إليها باختياره . وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو أعتق أمة وجعل عتقها صداقها فإن التسمية لا تصح لأن العتق ليس بمال، فإن تزوجته فلها مهر المثل، وإن أبت لا تجبر وعليها قيمتها للمولى، وكذا أم الولد لكن لا قيمة عليها له عند آبائها ولو قالت لعبدها أعتقتك على تتزوجني بألف فقبل عتق وعليه قيمته لها إن أبى أن يتزوجها وإلا قسم الألف على قيمة نفسه وعلى مهر مثلها، فما أصاب الرقبة فهو قيمته وما أصاب المهر فهو مهرها يتنصف بالطلاق قبل الدخول. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو تزوجها على أن يحج بها وجب مهر المثل لكن فرق في الخانية بين أن يتزوجها على أن يحج بها وبين أن يتزوجها على حجة فأوجب في الأولى مهر المثل وفي الثانية صحة التسمية.
And in al-Khaniyyah: If a man marries a woman on the condition of a slave-girl (jariyah) on the condition that her service is for him as long as she lives, or that what is in her womb is for him, then the slave-girl, her service, and what is in her womb belong to the woman if her mahr al-mithl equals or exceeds the value of the slave-girl. If her mahr al-mithl is less than the value of the slave-girl, then she gets mahr al-mithl unless the husband voluntarily gives the slave-girl to her. And the author pointed out that if he frees a female slave and makes her emancipation her dower, the naming is invalid because emancipation is not wealth; if she marries him, she gets mahr al-mithl, and if she refuses, she is not forced and she owes her value to the master. Similarly, umm walad (mother of his child) but no value is due from her to him according to her family. And if she says to her slave: 'I free you on condition that you marry me for a thousand,' and he accepts, he is freed and owes her his value if he refuses to marry her; otherwise, the thousand is divided proportionally between his value and her mahr al-mithl. What falls to the 'neck' (of slavery) is his value, and what falls to the mahr is her dower, which is halved by divorce before consummation. And the author pointed out that if he marries her on condition that he performs Hajj with her, mahr al-mithl is wajib, but al-Khaniyyah distinguishes between marriage on condition that he performs Hajj with her (mahr al-mithl) and marriage on condition of a Hajj (i.e., a specific Hajj act) – in the latter, the naming is valid.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage presents several discrete rulings on non-standard dowers. First, if the dower is a slave-girl with conditions attached (e.g., her service for the husband), the ruling depends on comparison with mahr al-mithl. Second, if a man frees a female slave and makes her freedom her dower, this is invalid because emancipation is not wealth; she gets mahr al-mithl. If she refuses the marriage, she owes her value. The case of umm walad (a slave who bore her master's child) is similar but no value is owed. Third, a case of a woman freeing her slave on condition of marriage; the slave's dower is calculated by dividing the sum. Fourth, dower of Hajj: the author notes a distinction between 'performing Hajj with her' (invalid, mahr al-mithl) and 'a Hajj' (a specific Hajj act) as valid dower. These rulings illustrate the Hanafi principle that the dower must be something of value (mal) or a valid usufruct.

Key Terms
جارية (jariyah): A young female slave (concubine).
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The standard dower for a woman of her status, used as a benchmark when the named dower is invalid or excessive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man marries on a dower of a slave-girl valued at 1000 with condition of her service, and her mahr al-mithl is 800, what does she receive?
A) The slave-girl with service
B) 800 dirhams as mahr al-mithl
C) 1000 dirhams
D) Nothing, the dower is void

Key Takeaway
A conditional dower (slave-girl with service/child) is valid but subject to value comparison with mahr al-mithl.

Invalid Dowers: Freeing a Slave and Related Cases
Multiple rulings on dower via emancipation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why emancipation cannot be a dower in Hanafi fiqh and identify the correct outcome (mahr al-mithl) for both a free man freeing a slave and a woman freeing her slave on condition of marriage.

Core Idea
Emancipation is not wealth, so it cannot be a dower; failure to perform the condition leads to mahr al-mithl.

This lesson covers three scenarios: a man freeing a female slave as dower, the special case of umm walad, and a woman freeing her male slave on condition of marriage. In all, the dower is invalid because emancipation is not considered mal (wealth). The wife receives mahr al-mithl, and the slave's freedom is evaluated separately.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of emancipation
Determine if the emancipation is by the husband of a female slave (including umm walad) or by a woman of her male slave.
Umm walad is a slave who bore her master's child.
2
Rule on the dower's validity
Emancipation is not mal, so naming it as dower is invalid. The wife gets mahr al-mithl.
This applies whether the man is freeing his own slave or the woman is freeing her slave.
3
Handle the consequences for the freed slave
If the slave is freed and the marriage proceeds (for the male slave case, conditional acceptance), the slave's freedom stands. If the condition is not fulfilled (woman's slave refuses marriage), the slave must pay his value.
In the umm walad case, no value is owed to the master.
4
Calculate proportional dower in the woman freeing her slave scenario
If the woman's slave agrees to marry her for a payment, the amount is divided proportionally between his value (as dower for her) and her mahr al-mithl.
This ensures fairness.

Source Text

Hajj as Dower: Valid and Invalid Forms
Distinction between valid and invalid Hajj dower.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a valid and invalid dower involving Hajj, applying the Hanafi principle that a pure usufruct (e.g., a specific Hajj) is valid but companionship (Hajj with her) is not.

Core Idea
A specified Hajj can be a dower; accompanying the husband on Hajj cannot.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling on making Hajj the dower. The key distinction is between 'Hajj with her' (invalid) and 'a Hajj' as a specified service (valid). The latter is considered a usufruct that can be measured, while the former involves companionship which is not pure usufruct.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrasing of the dower
Is the dower expressed as 'I will perform Hajj with you' or 'I will give you a Hajj' (i.e., the act of pilgrimage)?
The wording determines validity.
2
Apply the first case (Hajj with her)
If the marriage is on condition that he performs Hajj with her, this includes companionship and travel, which is not a pure usufruct. Therefore, the dower is invalid, and she gets mahr al-mithl.
Companionship cannot be precisely valued.
3
Apply the second case (a Hajj)
If the marriage is on condition of a Hajj (i.e., he will perform a specific Hajj on her behalf or provide the means), the dower is valid because Hajj is a measurable service that can be assigned a value.
This is considered a valid usufruct.
4
Note the source of distinction
This distinction is explicitly mentioned in al-Khaniyyah, showing the school's precision.
The author follows al-Khaniyyah on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Teaching Quran as Mahr: From Invalidity to Permissibility in the Hanafi School
Dispute over validity of teaching Quran as mahr and change in fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the original Hanafi ruling on teaching Quran as mahr, explain the later fatwa change, and identify the key proofs and the ongoing evolution.

Core Idea
Teaching Quran is not wealth, so it cannot be dower — but later Hanafi fatwa aligned with practice and permitted it.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a key nikah issue: can a husband give teaching of the Quran as the mahr (dower)? The original Hanafi position in Zahir al-Riwayah says no, but later fatwa changed. We will examine the proofs, the Shafi'i opposition, and the evolution of the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and original ruling
What is the act under discussion? (Teaching Quran as mahr). What is the original Hanafi ruling? (Invalid; mahr al-mithl is due). State the legal category (wajib for mahr al-mithl).
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah: teaching is not mal, so cannot be dower.
2
Locate the Hanafi proofs
List the three proofs cited: (1) dower must be wealth (mal), (2) teaching is an act of worship, not suitable for exchange, (3) Quranic verse 2:237 requires divisibility of the prescribed dower, which teaching lacks.
The hadith 'marry her with what you have of Quran' is interpreted non-literally.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i counter-evidence and the Hanafi response
Shafi'is accept the hadith as proof and allow any benefit as dower. Hanafis respond that the preposition 'ba' in the hadith indicates cause, not price. Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in validity.
The response shows Hanafi usul in action: not taking the apparent meaning when other indications exist.
4
Trace the later fatwa change and its basis
Later Hanafi fatwa (mutakhkhirin) permitted hiring for teaching Quran and fiqh. By extension, teaching can be valid as dower because whatever benefit is compensable in ijarah can be named as sadaq. This is based on a shift in the ruling on ijarah for teaching.
Ibn Nujaym notes this evolution but says he hasn't seen anyone explicitly state it.
5
Determine the mufta bihi today
The relied-upon position is that teaching Quran can be valid dower due to the change in fatwa on ijarah. The practical difference between Hanafi and Shafi'i is now minimal on this point.
Check fatwa hierarchy: original position is Zahir al-Riwayah, but later fatwa overrides for contemporary practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وتعليم القرآن أي يجب مهر المثل إذا جعل الصداق تعليم القرآن لأن المشروع إنما هو الابتغاء بالمال والتعليم ليس بمال وكذا المنافع على أصلنا، ولأن التعليم عبادة فلا يصلح أن يكون صداقاً، ولأن قوله تعالى فنصف ما فرضتم [البقرة: ٢٣٧] يدل على أنه لا بد أن يكون المفروض مما له نصف حتى يمكنه أن يرجع عليها بنصفه إذا طلقها قبل الدخول بعد القبض ولا يمكن ذلك في التعليم، وأما قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «زوجتكها بما معك من القرآن فليست الباء متعينة للعوض الجواز أن تكون للسببية أو للتعليل أي لأجل أنك أهل القرآن أو المراد ببركة ما معك منه فلا يصلح دليلاً، وسيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى في كتاب الإجارات أن الفتوى اليوم على جواز الاستئجار لتعليم القرآن والفقه فينبغي أن يصح مهراً لأن ما جاز أخذ الأجر في مقابلته من المنافع جاز تسميته صداقاً كما قدمناه نقله عن البدائع، ولهذا ذكر في فتح القدير هنا أنه لما جوز الشافعي أخذ الأجر على تعليم القرآن تسميته صداقاً، فكذا نقول : يلزم على المفتى به صحة تسميته صداقاً ولم أر أحداً له والله الموفق للصواب. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو أعتق أمة وجعل عتقها صداقها فإن التسمية لا تصح لأن العتق ليس بمال، فإن تزوجته فلها مهر المثل، وإن أبت لا تجبر وعليها قيمتها للمولى، وكذا أم الولد لكن لا قيمة عليها له عند ،آبائها ولو قالت لعبدها أعتقتك على تتزوجني بألف فقبل عتق وعليه قيمته لها إن أبى أن يتزوجها وإلا قسم الألف على قيمة نفسه وعلى مهر مثلها، فما أصاب الرقبة فهو قيمته وما أصاب المهر فهو مهرها يتنصف بالطلاق قبل الدخول. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو تزوجها على أن يحج بها وجب مهر المثل لكن فرق في الخانية بين أن يتزوجها على أن يحج بها وبين أن يتزوجها على حجة فأوجب في الأول مهر المثل وفي الثاني قيمة حجة وسط .اهـ. وقد وقع في شرحه هنا لابن الملك خلل في التوجيه فاجتنبه وفي الخانية : ولو تزوج امرأة على جارية على أن له خدمتها ما عاش أو ما في بطنها له كانت الجارية وخدمتها وما في بطنها للمرأة إن كان مهر مثلها مثل قيمة الخادم أو أكثر، وإن كان مهر مثلها أقل من قيمة الخادم كان لها مهر المثل إلا أن يسلم الزوج الخادم إليها باختياره .
His statement: (And teaching Quran), i.e., mahr al-mithl is obligatory if the dower is made teaching Quran, because what is prescribed is only acquisition with wealth, and teaching is not wealth, and likewise benefits according to our principle, and because teaching is a form of worship, so it is not suitable to be dower, and because the saying of Allah the Exalted 'then half of what you prescribed' (al-Baqarah 2:237) indicates that it is necessary that the prescribed thing have a half so that he can take back half from her if he divorces her before entry after taking possession, and that is not possible in teaching. As for his saying peace be upon him 'I marry her to you with what you have of Quran', the preposition 'with' is not necessarily for compensation; it could be for cause or explanation, i.e., because you are a person of Quran, or the intent is the blessing of what you have, so it is not a proof. It will come, Allah willing, in the Book of Ijarah that today the fatwa is upon the permissibility of hiring for teaching Quran and fiqh, so it should be valid as a dower because whatever it is permissible to take rent in exchange for from benefits, it is permissible to name it as dower, as we have previously transmitted from al-Bada'i. For this reason, it is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir that when al-Shafi'i permitted taking wages for teaching Quran, he named it as dower, so we also say: according to the mufta bihi, the validity of naming it as dower is necessary, and I have not seen anyone for it, and Allah is the grantor of success. And the author indicated that if he frees a slave woman and makes her emancipation her dower, the naming is not valid because emancipation is not wealth; if he marries her, she has mahr al-mithl, and if she refuses, she is not compelled and she owes her value to the master. Similarly, umm walad, but she owes no value to him according to her [؟] fathers. And if she says to her slave: I free you on condition that you marry me for a thousand, and he accepts, he is freed and he owes his value to her if he refuses to marry her; otherwise, the thousand is divided between his value and her mahr al-mithl: what corresponds to the slave body is his value, and what corresponds to the mahr is her mahr, and it is halved upon divorce before entry. And the author indicated that if he marries her on condition that he perform Hajj with her, mahr al-mithl is obligatory, but al-Khaniyyah distinguished between marrying on condition that he perform Hajj with her and between marrying on condition of a Hajj, so in the first he made mahr al-mithl obligatory, and in the second the value of an average Hajj. End. And there occurred in his commentary here by Ibn al-Malik a defect in the direction, so avoid it. And in al-Khaniyyah: If a man marries a woman on a slave girl on condition that he has her service as long as he lives, or what is in her belly is his, the slave girl and her service and what is in her belly belong to the woman if her mahr al-mithl is like the value of the servant or more, and if her mahr al-mithl is less than the value of the servant, she has mahr al-mithl unless the husband voluntarily hands over the servant to her.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Raiq explaining the ruling on teaching Quran as a dower. The Hanafi position is that teaching is not wealth (mal), and thus cannot be a valid dower; instead, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (proper dower). The commentator provides three proofs: (1) the legal principle that dower must be wealth, (2) teaching is an act of worship and not suitable for exchange, (3) the Quranic verse (2:237) assumes the dower can be halved, which is impossible for teaching. The hadith 'I marry her to you with what you have of Quran' is interpreted by Hanafis as referring to the cause or blessing, not the price. The commentator then notes that later fatwa (mutakkhirin) permits hiring for teaching Quran, and thus teaching can now be valid as dower by analogy to permissible benefits. This reflects an evolution within the Hanafi school from strict adherence to Zahir al-Riwayah to accommodating new realities. The passage also touches on other similar cases: emancipation, Hajj, and service of a slave girl as dower, all reinforcing the principle that non-wealth items cannot be dower unless later permissibility allows.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower equivalent to what women of her status receive, given when the named dower is invalid or not specified.
مال (mal): Wealth or property; in this context, what has material value and can be legally transacted.
صداق (sadaq): Synonym for mahr (dower); the gift given by the husband to the wife upon marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the original Hanafi ruling regarding teaching Quran as a dower?
A) It is valid and the wife is entitled to that teaching.
B) It is invalid, and the wife receives mahr al-mithl.
C) It is valid only if the husband is a scholar.
D) It is makruh but valid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school evolved from treating teaching Quran as an invalid mahr to permitting it, reflecting the principle that rulings can change based on prevailing custom and analogical extension (ijarah).

Service of a Slave Husband as Mahr
Ruling on making a slave's service to his wife the dower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making a husband's service the dower, distinguishing between free and slave spouses, and explain the reasoning (talil) behind the distinction.

Core Idea
A slave's service can be dower with permission; a free husband's service is invalid due to degradation.

The possibility of making a husband's personal service the dower in a marriage contract depends critically on the husband's status. This passage from the Hanafi literature clarifies the rule: a slave husband may serve his wife as mahr with his master's consent, but a free husband's service is forbidden because it is degrading. The reasoning hinges on the nature of freedom and the dignity it confers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the condition in a marriage contract that the husband serves the wife as mahr. The ruling: for a free husband, it is haram and invalid; for a slave husband with master's permission, it is valid.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is analogical reasoning (qiyas). The slave's service to his wife with the master's permission is equated to service to the master himself, and the lack of dignity in the slave's status makes it permissible.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause (illa) is the absence of the dignity of freedom. Since a slave has no such dignity, serving his wife is not degrading; for a free man, serving his wife is degrading and thus prohibited.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The passage cites multiple Hanafi authorities agreeing, but notes that some other schools might allow free husband's service. However, the Hanafi position is settled.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi is that a free husband's service cannot be valid mahr; a slave's can with permission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ولها خدمته لو عبداً) يعني لو تزوج عبد حرة على خدمته لها سنة بإذن مولاه صحت التسمية ويخدمها سنة لأنه لما خدمها بإذن المولى صار كأنه يخدم مولاه حقيقة ولأن خدمة العبد لزوجته ليست بحرام إذ ليس له شرف الحرية ولهذا سلبت عنه عامة الكرامات الثابتة للأحرار، فكذا هذا كذا في غاية البيان. وصرح الولوالجي في فتاواه بأن استخدام الزوج لا يجوز لما فيه من الاستهانة. وصرح قاضيخان في شرح الجامع الصغير بأن خدمة الزوج لها حرام لأنها توجب الإهانة اهـ . وفي البدائع : إن استخدام الحرة زوجها الحر حرام لكونه استهانة وإذلالاً اهـ. وحاصله أنه يحرم عليها الاستخدام ويحرم عليه الخدمة لها، وظاهر المختصر أن المرأة حرة لأنه جعل الخدمة لها. وأما لو تزوج عبد أمة على خدمته سنة لمولاها فإنه صحيح بالأولى ويخدم المولى. وينبغي أنه لو تزوجها على أن يخدمها أن لا تصح التسمية أصلاً ولم أرهما صريحاً
His statement: (And she has his service if he is a slave) meaning if a slave marries a free woman on condition of his service to her for a year, with the permission of his master, the naming [of the dower] is valid, and he serves her for a year because when he serves her with the master's permission, it is as if he serves his master in reality, and because the service of a slave to his wife is not forbidden since he does not possess the honor of freedom, and therefore all the dignities established for free men are denied to him. So this is the case. This is from Ghayat al-Bayan. And al-Walwaliji explicitly stated in his Fatawa that the use of a husband [for service] is not permissible because it involves degradation. And Qadikhan explicitly stated in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir that the service of a husband to her is forbidden because it necessitates degradation. End. And in al-Bada'i: The use of her free husband by a free woman is forbidden because it is degradation and humiliation. End. The conclusion is that it is forbidden for her to use him and forbidden for him to serve her. And the apparent meaning of the Mukhtasar is that the woman is free because he made the service for her. As for if a slave marries a slave woman on condition of his service to her master for a year, it is valid a fortiori, and he serves the master. And it is appropriate that if he marries her on condition that he serve her, the naming is invalid essentially, and I have not seen it explicitly.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on making a slave's service the dower. The matn states that a woman can have the service of her husband if he is a slave. The commentary clarifies that this is valid only if the slave husband's master permits it, because the service is effectively for the master. The reason a slave can serve his wife is that he lacks the honor of freedom, so it is not degrading for him. In contrast, it is forbidden for a free husband to serve his wife because it involves degradation, as stated by multiple authorities like al-Walwaliji and Qadikhan. The commentary also notes that if a slave marries a female slave, her master can stipulate the husband's service to him, and that is valid. The author suggests that if the condition is simply that the husband serve his wife (without specifying slave), the naming is invalid, though he hasn't found an explicit text.

Key Terms
خدمة (khidmah): Service; specifically the husband's personal service to his wife as a condition in the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Valid, and he must serve her.
B) Makruh, but valid.
C) Invalid, and she gets mahr al-mithl because it is forbidden.
D) Valid only if he is a slave.

Key Takeaway
The validity of service as mahr hinges on the husband's freedom; a slave's service is permissible, a free man's is not.

Husband's Recoupment of Half Dower When Wife Gifts Fungible Mahr
Ruling on recouping half dower when wife gifts and divorce occurs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a husband recoups half the dower when the wife gifts it back and divorce occurs before consummation, and explain the qiyas vs. istihsan distinction.

Core Idea
A gift of fungible dower after acceptance does not cancel the husband's right to half upon divorce before consummation.

This lesson explores a specific marriage contract scenario: after the wife takes full possession of the dower (e.g., 1000 dirhams) and then gifts it to her husband, he divorces her before consummation. Does he still get half the dower? The Hanafi school applies istihsan to conclude he does, because dirhams and dinars are fungible and the gift does not deliver the exact half he is owed. We will unpack the reasoning, including an intra-Hanafi disagreement with Zufar who follows strict qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
Recall the general rule: if a husband divorces before consummation, the wife is entitled to half the specified dower. Here, the wife already accepted the full dower and then gave it back as a gift. The question is whether the husband can recover half from her.
Default ruling: half dower is due to wife, but she gifted it back. Does that satisfy the husband's obligation?
2
Apply the ruling to the given scenario
In the scenario where the wife accepted dirhams (fungible) and then gifted all of them, the husband takes back half. Reason: dirhams are not specified in contracts, so the gift does not convey the exact half he is entitled to. He may demand half the value.
Crucial condition: the dower must be fungible (dirhams/dinars). If the dower is a specific commodity, the ruling differs.
3
Contrast qiyas and istihsan
Zufar held that by qiyas the husband should get nothing because the gift is like an ibra' (release) – it transfers ownership fully and extinguishes any claim. However, the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) adopted istihsan, reasoning that the purpose of the gift is to clear the husband's liability, but for fungibles, the gift does not achieve that because the husband still owes half the dower. Thus, he recoups half.
The dispute hinges on the nature of the gift: does it operate as a discharge of the dower debt or not?
4
Distinguish other scenarios
If the wife never accepted any dower, or accepted only half and then gifted the whole, or if the dower is a specified commodity, the husband gets nothing upon divorce before consummation. The three subcases are explained in the text.
The istihsan exception applies only when she accepted and gifted all fungible dower.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو قبضت ألف المهر ووهبته له فطلقها قبل الوطء رجع عليها بالنصف لأنه لم يصل إليه بالهبة عين ما يستوجبه لأن الدراهم والدنانير لا يتعينان في العقود والفسوخ، ولذا لو سمى لها دراهم وأشار إليها له أن يحبسها ويدفع مثلها جنساً ونوعاً وقدراً وصفة كذا في البدائع. ولا يلزمها رد عين ما أخذت بالطلاق قبل الدخول، ولذا قال الولوالجي في فتاواه من باب الزكاة : ولو تزوج رجل امرأة على ألف درهم وقبضت وحال الحول ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بها زكت الألف كلها لأنه وجب في ذمتها مثل نفس المقبوض لا عين المقبوض، والدين بعد الحول لا يسقط الواجب، ولو كانت سائمة غير الأثمان زكت نصفها لأنه استحق نصفها من غير اختيارها فصار كالهلاك، ولا يزكي الزوج شيئاً لأن ملك الزوج الآن عاد في النصف ا هـ . وأشار المصنف إلى أن حكم المكيل والموزون إذا لم يكن معيناً حكم النقد لعدم التعيين، وأما المعين منه فكالعرض وفي البدائع : وإن كان تبراً أو نقرة ذهباً أو فضة فهو كالعرض في رواية فيجبر على تسليم العين وفي رواية كالمضروب فلا يجبر . قوله : (فإن لم تقبض الألف أو قبضت النصف ووهبت الألف أو وهبت العرض المهر قبل القبض أو بعده فطلقت قبل الوطء لم يرجع عليها بشيء) بيان لمفهوم المسألة المقتدمة وهي مسائل : ثلاث الأولى إذا لم تقبض شيئاً من المهر ثم وهبته كله له ثم طلقها قبل الدخول فإنه لا رجوع له عليها بشيء، وفي القياس يرجع عليها بنصف الصداق وهو قول زفر لأنه سلم له بالإبراء فلا تبرأ عما يستحقه بالطلاق ووجه الاستحسان أنه وصل إليه عين ما يستحقه بالطلاق قبل الدخول وهو براءة ذمته عن نصف المهر، ولا يبالي باختلاف السبب عند حصول المقصود وله نظائر منها ما في معراج الدراية الغاصب إذا وهب المغصوب
His statement: (And if she accepted one thousand of the dower and gifted it to him, and he divorced her before intercourse, he takes back half from her) because what he received via the gift is not the exact thing he is entitled to, because dirhams and dinars are not specified in contracts and annulments. Hence, if he named dirhams for her and pointed to them, he may withhold them and pay their like in type, quantity, and quality, as in al-Bada'i. And she is not obliged to return the exact thing she took upon divorce before entry. Hence al-Walwaliji said in his Fatawa in the chapter of zakat: If a man marries a woman on one thousand dirhams, and she accepted and a year passed, then he divorces her before entry, she pays zakat on the entire thousand because a like of what she received became due in her liability, not the exact thing, and debt after a year does not drop the obligation. And if [the dower] were livestock other than silver/gold, she pays zakat on half of it because half becomes due from her involuntarily, so it is like destruction. And the husband does not pay zakat because his ownership of half now returns. End. And the author indicated that the ruling for measured and weighed items if unspecified is like cash due to lack of specification; but if specified, it is like a commodity. And in al-Bada'i: If it is gold or silver in nugget or dust form, it is like a commodity in one narration—he is forced to deliver the exact thing; in another narration, like minted coin—he is not forced. His statement: (If she did not accept the thousand, or she accepted half and gifted the thousand, or she gifted the commodity dower before or after acceptance, then he divorces before intercourse, he does not take back anything from her) is an explanation of the implication of the preceding issue, and they are three issues: First: if she did not accept anything of the dower then she gifted all of it to him, then he divorced her before entry, he has no recourse to anything from her. In qiyas, he would take back half the dower—this is the view of Zufar—because he released her (by accepting the gift) and she does not become free from what he is entitled to by divorce. The istihsan justification is that he received exactly what he is entitled to upon divorce before entry, which is the clearance of his liability for half the dower, and differing causes are not considered when the goal is achieved. There are parallels to it, including what is in Mi'raj al-Dirayah: the usurper if he gifts the usurped [item]...
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where the wife takes possession of the full dower (e.g., 1000 dirhams) and then gifts it back to her husband. If he divorces her before consummation, does he recoup half? The ruling: yes, he takes back half, because dirhams and dinars are fungible (not specified), so the gift does not deliver the exact thing he is owed (the husband's right is to half the dower, but he hasn't gotten it yet). However, if she never took possession, or only took half and then gifted the whole, then if she gifts before divorce, he gets nothing because the gift effectively clears his claim. The passage contrasts qiyas (analogy, held by Zufar) and istihsan. Qiyas says he should still get half because the gift is like an ibra' (release) that doesn't fulfill the spouse's right. Istihsan says he gets nothing because the husband received the benefit of being free from half the dower. The passage also touches on zakat implications for the wife, and distinguishes between specified and unspecified commodities.

Key Terms
القبض (al-qabd): Taking possession of the dower by the wife; legal acceptance that transfers liability.
الهبة (al-hibah): Gift; here, the wife's voluntary transfer of the dower back to the husband.
الطلاق قبل الدخول (al-talaq qabl al-dukhul): Divorce before consummation; results in half the dower being due to the wife if specified.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference; deviation from qiyas in favor of a more equitable outcome.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a wife accepts 1000 dirhams as dower, then gifts it to the husband, and he divorces her before consummation, how much does the husband recoup?
A) Nothing
B) 500 dirhams (half)
C) 1000 dirhams (full)
D) It depends on whether the dirhams were specified

Key Takeaway
The husband recoups half the dower if the wife accepted fungible dower and then gifted it, because the gift does not extinguish his half right.

beginner
5 min
Return of Half Mahr and the Gift Exception
Initial matn and brief commentary on mahr return exception when wife gifts back

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule of mahr return upon pre-consummation divorce and identify the three scenarios where the husband recovers nothing due to the wife's gift.

Core Idea
If the wife gifts the mahr to the husband, he cannot recover half upon pre-consummation divorce.

This lesson examines the foundational rule from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: when a husband divorces his wife before consummation, he is entitled to half the mahr. However, the rule has an important exception: if the wife has gifted the mahr to her husband, whether before or after taking possession, he recovers nothing. Understanding this exception requires attention to the timing and nature of the gift.

Guided Path
1
State the general principle
Read the opening line: before intercourse, the husband takes back half of the mahr.
This is the default rule (hukm asli).
2
List the three exception scenarios
Identify: (a) wife never took possession of the mahr and gifts it, (b) she took half and then gifted the entire mahr, (c) she gifted the 'ard mahr (non-cash) before or after receipt.
In all three, the husband recovers nothing.
3
Recognize the condition of a valid gift
The gift (hiba) must be validly executed: offer, acceptance, and delivery.
If the gift is invalid, the exception does not apply.
4
Note the valuation detail
The commentary adds that in the default case, half is based on mahr al-mithl; in the 'ard case, value is assessed by a credible witness.
This clarifies how to calculate the half when the mahr is not monetary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكاح باب المهر قبل الوطء رجع عليها بالنصف فإن لم تقبض الألف أو قبضت النصف ووهبت الألف أو وهبت العرض المهر قبل القبض أو بعده فطلقت قبل الوطء لم يرجع عليها بشيء الأول مهر المثل وفي الثاني قيمة حجة وسط
Book of Nikah, Chapter of Mahr: Before intercourse, he takes back half. If she did not receive the thousand, or she received half and gifted the thousand, or she gifted the 'ard mahr before or after receipt, and he divorced her before intercourse, he does not take back anything from her. First: mahr al-mithl; and in the second: value of a medium witness.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is the matn (core text) from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It states the general rule: if a husband divorces his wife before consummation, he recovers half the mahr. However, if she has not yet taken possession of the mahr (e.g., the specified amount of dirhams or a specific item) and then gifts it back to him, or if she takes possession of half and then gifts the entire mahr, or if she gifts the 'ard mahr (non-monetary dower) either before or after taking possession, and then he divorces her before consummation, he does not recover anything. The brief comment explains that in the first case (default) the half is based on mahr al-mithl (the proper dower), and in the second scenario (gift of 'ard) the value is assessed by a medium witness.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): The dower given by the husband to the wife as an obligation of marriage.
قبض (qabd): Taking possession of the mahr (receiving it physically or constructively).
هبة (hiba): Gift; here the wife gifting back the mahr to the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, in which of the following scenarios does the husband recover half the mahr after a pre-consummation divorce?
A) Wife never received the mahr and gifts it back.
B) Wife received half the mahr and gifts the full mahr back.
C) Wife received the full mahr and does not gift it back.
D) Wife received the full mahr and then gifts it back.

Key Takeaway
If the wife gifts the mahr to the husband before pre-consummation divorce, he loses his right to recover half.

Istihsan Overriding Qiyas: The Case of Mahr Gift and Divorce Before Consummation
Extended commentary on mahr gift exception with istihsan vs qiyas debate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each of the three mahr gift scenarios and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas in the first scenario.

Core Idea
When the wife gifts the entire mahr before receipt, the husband recovers nothing by istihsan because his objective is already achieved.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on a subtle exception in mahr rulings. It presents three scenarios where the wife gifts the mahr and is divorced before consummation. The first scenario involves no prior receipt, and the Hanafi school applies istihsan to override the qiyas that would require recovery. The discussion reveals the school's methodology for prioritizing practical objectives over strict analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sub-issues
The passage breaks down the matn exception into three cases: (a) wife never received mahr and gifts it all, (b) wife received half and gifts entire mahr, (c) wife gifts the 'ard mahr. Distinguish the scenarios.
2
Analyze the first sub-issue: no receipt, full gift
Note the ruling: husband recovers nothing by istihsan. Understand the opposing qiyas (Zufar's view) and why istihsan overrides.
3
Examine the istihsan reasoning
The husband's objective (release from half the mahr) is achieved through the gift; difference in cause (gift vs. divorce) is irrelevant when the objective is met.
The passage lists analogues to reinforce this principle.
4
Consider the analogues and objections
Analogue cases include usurpation, fasid sale, gift from a sick person, mortgage, and salam. An objection from al-Tabyin about differing objectives is addressed.
5
Understand the second sub-issue: intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
When wife receives half and gifts all, Abu Hanifa says no recovery; the Sahibayn say recover half of what she received. Grasp the thamarah al-khilaf.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's view.

أن يحبسها ويدفع مثلها جنساً ونوعاً وقدراً وصفة كذا في البدائع. ولا يلزمها رد عين ما أخذت بالطلاق قبل الدخول، ولذا قال الولوالجي في فتاواه من باب الزكاة : ولو تزوج رجل امرأة على ألف درهم وقبضت وحال الحول ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بها زكت الألف كلها لأنه وجب في ذمتها مثل نفس المقبوض لا عين المقبوض، والدين بعد الحول لا يسقط الواجب، ولو كانت سائمة غير الأثمان زكت نصفها لأنه استحق نصفها من غير اختيارها قبل الوطء لم يرجع عليها بشيء) بيان لمفهوم المسألة المقتدمة وهي مسائل : : الأولى إذا لم تقبض شيئاً من المهر ثم وهبته كله له ثم طلقها قبل الدخول فإنه لا ثلاثة رجوع له عليها بشيء، وفي القياس يرجع عليها بنصف الصداق وهو قول زفر لأنه سلم له بالإبراء فلا تبرأ عما يستحقه بالطلاق ووجه الاستحسان أنه وصل إليه عين ما يستحقه بالطلاق قبل الدخول وهو براءة ذمته عن نصف المهر، ولا يبالي باختلاف السبب عند حصول المقصود وله نظائر منها ما في معراج الدراية الغاصب إذا وهب المغصوب للمغصوب منه ومثله ما إذا قال إنك غصبت مني ألف درهم فقال المدعى عليه بل استقرضتها اهـ. وتمامه في التلخيص. ومنها ما إذا باع بيعاً فاسداً وقبض المشتري المبيع ثم وهبه للبائع لا يضمن قيمته لحصول المقصود بخلاف ما لو وصل المبيع إليه من جهة غير المشتري حيث لا يبرأ من الضمان لأنه لم يصل إليه من الجهة المستحقه. ومنها ما إذا اشترى جارية بعبد ثم وهب الجارية من مشتري العبد ثم استحق العبد من يده فإنه لا يرجع على المشتري للجارية بقيمتها استحساناً. ومنها مريض وهب جارية من إنسان لا مال له غيرها وسلم الجارية إليه ثم وهب الموهوب له الجارية من المريض ثم مات من مرضه فإنه لا يضمن الموهوب له قيمة ثلثي الجارية للورثة استحساناً بخلاف ما لو وهب المريض لأحد بنيه عبداً ثم وهبه الأخ لأخيه ثم مات الأب فإنه يرجع على أخيه الواهب بنصف قيمة العبد لأنه ما وصل إليه من جهة أبيه ومنها المرتهن إذا أبرأ الراهن عن الدين ثم هلك الرهن في يد المرتهن يضمن. ومنها المسلم إليه إذا وهب رأس المال وهو عرض من رب السلم ثم تقايلا السلم لا يعزم المسلم إليه شيئاً استحساناً، ويلزمه قيمته قياساً وهو قول زفر . كذا في المحيط. ويرد على هذا الأصل أعني أنه لا اعتبار لاختلاف السبب إذا حصل المقصود ما ذكره في التبيين من باب التحالف : لو قال بعتني هذه الجارية فأنكر فقال ما بعتكها وإنما زوجتكها فإنه لا يجوز له أن يطأها لاختلاف الحكم فإن حكم ملك اليمين خلاف حكم الزوجية ا هـ . إلا أن يقال : إنه ليس من قبيل حصول المقصود لأن المقصود منهما مختلف، وينبغي أن يكون داخلاً تحت الأصل المذكور ما إذا أقر له هي بألف من ثمن متاع فقال المقر له غصب قال الزيلعي من باب التحالف: إنه يؤمر بالدفع إليه لاتحاد الحكم وفي تلخيص الجامع من باب الإقرار بما يكون قصاصاً : قال : أودعتني هذه الألف فقال بل لي ألف قرض فقد لأن رد العين غير الدين إلا أن يتصادقا لأن المقر كالمبتدئ، ولو قال أقرضتكها أخذ الألف لأن التكاذب في الزوال. ولو قال غصبتك أخذ ألفاً لأن موجبه الضمان فاتفقا على الدين واختلفا في الجهة فلغت، وكذا لو أقر بالقرض وهو ادعى الثمن ا هـ . وفي المعراج : فإن قيل يلزم على هذا ما إذا اشترى عبداً بألف ثم حط البائع عشر الثمن ثم وجد به عيباً ينقص عشر الثمن حيث يرجع بنقصان العيب وإن حصل له هذا بالحط قلنا موجب العيب سقوط بعض الثمن وهذا لا يحصل له بالحط لأن المحطوط خرج عن كونه ثمناً ا هـ. المسألة الثانية ما إذا قبضت النصف ثم وهبت الكل المقبوض وغيره ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بها فإنه لا يرجع واحد منهما على صاحبه بشيء عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا يرجع عليها بنصف ما قبضت اعتباراً للبعض بالكل لأن الحط يلتحق بأصل العقد وله أن مقصوده سلامة النصف بالطلاق وقد حصل والحط لا يلتحق بأصل العقد في النكاح كالزيادة، ولذا لا تتنصف الزيادة مع الأصل اتفاقاً. هكذا في الهداية وغاية البيان والتبيين وكثير من الكتب واستشكله في فتح القدير بأن التحاق
His saying: (And if she received the thousand of the mahr and gifted it to him, then he divorced her before intercourse, he takes back half from her) because what he is entitled to did not reach him through the gift as a specific thing, since dirhams and dinars are not determined in contracts and dissolutions. Therefore, if he specified dirhams for her and pointed to them, he may withhold them and give their like in type, kind, quantity, and description. So in al-Bada'i'. And she is not obliged to return the very thing she took upon divorce before consummation. Hence al-Walwalji said in his Fatawa in the chapter of Zakat: If a man marries a woman on a thousand dirhams, she receives it, a year passes, then he divorces her before consummation, she pays zakat on the entire thousand because obligation fell on her for the like of what was received, not the specific thing; and debt after a year does not drop the obligation. But if it was grazing livestock other than precious metals, she pays zakat on half because half becomes due from her without her choice, so it is like destruction. The husband does not pay zakat on anything because his ownership has returned to half. The author indicated that the ruling for measured and weighed items, if not specified, is the same as currency due to lack of specification; if specified, it is like an 'ard. In al-Bada'i': if it is gold or silver in nugget or ingot form, it is like an 'ard in one narration, so he is forced to deliver the specific item; in another narration, it is like minted coins, so he is not forced. His saying: (If she did not receive the thousand, or she received half and gifted the thousand, or she gifted the 'ard mahr before or after receipt, and he divorced her before intercourse, he does not take back anything) is an explanation of the concept of the preceding issue, and they are three issues: First: if she did not receive anything of the mahr then gifted it all to him, then he divorced her before consummation, he does not take back anything from her. By qiyas, he would take back half the dower, which is the view of Zufar, because he transferred (ownership) to him by discharge, so she is not cleared from what he deserves by divorce. The aspect of istihsan is that the very thing he deserves by divorce before consummation reached him, i.e., the discharge of his liability for half the mahr. Difference in cause is not considered when the objective is achieved. There are analogues to this, from Ma'raj al-Diraya: a usurper who gifts the usurped item to the one from whom it was usurped; similarly, if one says 'you usurped a thousand dirhams from me' and the defendant says 'rather I borrowed it'; and from it, if one sold a fasid sale, the buyer took possession of the sold item, then gifted it to the seller, he is not liable for its value because the objective is achieved, unlike if the sold item reached him from someone other than the buyer. And from it, if one bought a female slave for a slave, then gifted the female slave to the buyer of the slave, then the slave is found to be owned by another from his hand, he does not take back from the buyer of the female slave its value by istihsan. And from it, a sick person gifted a female slave to a person who has no property other than her, handed her over, then the donee gifted the female slave back to the sick person, then the sick person died from his illness: the donee is not liable for two-thirds of the female slave's value to the heirs by istihsan, unlike if the sick person gifted a slave to one of his sons, then the brother gifted to his brother, then the father died: he does take back from the brother half the value of the slave because it did not reach him from his father's side. And from it, the mortgagee if he discharges the mortgagor from the debt, then the pledge perishes in the mortgagee's hand, he is liable. And from it, the one to whom salam is given if he gifts the capital, which is an 'ard, to the rabb al-salam, then they rescind the salam, the muslim ilayh does not owe anything by istihsan; by qiyas he must pay its value, which is the view of Zufar. Thus in al-Muhit. There is an objection to this principle, i.e., that difference in cause is not considered when the objective is achieved: what is mentioned in al-Tabyin from the chapter of Tahlif: if one says 'you sold me this female slave' and the other denies saying 'I did not sell her, rather I married her to you', it is not permissible for him to have intercourse with her due to difference in ruling, for the ruling of right hand possession is different from the ruling of marriage. But it could be said that this is not of the type where the objective is achieved, because the objectives are different. It should be included under the mentioned principle if one acknowledges to him a thousand as price of goods, and the acknowledged says 'usurpation'. al-Zayla'i said from the chapter of Tahlif: he is ordered to pay him because of unity of ruling. In Talkhis al-Jami' from the chapter of Iqrar: he said: 'You deposited this thousand with me', and the other said 'rather, I have a loan of a thousand against you', he takes it because the return of the specific thing is different from debt unless they agree, because the acknowledger is like a beginner. And if he said 'I lent it to you', he takes the thousand because the conflict is about its removal. And if he said 'you usurped', he takes a thousand because its cause is liability, so they agree on the debt and differ on the cause, which is disregarded. Similarly if he acknowledged a loan and he claims the price. In al-Mi'raj: if it is said that this obliges that if one buys a slave for a thousand, then the seller reduces a tenth of the price, then he finds a defect that reduces a tenth of the price, he takes back for the defect despite having obtained this by reduction; we say: the effect of the defect is to drop part of the price, and this is not obtained by reduction because the reduced amount is no longer part of the price. The second issue: if she received half then gifted all that was received and other (the remaining half), then he divorced her before consummation: none of them takes back anything from the other according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: he takes back half of what she received, considering the part like the whole, because the reduction attaches to the original contract. And he (Abu Hanifa) says: his objective is the safety of half through divorce, which has been achieved, and reduction does not attach to the original contract in marriage like increase. Therefore, increase is not halved with the original, unanimously. Thus in al-Hidaya, Ghayat al-Bayan, al-Tabyin, and many books. And al-Fath al-Qadir questioned it saying that the attachment...
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage is an extended expansion on the matn rule regarding the wife's gift of the mahr and subsequent divorce before consummation. It opens with the sub-case where the wife received the entire thousand dirham mahr and then gifted it back; the husband still recovers half because the gift did not transfer the specific money he was entitled to reclaim. The commentator explains the Hanafi principle that dirhams and dinars are not determined in contracts, so the husband is only entitled to the like, not the specific coins. He then cites al-Walwalji's fatwa on zakat for such a wife, showing she must pay zakat on the full amount because she owes the like. The text then returns to the matn phrase about the exception (when she does not receive or only receives half and gifts all), elaborating that the exception is explained through three sub-issues. The first sub-issue is detailed: if she never received any mahr and gifts it all, the husband does not recover anything by istihsan, even though qiyas (the view of Zufar) would require return of half. The Hanafi istihsan reasoning is that the husband has already received what he would have been entitled to—the release of his liability for half the mahr—through the gift. Difference in cause (gift vs. divorce) is irrelevant when the objective is achieved. The passage then lists several legal analogies supporting this istihsan principle, including cases of usurpation, fasid sale, gift from a sick person, mortgage, and salam. It also notes an objection from al-Tabyin regarding cases where the objective differs (like sale vs. marriage), and provides responses. The second sub-issue appears at the end: when she receives half the mahr and then gifts everything (both received half and the remaining half), Abu Hanifa says no return, while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he recovers half of what she received. The Hanafi position is that reduction (hatt) does not attach to the original marriage contract unlike increase, so the husband's objective (securing half without return) is achieved. The passage ends with a reference to a criticism from Fath al-Qadir, which is cut off.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling due to a stronger evidence or custom.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction; applying the ruling of an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause.
عين ('ayn): Specific thing; as opposed to dayn (debt). Here, dirhams are not considered 'ayn (specific coins) but as debt.
زفر (Zufar): Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, a major Hanafi disciple known for strict adherence to qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first sub-issue, if the wife has not received any mahr and then gifts the entire mahr to the husband, what is the ruling according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) The husband recovers half of the mahr by qiyas.
B) The husband recovers nothing by istihsan.
C) The wife must return the full mahr.
D) The husband can choose to either recover half or nothing.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when the wife gifts the entire mahr before receipt and is divorced before consummation, the husband recovers nothing by istihsan because his objective (release from half) is achieved, overriding the qiyas.

Nikah — Marriage

Attachment of Increase in Mahr to the Contract
Reconciling Hanafi texts on mahr increase attachment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on whether an increase in mahr attaches to the original contract and distinguish its effect on validity versus halving upon divorce.

Core Idea
Increase in mahr attaches to the contract to validate it, but does not attach for the purpose of halving upon divorce.

The Hanafi school teaches that an increase in mahr made after the marriage contract is valid, but there is an apparent contradiction in earlier texts: sometimes the increase is said to attach to the contract, sometimes not. This lesson, based on Ibn Nujaym's commentary, shows that the attachment is partial: it secures the validity of the increase, but does not affect the husband's right to recover half the original mahr upon divorce before consummation. Understanding this nuance prevents misinterpretation of the school's position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Apparent Contradiction
Note that earlier Hanafi scholars stated both that the increase does not attach to the contract (so it's a separate gift) and that it does attach (to validate it). Determine the two contexts in which each statement was made.
The contradiction arises because the statements were made in different contexts: one for halving, one for validity.
2
Understand the Reason for Attachment
Attachment is necessary to prevent the increase from being an invalid exchange of ownership for ownership (māl bi-māl). The text that validates the increase requires that it be considered part of the contract for this purpose.
Without attachment, the increase would be void as a sale of money for money, which is prohibited.
3
Understand the Reason for Non-Attachment
When it comes to halving the mahr upon divorce before consummation, the increase does not attach. Halving (intisāf) is only for the original mahr named at the time of contract. The husband's right to half is preserved by excluding the increase.
The increase is a voluntary gift; it is not subject to the rules of the original mahr.
4
Distinguish the Two Contexts
The increase attaches for validity but not for division. This is a legal construction (ta'līl) based on necessity (istiḥsān) and practicality, not a contradiction. The school acts in each situation according to what is appropriate.
The principle is: attachment is from one aspect only, not absolute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الزيادة بأصل العقد هو الدافع لقول المانعين لها لو صحت كان ملكه عوضاً عن ملكه فإذا لم تلتحق بقي إبطالهم بلا جواب فالحق أنها تلتحق كما يعطيه كلام غير واحد من المشايخ، وإنما لا تتنصف لأن الانتصاف خاص بالمفوض في نفس العقد حقيقة كما قدمناه ا هـ . وحاصله أنه تناقض كلامهم فصرحوا هنا بعدم الالتحاق وفي مسألة زيادة المهر بالالتحاق فرجح المحقق ما صرحوا به في المسألة السابقة وأبطل كلامهم هنا. والحق أن كلامهم في الموضعين صحيح لأن قولهم هناك بالالتحاق إنما هو من وجه دون وجه لتصريحهم بأنها لو حطت من المهر حتى صار الباقي أقل من عشرة فإنه لا يضر، ولو التحق الحط بأصل العقد من كل وجه للزم تكميلها ولوجب مهر المثل لو حطت الكل كأنه لم يسم شيئاً، وقولهم هنا بعدمه إنما هو من وجه دون وجه عملاً في كل موضع بما يناسبه فروعي جانب الالتحاق لتصحيح الزيادة حتى لا يكون ملكه عوضاً عن ملكه للنص المفيد لصحتها كما أسلفناه، وروعي جانب عدمه هنا لأنه لا داعي إليه لأن المقصود سلامة النصف للزوج وقد حصل فلا ضرورة إلى القول بالالتحاق الذي هو خلاف الأصل لأنه مغير للعقد والله الموفق للصواب.
The increase at the root of the contract repels the statement of those who prevent it, because if it were valid, his ownership would be a substitute for his ownership. And if it does not attach, their invalidation remains unanswered. So the truth is that it attaches, as supported by the words of more than one of the mashayikh. And it is only not halved because halving is specific to the delegated (mufawwid) in the contract itself, as we have mentioned earlier. Its summary: Their words contradict: here they stated non-attachment, and in the issue of increase of mahr they stated attachment. So the muhaqqiq preferred what they stated in the previous issue and invalidated their words here. But the truth is that their words in both places are correct: because their statement there of attachment is only from one aspect not another, as they explicitly stated that if she reduces the mahr until the remaining is less than ten, that does not harm. And if the reduction attached to the root of the contract from every aspect, it would necessitate completing it, and mahr al-mithl would become obligatory if she reduced all, as if she did not name anything. And their statement here of non-attachment is only from one aspect not another, acting in every place according to what is appropriate. So the aspect of attachment was considered to validate the increase so that his ownership is not a substitute for his ownership, due to the text that indicates its validity as we have stated above. And the aspect of non-attachment was considered here because there is no need for it, since the purpose is the safety of half for the husband and that has been achieved. So there is no need for the statement of attachment, which is contrary to the principle, because it alters the contract. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the ruling of increase in mahr (ziyada) and whether it attaches to the original contract. The author, Ibn Nujaym, resolves an apparent contradiction in the statements of earlier Hanafi scholars. On one hand, they said the increase does not attach to the contract (so it is a separate gift). On the other, in the context of validating the increase, they said it does attach. The author harmonizes: the increase attaches to the contract for the purpose of validity (so that it is not an exchange of ownership for ownership, which is invalid), but it does not attach when it comes to the division of mahr upon divorce before consummation. The reason: halving of mahr is only applicable to what was originally specified in the contract. The increase, being a later addition, is not subject to halving. Thus, the principle is contextual: attachment is used to validate, non-attachment used to preserve the husband's half. This is a nuanced ruling based on istihsan and practical necessity.

Key Terms
الزيادة بأصل العقد (al-ziyādatu bi-aṣli al-ʿaqd): An addition to the mahr agreed upon at the time of contract, made by one party and accepted by the other.
الانتصاف (al-intiṣāf): The right of the husband to recover half the mahr when divorce occurs before consummation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the increase in mahr not subject to halving when divorce occurs before consummation?
A) Because the increase was not specified at the time of contract.
B) Because halving is only for what was originally named in the contract.
C) Because the wife already received the increase.
D) Because the husband renounced his right.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that an increase in mahr attaches to the contract for validity but not for the purpose of halving upon divorce; context determines the extent of attachment.

Wife Gifts Mahr and Divorced Before Consummation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr gift scenarios.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Abu Hanifa's ruling on how much of the mahr the husband can recover when the wife gifts part of the mahr before divorce, and distinguish the Sahibayn's position.

Core Idea
A gift of mahr before receipt cancels the husband's right to half; receipt changes the calculation.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a wife gives her mahr (dowry) as a gift to her husband before consummation, and then the husband divorces her, a dispute arises over how much he can recover. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, differ on whether the gift nullifies his right to half the mahr. This lesson unpacks the three scenarios detailed in Al-Bahr al-Raiq, focusing on the role of receipt (qabd).

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
The husband has a wajib right to half the mahr upon divorce before consummation. The wife may gift all or part of the mahr to him. The question: does the gift eliminate or reduce his recovery right?
The gift is a voluntary transfer of ownership.
2
Scenario 1: Gift before any receipt
If the wife gifts the entire mahr (or half) before receiving anything, Abu Hanifa holds that the husband recovers nothing. The Sahibayn disagree: they say he recovers half of what she would have received (i.e., half of the mahr).
The text says 'cinda' (Abu Hanifa) vs. 'khilafan lahuma' (contrary to the two).
3
Scenario 2: Receipt of more than half, then gift of the excess
If she receives 600 of 1000 dirhams and gifts 400, she still has 200 in hand. Abu Hanifa says she returns the excess over half (100). The Sahibayn say she returns half of what she received (300).
The text gives the example of 600 received, 400 gifted: return 100 vs. 300.
4
Scenario 3: Receipt of less than half
If she receives less than half (e.g., 200) and gifts the remainder (800 in liability), Abu Hanifa says the husband can recover to complete his half (i.e., 300). This is understood by 'greater reason' (awla).
The text says 'ma'lum bi al-awla'.
5
Apply to unspecified fungibles
The same ruling applies to mithli ghayr mu'ayyan (fungible goods like grain) as to cash.
This extends the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله ووهبت الألف عائد إلى المسألتين مع أن هبة الألف ليس بقيد في الثانية لأنها لو وهبت النصف الذي في ذمته فالحكم كذلك أنه لا من رجوع له عليها عنده خلافاً لهما. وقيد بقبض النصف للاحتراز عما إذا قبضت أكثر من النصف ووهبت الباقي فإنها ترد عليه ما زاد على النصف عنده كما لو قبضت ستمائة ووهبت أربعمائة فإنه يرجع بمائة. وعندهما يرجع بنصف المقبوض فترد ثلثمائة كما في غاية البيان. ولو وهبته مائتين رجع بثلاث مائة تتميماً للنصف كما في النهاية، وأما إذا قبضت أقل من النصف ووهبت الباقي فهو معلوم بالأولى فعلم أن التقييد بالنصف للاحتراز عن الأكثر لا عن الأقل، وحكم المثلى الغير المعين حكم النقد هنا أيضاً.
And his statement: 'and she gifted the thousand' refers to both issues, although the gift of the thousand is not a condition in the second, because if she gifted half of what was in her liability, the ruling is the same: that he has no recourse against her according to him (Abu Hanifa), contrary to them (the two companions). And it is restricted by 'receipt of half' to avoid the case where she receives more than half and gifts the remainder: then she returns to him what exceeds half according to him, as if she received six hundred and gifted four hundred, then he recovers one hundred. According to them, he recovers half of what was received, so she returns three hundred, as in Ghayat al-Bayan. And if she gifted him two hundred, he recovers three hundred to complete the half, as in al-Nihaya. As for when she receives less than half and gifts the remainder, it is known by greater reason. So it is understood that the restriction to half is to avoid the greater, not the lesser. And the ruling of unspecified fungible goods (mithli ghayr mu'ayyan) is also like cash here.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling when a wife gifts the mahr (cash) to her husband before consummation and then he divorces her. The key dispute: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, if she gifts the entire mahr (or half) and has not received it yet, the husband has no right to recover anything because the gift effectively transfers ownership. However, if she has already received part of the mahr and then gifts it, different rules apply: if she received more than half and gifted the excess, she must return the excess to the husband. If she received less than half and gifted, the husband can still recover to complete his half. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the husband always recovers half of what the wife actually received, regardless of what she gifted. The text also notes that the same ruling applies to unspecified fungible goods (mithli ghayr mu'ayyan) as to cash.

Key Terms
وهبت الألف (wahabat al-alf): The wife gifted the thousand (i.e., the entire mahr of one thousand dirhams) to the husband.
عنده (ʿindahu): According to Imam Abu Hanifa.
خلافاً لهما (khilāfan lahumā): Contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a wife receives 800 dirhams of a 1000 dirham mahr and then gifts 600 dirhams to her husband, how much must she return after divorce before consummation?
A) 300 dirhams
B) 200 dirhams
C) 400 dirhams
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The husband's right to half the mahr can be modified by the wife's gift, but receipt of part changes the amount recoverable.

Wife Gifts Goods Mahr Then Divorced Before Consummation
Ruling when mahr is a specific commodity and wife gifts it to husband before divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a wife gifts the mahr (a specific commodity) to her husband and then is divorced before consummation, and identify the exceptions when the husband has recourse.

Core Idea
If the wife gifts the specific mahr to the husband, he keeps it all—unless the mahr was defective or the transaction was a sale, not a gift.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on a core ruling of 'mahr' in Hanafi fiqh. When the mahr is a specific commodity and the wife gifts it to the husband before divorce, the general rule is that the husband has no claim. However, several nuanced exceptions arise, such as when the commodity had a major defect, when the wife sold it instead of gifting, or when a third party intervened. Understanding these exceptions is essential for properly applying the law.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling
Identify the core rule: when the wife gifts the specific mahr to the husband, he receives his exact right, so if he divorces her, he has no recourse.
This applies whether the gift occurred before or after she took possession.
2
Identify the first exception: major defect
If the commodity had a major defect at the time of gift, the gift is considered to be of a different object. The husband can claim half its value on the day she received it.
Minor defects are tolerated and do not trigger this exception.
3
Identify the second exception: sale instead of gift
If the wife sells the mahr to the husband and then he divorces, he does have recourse for half—whether half the value or half the price paid (the author leans toward value).
The distinction between gift and sale is crucial.
4
Identify the third exception: gift via a third party
If she gifts the commodity to a stranger, who then gifts it to the husband, the husband can claim half from the wife because the half did not come directly from her.
This applies whether the mahr is a specific object or a debt.
5
Analyze the special nature of mahr in marriage
In marriage, a commodity is treated as a liability (thiqqa) because wealth is not the main purpose; thus tolerance is allowed, unlike in sales.
This explains why a commodity can be owed as mahr even without specification in some cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثالثة لو كان المهر عرضاً فوهبته له ثم طلقها قبله فإنه لا رجوع له بشيء عليها، سواء كانت الهبة قبل القبض أو بعده، لأنه وصل إليه عين حقه لتعينه في الفسخ كتعينه في العقد، ولهذا لم يكن لكل واحد منهما دفع شيء آخر . وأشار بقوله «العرض «المهر إلى أنه لم يتعيب لأنها لو وهبته له بعدما تعيب بعيب فاحش ثم طلقها قبله فإنه يرجع عليها بنصف قيمة العرض يوم قبضت لأنه لما تعيب فاحشاً صار كأنها وهبته عيناً أخرى غير المهر كما في التبيين. وظاهره أن العيب اليسير كالعدم لما سيأتي أن العيب اليسير في المهر متحمل. وأطلق في العرض فشمل المعين وما في الذمة بخلاف المثليات فإن ما في الذمة منها ليس حكمه كالعرض والمعين منها كالعرض وهو من خصوص النكاح فإن العرض فيه يثبت في الذمة لأن المال فيه ليس بمقصود فيجري فيه التسامح بخلاف البيع، وتمثيلهم هنا له بالحيوان المراد به هنا الفرس والحمار ونحوهما لا مطلق الحيوان فإن التسمية تفسد كما سيأتي . وقيد بالهبة لأنها لو باعت عرض الصداق من الزوج ثم طلقها قبله فإنه يرجع عليها بالنصف. كذا في غاية البيان ولم يبين أنه يرجع عليها بنصف قيمته أو بنصف الثمن المدفوع، والظاهر الأول . وقيد بهبة المرأة للزوج لأنها لو وهبت العرض لأجنبي بعد قبضه ثم وهبه الأجنبي من الزوج . ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بها رجع عليها بنصف الصداق، العين والدين في ذلك سواء، لأنه لم يسلم له النصف من جهتها. كذا في المبسوط . وقيد بهبة جميع العرض لأنها لو وهبت له أقل من النصف وقبضت الباقي فإنها ترد ما زاد على النصف، ولووهبت له أكثره أو النصف فلا رجوع له. ومما يناسب مسألة هبة المرأة العرض المهر ما في الظهيرية : لو وهبت المرأة العين الممهورة للزوج ثم استحقت فإنها نرجع عليها بقيمتها ا هـ. لأنه بالاستحقاق بطلت الهبة وقد تزوجها على عين مملوكة لغيره، وقد ظهر لي هنا أن هذه المسألة أعني ما إذا طلقها قبل الدخول بعدما وهبته على ستين وجهاً لأن المهر إما ذهب أو فضة أو مثلي غيرهما أو قيمي؛ فالأول على عشرين وجهاً لأن الموهوب إما الكل أو النصف، وكل منهما إما أن يكون قبل القبض أو بعد القبض أو بعد قبض النصف أو أقل منه أو أكثر منه فهي عشرة، وكل منها إما أن يكون مضروباً أو تبراً فهي عشرون والعشرة الأولى في المثلي، وكل منها إما أن يكون معيناً أو لا، وكذا في القيمي، والأحكام مذكورة فليتأمل .
The third issue: If the mahr is a commodity ('ard) and she gifts it to him, then he divorces her before consummation, then he has no recourse against her for anything, whether the gift was before or after receipt, because he received the very object of his right, as it is determined in dissolution just as it is determined in contract. Therefore, neither of them can give something else. And by his saying 'the commodity mahr' he indicated that it is not defective, because if she gifted it to him after it became defective with a major defect, then he divorces her before consummation, he would have recourse against her for half the value of the commodity on the day she received it, because when it became severely defective, it is as if she gifted him a different object than the mahr, as in al-Tabyin. Its apparent meaning is that a minor defect is like none, because it will come that minor defect in mahr is tolerated. And he dealt absolutely with 'commodity' so it includes what is determined and what is in liability, unlike fungibles (mithliyyat), for what is in liability of them is not like a commodity, and what is determined of them is like a commodity. This is specific to marriage: because the commodity is established in liability in marriage since wealth is not the objective, so tolerance is allowed, unlike sale. Their example here of livestock means specifically horse, donkey, and the like, not absolute livestock, because naming (an unspecified animal) invalidates, as will come. And he restricted by 'gift' because if she sold the commodity of the sadaq to the husband and then he divorces her before consummation, he would have recourse against her for half. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan, but it did not clarify whether he recovers half its value or half the price paid; the apparent is the former. And restricted by the wife's gift to the husband, because if she gifted the commodity to a stranger after receipt, then the stranger gifted it to the husband, then he divorces her before consummation, he has recourse against her for half of the sadaq, whether it is a specific object or a debt, because the half did not reach him from her. Thus in al-Mabsut. And restricted by gift of the entire commodity, because if she gifted him less than half and received the rest, she returns what exceeds half; if she gifted him more than half or exactly half, he has no recourse. And related to the issue of the wife gifting the commodity mahr is what is in al-Zahiriyyah: If the wife gifted the specific object that was the mahr to the husband, then it was claimed by a rightful owner, she (the wife) has recourse against him for its value. Because the gift became void by the claim, and she married him on an object owned by someone else. And it has become clear to me here that this issue, i.e., if he divorces her before consummation after she gifted, has sixty aspects: because the mahr is either gold, silver, other fungible, or non-fungible; the first has twenty aspects because the gifted object is either all or half, and each of these is before or after receipt, or after receipt of half or less or more, making ten, and each of these is either minted or bullion, making twenty. The first ten apply to fungibles, and each of those is either determined or not, similarly for non-fungibles. The rulings are mentioned, so let one reflect.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling when the mahr is a specific commodity (like a horse or cloth) and the wife gifts it to the husband before consummation, then he divorces her. The general rule: the husband has no claim because he literally received his own property. However, several qualifications arise: (1) If the commodity had a major defect when gifted, the gift is essentially of a different object, so the husband can claim half the value. (2) If she sells the commodity to him instead of gifting, he does have claim to half because sale is different from gift. (3) If she gifts to a third party who then gifts to husband, the husband can claim half from her because the half did not come from her. (4) If she gifts only part, the rules of excess apply. The author also notes that in marriage, even a commodity is treated as a liability (dhimma) because wealth is not the main objective, so tolerance applies. He then mentions that this issue can be analyzed into sixty possible scenarios depending on the nature of the mahr (gold, silver, fungible, non-fungible) and the timing and extent of the gift. This demonstrates the depth of Hanafi legal analysis.

Key Terms
العرض (al-ʿaraḍ): A specific commodity, as opposed to cash or fungibles.
العيب الفاحش (al-ʿayb al-fāḥish): A major defect that significantly reduces value, such that the object is considered different.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Husband recovers nothing.
B) Husband recovers half the value of the horse on the day she received it.
C) Husband recovers half the mahr in cash.
D) The gift is void, and she must return the horse.

Key Takeaway
The gift of a specific mahr to the husband before divorce generally bars his claim, but exceptions arise when the mahr is defective or the transfer is not a pure gift.
