Marriage with Conditions: Effect on Mahr
Ruling on marriage conditions and mahr obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a marriage condition benefiting the wife affects the mahr obligation, distinguishing between fulfilled and violated conditions.

Core Idea
A marriage condition benefiting the wife is valid; if violated, mahr al-mithl replaces the named mahr.

Marriage contracts often include stipulations, such as not traveling or not taking a second wife. This lesson examines how Hanafi fiqh treats these conditions: they are enforceable and directly impact the mahr amount. Understanding this ruling is crucial for properly advising on marriage contracts and resolving mahr disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its beneficiary
First, determine what condition was stipulated (e.g., not moving, not marrying another) and who benefits from it (the wife, her father, or a mahram relative).
Only conditions providing a benefit are considered; frivolous conditions are treated differently.
2
Determine if the condition is fulfilled
Check whether the husband adhered to the condition. If he did, the named mahr is due; if he violated it, the wife's consent to the named mahr is no longer valid.
The condition must be a real benefit; if it becomes impossible, the same ruling applies.
3
State the mahr outcome
If the husband fulfills the condition, the wife receives the named mahr (the amount agreed). If he violates it, she receives mahr al-mithl (the mahr of a woman similar to her).
Mahr al-mithl is determined by factors like age, beauty, wealth, and family status.
4
Note the scope and examples
The principle applies to conditions like not taking the wife out of the city, not marrying another, or not burdening her with hard labor. It also covers benefits stipulated for her father or mahram.
The condition must be a benefit for the wife or her close relatives; conditions harming her are invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو نكحها بألف على أن لا يخرجها أو على أن لا يتزوج عليها أو على ألف إن أقام بها وعلى ألفين إن أخرجها فإن وفي وأقام فلها الألف وإلا فمهر المثل) بيان لمسألتين : الأولى ضابطها أن لها قدراً ومهراً مثلها أكثر منه ويشترط منفعة لها أو لأبيها أو لذي - رحم محرم منها، فإن وفى بما شرط فلها المسمى لأنه صلح مهراً وقد تم رضاها به وإلا فمهر المثل لأنه . سمى مالها فيه نفع، فعند فواته ينعدم رضاها بالمسمي فيكمل مهر مثلها كما إذا شرط أنه لا يخرجها من البلد أو لا يتزوج عليها أو أن يكرمها ولا يكلفها الأعمال الشاقة أو
His statement: (And if he marries her for a thousand on condition that he does not take her out, or that he does not marry another woman, or for a thousand if he stays with her and two thousand if he takes her out; then if he fulfills and stays, she has the thousand; otherwise, she has mahr al-mithl.) This is an explanation of two issues. The first: its principle is that she has an amount and her mahr al-mithl is more than it, and he stipulates a benefit for her or her father or a mahram relative. If he fulfills what he stipulated, she has the named (mahr) because it is valid as mahr and her consent is complete; otherwise, she has mahr al-mithl because he named something in which there is a benefit for her, so when that benefit is lost, her consent to the named amount ceases, so her mahr al-mithl is completed, such as when he stipulates that he will not take her out of the city, or that he will not marry another woman, or that he will honor her and not burden her with hard labor.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on marriage contracts that include conditions related to the husband's conduct, such as not moving her, not marrying another, or tying the mahr amount to where they live. The key principle: if the husband fulfills the condition, the wife receives the named mahr. If he violates the condition, she receives mahr al-mithl (the mahr of her peers). This is because her consent to the named mahr was conditional on receiving the stipulated benefit. When the benefit is lost, her consent is no longer valid, so the mahr defaults to what is fair. Examples include conditions of not taking her out of the city, not taking a co-wife, or treating her well. The ruling also applies if the benefit is stipulated for her father or a mahram. This shows that conditions in marriage can affect the mahr obligation.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The mahr of a woman similar to the bride in age, beauty, wealth, family, etc., used when the named mahr is invalid or consent is lost.
شرط منفعة (sharṭ manfaʿa): A condition that provides a benefit to the wife or her family, like not traveling or not marrying another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man marries a woman with the condition that he will not take a second wife, but later he does, what mahr is she entitled to?
A) The named mahr only.
B) Mahr al-mithl only.
C) The named mahr plus compensation.
D) There is no effect on mahr.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a marriage condition benefiting the wife is enforceable; violation triggers mahr al-mithl.

Condition of Benefit in Mahr: When the Specified Dower Is Contingent on a Promise
Expansion on the ruling of benefit conditions in mahr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage contracts with benefit conditions and determine when mahr al-mithl becomes due instead of the specified dower.

Core Idea
A stipulated benefit conditions the wife's consent; if unfulfilled, the specified dower is void and mahr al-mithl is due.

Marriage contracts often include conditions that benefit the wife, such as not moving her or not marrying another. The Hanafi school treats these conditions as integral to the wife's consent to the specified dower. In this lesson, we examine the detailed rulings from Al-Bahr al-Ra’iq on how such conditions affect the dower amount when the husband fails to fulfill them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its benefit
Look for a condition in the marriage contract that provides a benefit to the wife, such as not moving her out of town, not marrying another, or giving a gift. The benefit must be permissible and definite.
Conditions harming the wife do not affect the dower.
2
Check if the condition is a valid benefit
The benefit must be legally permissible (e.g., not wine or pork) and expressed as a promise (future tense) if it involves freeing or divorce. If expressed as a verbal noun, the action is binding immediately.
Ambiguous benefits like 'honor' or unspecified gifts are not enforceable per the preferred view.
3
Determine fulfillment or breach
If the husband fulfills the condition, the specified dower is valid. If he breaches, the wife's consent to the specified amount is nullified.
Breach triggers the obligation of mahr al-mithl.
4
Apply the rule: specify dower or mahr al-mithl
If the condition is unfulfilled and her mahr al-mithl is greater than the specified dower, she receives mahr al-mithl. If the specified dower equals or exceeds mahr al-mithl, she receives only the specified amount.
The condition must be solely for her benefit (not a third party) to affect the dower.

قوله : (ولو نكحها بألف على أن لا يخرجها أو على أن لا يتزوج عليها أو على ألف إن أقام بها وعلى ألفين إن أخرجها فإن وفي وأقام فلها الألف وإلا فمهر المثل) بيان لمسألتين : الأولى ضابطها أن لها قدراً ومهراً مثلها أكثر منه ويشترط منفعة لها أو لأبيها أو لذي - رحم محرم منها، فإن وفى بما شرط فلها المسمى لأنه صلح مهراً وقد تم رضاها به وإلا فمهر المثل لأنه سمى مالها فيه نفع، فعند فواته ينعدم رضاها بالمسمي أزوجك أمتي الأخرى ففعل طلقت رجعية شيء له إن لم يزوجه لأن البضع عند خروجه لا قيمة له كما في المحيط. قيد بكون المنفعة المشروطة لها لأنه لو شرط مع المسمى منفعة لأجنبي ولم يوف فليس لها إلا المسمى، لأنها لو كان مثل مهر المثل أو أكثر منه ولم يوف بما وعد فليس لها إلا المسمى كذا في غاية البيان. وأشار بما ذكره إلى أن المنفعة المشروطة لها مما يباح لها الانتفاع به لأنه لو شرط لها ومع المسمى ما لا يباح الانتفاع به شرعاً كالخمر والخنزير، فإن كان المسمى عشرة فصاعداً وجب لها وبطل الحرام ولا يكمل مهر المثل لأن المسلم لا ينتفع بالحرام فلا يجب عوض بفواته . كذا في غاية البيان . ثم اعلم أن صاحب الهداية ذكر أن هذه المسألة أعني مسألة شرط المنفعة مع المسمى ما إذا شرط الكرامة والهدية مع الألف، فظاهره أنه إن وفى فلها المسمى وإلا فلها مهر المثل كما صرح به في غاية البيان في مسألة ما إذا ظهر أحد العبدين حراً مع أن الهدية والكرامة مجهولتان ولا يمكن الوفاء بالمجهول، والظاهر أنها ليست داخلة في هذه المسألة.
His saying: (If he marries her for one thousand on condition that he does not take her out, or that he does not marry another, or for one thousand if he stays with her and two thousand if he takes her out, then if he fulfills and stays, she gets the one thousand; otherwise, mahr al-mithl.) An explanation of two issues: The first is that its principle is that she is given a specified amount and her mahr al-mithl is more than that, and a benefit is stipulated for her or for her father or for a mahram relative of hers. If he fulfills what he stipulated, then she gets the named dower because it was a dower and her consent to it was complete. Otherwise, she gets mahr al-mithl because he named something in which she had no benefit, so when it is lost, her consent to the named amount is nullified, and he completes her mahr al-mithl, as if he stipulated that he would not take her out of the city, or not marry another, or that he would honor her and not burden her with hard work, or if he takes her out, then if he fulfills and stays, she gets the one thousand; otherwise, mahr al-mithl. And if he marries her for this slave or that he gives her a gift, or that he divorces her co-wife, or that he frees her brother, or that he marries her father's daughter. He explained in al-Muhit that she benefits from what is for her brother and her son, so it becomes like a stipulated benefit for her. It is necessary that it be in the future tense form regarding freeing and divorce so that it is a promise; if he fulfills it, fine; otherwise, he is not obliged to free or divorce, and he completes for her mahr al-mithl. But if he stipulates it with a verbal noun, as if he marries her for one thousand and the freeing of her brother or the divorce of her co-wife, then the brother is freed and the woman is divorced by the contract itself, and it is not dependent on his executing them, and the woman gets only the named dower. As for the wala of the brother: if the husband says 'and freeing her brother for her', then it is for her because she is the one freeing due to prior ownership, and the slave becomes part of the named dower. If the husband does not say 'for her', then he is the one freeing and the wala is for him. The divorce that occurred is revocable because it is exchanged for the vulva, which is not valuable; its valuation by contract is for the necessity of ownership, so it does not extend beyond that; thus it does not appear in the right of the divorce occurring on the co-wife, so it remains a divorce without compensation, so it is revocable, just as if the master of the married woman said to the husband: 'Divorce her on condition that I marry you to my other female slave', and he did so, she is divorced revocably if he does not marry her, because the vulva at the time of exit has no value, as in al-Muhit. It is restricted to the benefit being stipulated for her, because if he stipulated with the named dower a benefit for a third party and did not fulfill, she gets only the named dower, since it is not a benefit intended for either contract party. Similarly in al-Muhit, and it is not hidden that the ruling when he stipulates with the named dower something harmful to her, like marrying another, is that she gets only the named dower unconditionally, a fortiori. And we restricted it to her mahr al-mithl being greater than the named dower, because if the named dower is equal to or greater than mahr al-mithl and he does not fulfill his promise, she gets only the named dower, as in Ghayat al-Bayan. And he indicated by what he mentioned that the stipulated benefit for her is that which it is permissible for her to benefit from, because if he stipulates for her with the named dower something that is not legally permissible to benefit from, like wine or pigs, and the named dower is ten or more, then it becomes due to her and the unlawful is void, and mahr al-mithl is not completed, because a Muslim does not benefit from the unlawful, so no compensation is due for its loss. As in Ghayat al-Bayan. Then know that the author of al-Hidayah mentioned that this issue, meaning the issue of stipulating benefit with the named dower, applies when he stipulates honor and a gift with the one thousand. Its apparent meaning is that if he fulfills, she gets the named dower; otherwise, she gets mahr al-mithl, as is stated in Ghayat al-Bayan in the issue of when one of the two slaves appears to be free, even though the gift and honor are unknown and fulfillment of the unknown is impossible. The apparent view is that it is not included in this issue.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author explains the cases where a marriage contract is concluded with a specified dower (mahr musamma) along with a condition that benefits the wife. The key principle is: the wife's consent to the specified dower is contingent on the benefit. If the husband fulfills the condition, the specified dower is valid. If he fails, her consent is deemed incomplete, and she is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the dower of her peers), which is typically higher than the specified amount. The passage details various forms of such benefits: not moving her out of town, not marrying another, a gift, freeing her brother, etc. It also clarifies that the condition must be expressed in the future tense (mudari') to be a promise; if expressed as a verbal noun (masdar), the action is immediately binding. The passage also addresses the issue of wala' (patronage) when a slave is freed as part of the dower. Finally, it discusses the exception when the benefit is impermissible (like wine) or when the specified dower is already equal to or greater than mahr al-mithl. The author also notes a difference of opinion regarding whether a condition of 'honor' or 'gift' falls under this ruling, suggesting that the Hidayah may have included it but the preferred view excludes it due to ambiguity.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower equivalent to that of women similar to her in status (family, beauty, etc.)
المسمى (al-musamma): The dower explicitly named in the marriage contract
المنفعة (al-manfa'a): A benefit stipulated in the contract for the wife, such as not moving or gifts

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man marries a woman for 1000 dirhams on condition that he does not marry another wife, and later he marries another, what dower does the first wife receive?
A) 1000 dirhams
B) Mahr al-mithl
C) Nothing
D) Half of 1000 dirhams

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a stipulated benefit in the marriage contract conditions the wife's consent; if the benefit is a definite permissible benefit and the husband fails to fulfill it, she receives mahr al-mithl instead of the specified dower.

The Binding Promise of Benefit in the Dower: Promise vs Immediate Condition
Ruling with proof on stipulating benefits with dower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a promise (wa'd) in the future tense and an immediate condition (shart) in the infinitive, and state the resulting dower consequences in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
A promised benefit in the marriage contract binds the husband to fulfill it or pay mahr al-mithl.

In Hanafi marriage law, a man may stipulate a benefit for his wife beyond the specified dower, such as freeing her brother or divorcing her co-wife. The legal force of this stipulation depends on its wording: a future tense promise triggers a fallback dower if unfulfilled, while an infinitive condition takes effect immediately. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is stipulating a benefit in the marriage contract. The overall marriage is valid (sahih). The ruling: if the husband fulfills the promised benefit, she gets the specified dower; if not, she gets mahr al-mithl.
2
Classify the stipulation wording
Distinguish between future tense (wa'd) and infinitive (shart). Future tense: 'I will free your brother.' Infinitive: 'on condition of freeing your brother.' The former is a promise; the latter is an immediate condition.
Key distinction in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Apply the rule to indirect benefits
The passage extends the rule to indirect benefits like freeing her brother or divorcing her co-wife, using qiyas: she benefits from these actions, so they are like a direct benefit.
Qiyas khafi: the benefit is not direct but is still beneficial.
4
Trace the patronage and divorce sub-rulings
If the husband says 'freeing her brother from her,' the wife becomes the manumitter and the slave becomes part of the dower. If not, the husband is the manumitter. The divorce of the co-wife is revocable because it is not exchanged for property.
These are consequences of how the condition is worded.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) might void the condition entirely, but Hanafis treat it as a binding promise, leading to mahr al-mithl if broken.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن أخرجها فإن وفى وأقام فلها الألف وإلا فمهر المثل ولو نكحها على هذا العبد أو أن يهدي لها هدية أو أن يطلق ضرتها أو على أن يعتق أخاها أو على أن يزوج أباها ابنته. وعلله في المحيط بأنها تنتفع بما لأخيها وابنها فصارت كالمنفعة المشروطة لها ا هـ. ولا بد أن يكون بصيغة المضارع في العتق والطلاق ليكون وعداً إن وفى به فبها وإلا لا يلزمه الإعتاق والتطليق ويكمل لها مهر المثل، أما إذا شرطه بالمصدر كما إذا تزوجها على ألف. وعتق أخيها أو طلاق ضرتها عتق الأخ وطلقت المرأة بنفس النكاح ولا يتوقف على أن يوقعهما وللمرأة المسمى فقط. وأما ولاء الأخ فإن قال الزوج وعتق أخيها عنها فهو لها لأنها المعتقة لتقدم الملك لها ويصير العبد من جملة المهر المسمى وإن لم يقل الزوج عنها فهو المعتق والولاء له والطلاق الواقع رجعي لأنه قوبل بالبضع وهو ليس بمتقوم وتقومه بالعقد لضرورة التملك فلا يعدوها فلم يظهر في حق الطلاق الواقع على الضرة فبقي طلاقاً بغير بدل فكان رجعياً كما لو قال مولى المنكوحة للزوج طلقها على أن أزوجك أمتي الأخرى ففعل طلقت رجعية شيء له إن لم يزوجه لأن البضع عند خروجه لا قيمة له كما في المحيط. قيد بكون المنفعة المشروطة لها لأنه لو شرط مع المسمى منفعة لأجنبي ولم يوف فليس لها إلا المسمى، لأنها ليست بمنفعة مقصودة لأحد المتعاقدين. كذا في المحيط ولا يخفى أن حكم ما إذا شرط مع المسمى ما يضرها كالتزوج عليها أنه ليس لها إلا المسمى مطلقاً بالأولى. وقيدنا بأن يكون مهر مثلها أكثر من المسمى لأن المسمى لو كان مثل مهر المثل أو أكثر منه ولم يوف بما وعد فليس لها إلا المسمى كذا في غاية البيان. وأشار بما ذكره إلى أن المنفعة المشروطة لها مما يباح له الانتفاع به لأنه لو شرط لها ومع المسمى ما لا يباح الانتفاع به شرعاً كالخمر والخنزير، فإن كان المسمى عشرة فصاعداً وجب لها وبطل الحرام ولا يكمل مهر المثل لأن المسلم لا ينتفع بالحرام فلا يجب عوض بفواته . كذا في غاية البيان .
If he brings her out, then if he fulfills and executes, she gets the thousand, otherwise she gets mahr al-mithl. And if he marries her for this slave, or that he gives her a gift, or that he divorces her co-wife, or that he frees her brother, or that he marries her father's daughter to her. And it is necessary that it be in the future tense for freeing and divorce to be a promise; if he fulfills it, fine, otherwise he is not obliged to free or divorce, and she gets complete mahr al-mithl. As for the patronage of the brother, if the husband says 'and freeing her brother from her,' then it is for her because she is the one freeing due to prior ownership, and the slave becomes part of the specified dower; if the husband does not say 'from her,' then he is the one freeing and the patronage is his, and the divorce that occurs is revocable because it was exchanged for the vulva, which is not considered property, and its being considered property by the contract for necessity of ownership does not extend beyond it, so it does not appear regarding the divorce of the co-wife; thus it remains a divorce without compensation, so it is revocable, as if the master of the married woman said to the husband: 'Divorce her on condition that I marry you to my other slave-girl,' and he did so, she is divorced revocably, and something is for him if he does not marry him, because the vulva when it leaves has no value. This is in Ghayat al-Bayan.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with explanation on the topic of stipulating a benefit along with a specified dower in a marriage contract. The author begins by stating the general rule: If the husband fulfills the promised benefit, the wife receives the specified dower; otherwise, she is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the dower of a woman of her like). Examples include marrying her on condition of freeing a specific slave, giving a gift, divorcing her co-wife, freeing her brother, or marrying her father's daughter to her. The reasoning from al-Muhit is that she benefits indirectly from these actions (e.g., her brother's freedom helps her), so they are analogous to a directly stipulated benefit. The author then explains a key condition: For freeing and divorce, the promise must be stated in the future tense (e.g., 'I will free') to be a binding promise. If stated as an infinitive (e.g., 'on condition of freeing'), the action takes effect immediately upon the contract, and she gets only the specified dower. The discussion then covers the issue of patronage (wala') of the freed slave: if the husband says 'freeing her brother from her,' the wife becomes the manumitter and the slave becomes part of the specified dower; otherwise, the husband is the manumitter. The divorce of the co-wife is revocable because it is not compensated by property. The passage also clarifies exceptions: If the benefit is for a third party, or if the specified dower is equal to or greater than mahr al-mithl, or if the benefit is unlawful (like wine or pork), then she gets only the specified dower. The underlying principle is that the stipulated benefit must be permissible and beneficial to the wife.

Key Terms
منفعة مشروطة (manfa'ah mashrutah): A benefit stipulated in the marriage contract for the wife, enforceable as a promise.
وعد (wa'd): A promise, distinct from an immediate condition; in this context, a future tense statement that obliges fulfillment morally but legally triggers mahr al-mithl if broken.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower appropriate for a woman of her social standing, profession, and family.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man marries a woman on the condition that he will free her brother (future tense), but he does not free him, what mahr is she entitled to?
A) The specified dower
B) Mahr al-mithl
C) Nothing
D) Half the specified dower

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a promised benefit in the marriage contract is binding; failure to fulfill it entitles the wife to mahr al-mithl if the specified dower is less.

Exceptions and Conditions: Third Party, Mahr al-Mithl Threshold, Unlawful Benefits
Exception rules to the general promise-benefit ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify three exceptions to the general rule of mahr al-mithl for a broken promise: (1) benefit for a third party, (2) specified dower equal to or greater than mahr al-mithl, and (3) unlawful benefits.

Core Idea
A broken promise only triggers mahr al-mithl if the benefit is for the wife, permissible, and the specified dower is less.

The general rule that a broken promise of benefit entitles the wife to mahr al-mithl has three key exceptions. If the benefit is for a third party, if the specified dower already equals or exceeds mahr al-mithl, or if the promised benefit is unlawful, the wife receives only the specified dower. This lesson clarifies these exceptions with examples from the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first exception: benefit for a third party
If the husband promises a benefit for someone other than the wife (e.g., a gift to her father), and he fails to fulfill it, she gets only the specified dower. The reason: she does not directly benefit, so it is not a stipulated benefit for her.
Based on al-Muhit: 'ليست بمنفعة مقصودة لأحد المتعاقدين'
2
Identify the second exception: specified dower equal or greater than mahr al-mithl
If the specified dower is equal to or greater than her mahr al-mithl, she gets only the specified dower even if the promise is broken. The promise does not increase her entitlement beyond the higher specified dower.
From Ghayat al-Bayan: 'إذا كان المسمى مثل مهر المثل أو أكثر منه'
3
Identify the third exception: unlawful benefit
If the promised benefit is unlawful (e.g., wine or pork), it is void, and she gets the specified dower only. No compensation for the loss of an unlawful benefit.
Ghayat al-Bayan: 'المسلم لا ينتفع بالحرام'
4
Note the condition of harm
If the stipulation harms the wife (e.g., the husband marrying another woman), it is also not enforceable, and she gets only the specified dower.
The text says 'بالأولى' (a fortiori) that harmful stipulations are not binding.

إن أخرجها فإن وفى وأقام فلها الألف وإلا فمهر المثل ولو نكحها على هذا العبد أو أن يهدي لها هدية أو أن يطلق ضرتها أو على أن يعتق أخاها أو على أن يزوج أباها ابنته. وعلله في المحيط بأنها تنتفع بما لأخيها وابنها فصارت كالمنفعة المشروطة لها ا هـ. ولا بد أن يكون بصيغة المضارع في العتق والطلاق ليكون وعداً إن وفى به فبها وإلا لا يلزمه الإعتاق والتطليق ويكمل لها مهر المثل، أما إذا شرطه بالمصدر كما إذا تزوجها على ألف. وعتق أخيها أو طلاق ضرتها عتق الأخ وطلقت المرأة بنفس النكاح ولا يتوقف على أن يوقعهما وللمرأة المسمى فقط. وأما ولاء الأخ فإن قال الزوج وعتق أخيها عنها فهو لها لأنها المعتقة لتقدم الملك لها ويصير العبد من جملة المهر المسمى وإن لم يقل الزوج عنها فهو المعتق والولاء له والطلاق الواقع رجعي لأنه قوبل بالبضع وهو ليس بمتقوم وتقومه بالعقد لضرورة التملك فلا يعدوها فلم يظهر في حق الطلاق الواقع على الضرة فبقي طلاقاً بغير بدل فكان رجعياً كما لو قال مولى المنكوحة للزوج طلقها على أن أزوجك أمتي الأخرى ففعل طلقت رجعية شيء له إن لم يزوجه لأن البضع عند خروجه لا قيمة له كما في المحيط. قيد بكون المنفعة المشروطة لها لأنه لو شرط مع المسمى منفعة لأجنبي ولم يوف فليس لها إلا المسمى، لأنها ليست بمنفعة مقصودة لأحد المتعاقدين. كذا في المحيط ولا يخفى أن حكم ما إذا شرط مع المسمى ما يضرها كالتزوج عليها أنه ليس لها إلا المسمى مطلقاً بالأولى. وقيدنا بأن يكون مهر مثلها أكثر من المسمى لأن المسمى لو كان مثل مهر المثل أو أكثر منه ولم يوف بما وعد فليس لها إلا المسمى كذا في غاية البيان. وأشار بما ذكره إلى أن المنفعة المشروطة لها مما يباح له الانتفاع به لأنه لو شرط لها ومع المسمى ما لا يباح الانتفاع به شرعاً كالخمر والخنزير، فإن كان المسمى عشرة فصاعداً وجب لها وبطل الحرام ولا يكمل مهر المثل لأن المسلم لا ينتفع بالحرام فلا يجب عوض بفواته . كذا في غاية البيان .
If he brings her out, then if he fulfills and executes, she gets the thousand, otherwise she gets mahr al-mithl. And if he marries her for this slave, or that he gives her a gift, or that he divorces her co-wife, or that he frees her brother, or that he marries her father's daughter to her. And he explained in al-Muhit that she benefits from what belongs to her brother and her son, so it becomes like a stipulated benefit for her. And it is necessary that it be in the future tense for freeing and divorce to be a promise; if he fulfills it, fine, otherwise he is not obliged to free or divorce, and she gets complete mahr al-mithl. But if he stipulates it with the infinitive, as if he marries her for a thousand and freeing her brother or divorcing her co-wife, then the brother is freed and the woman is divorced by the marriage itself, not dependent on him performing them, and she gets only the specified dower. As for the patronage of the brother, if the husband says 'and freeing her brother from her,' then it is for her because she is the one freeing due to prior ownership, and the slave becomes part of the specified dower; if the husband does not say 'from her,' then he is the one freeing and the patronage is his, and the divorce that occurs is revocable because it was exchanged for the vulva, which is not considered property, and its being considered property by the contract for necessity of ownership does not extend beyond it, so it does not appear regarding the divorce of the co-wife; thus it remains a divorce without compensation, so it is revocable, as if the master of the married woman said to the husband: 'Divorce her on condition that I marry you to my other slave-girl,' and he did so, she is divorced revocably, and something is for him if he does not marry him, because the vulva when it leaves has no value. He restricted it to the benefit stipulated for her because if he stipulates with the specified dower a benefit for a third party and does not fulfill, she gets only the specified dower, as it is not a benefit intended for one of the contracting parties. This is in al-Muhit. And it is not hidden that the ruling if he stipulates with the specified dower something harmful to her, like marrying another over her, is that she gets only the specified dower absolutely, a fortiori. And we restricted it to when her mahr al-mithl is more than the specified dower, because if the specified dower is like mahr al-mithl or more and he does not fulfill what he promised, she gets only the specified dower. This is in Ghayat al-Bayan. And what he mentioned indicates that the benefit stipulated for her must be permissible for her to benefit from, because if he stipulates for her with the specified dower something not permissible to benefit from legally, like wine and pork, if the specified dower is ten or more, it is obliged to her and the unlawful is void, and mahr al-mithl is not completed because the Muslim does not benefit from the unlawful, so no compensation is obliged for its loss. This is in Ghayat al-Bayan.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with explanation on the topic of stipulating a benefit along with a specified dower in a marriage contract. The author begins by stating the general rule: If the husband fulfills the promised benefit, the wife receives the specified dower; otherwise, she is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the dower of a woman of her like). Examples include marrying her on condition of freeing a specific slave, giving a gift, divorcing her co-wife, freeing her brother, or marrying her father's daughter to her. The reasoning from al-Muhit is that she benefits indirectly from these actions (e.g., her brother's freedom helps her), so they are analogous to a directly stipulated benefit. The author then explains a key condition: For freeing and divorce, the promise must be stated in the future tense (e.g., 'I will free') to be a binding promise. If stated as an infinitive (e.g., 'on condition of freeing'), the action takes effect immediately upon the contract, and she gets only the specified dower. The discussion then covers the issue of patronage (wala') of the freed slave: if the husband says 'freeing her brother from her,' the wife becomes the manumitter and the slave becomes part of the specified dower; otherwise, the husband is the manumitter. The divorce of the co-wife is revocable because it is not compensated by property. The passage also clarifies exceptions: If the benefit is for a third party, or if the specified dower is equal to or greater than mahr al-mithl, or if the benefit is unlawful (like wine or pork), then she gets only the specified dower. The underlying principle is that the stipulated benefit must be permissible and beneficial to the wife.

Key Terms
منفعة مشروطة (manfa'ah mashrutah): A benefit stipulated in the marriage contract for the wife, enforceable as a promise.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower appropriate for a woman of her social standing, profession, and family.
منفعة محرمة (manfa'ah muharramah): An unlawful benefit, such as wine or pork, which is void and not compensable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man promises his wife (future tense) to give her a bottle of wine as part of the dower agreement. He fails to give it. What is she entitled to?
A) Mahr al-mithl
B) The specified dower only
C) The value of the wine
D) Nothing, because the promise was unlawful

Key Takeaway
The entitlement to mahr al-mithl for a broken promise is conditional: the benefit must be for the wife, permissible, and the specified dower must be less than mahr al-mithl.

Vague Stipulations in Mahr: Gift or Honour
Intra-Hanafi dispute on vague dower stipulations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two Hanafi views on vague stipulations in mahr and state the reconciled position for divorce before consummation.

Core Idea
A vague promise of gift/honour remains valid if fulfilled; otherwise mahr al-mithl, but before consummation only half the specified dower.

This passage examines an intra-Hanafi dispute: does stipulating an unspecified 'gift' or 'honour' alongside a fixed dower invalidate the naming? The author of al-Hidayah and later commentators reconcile two positions, with practical implications for divorce before consummation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the view of al-Hidayah (and al-Mabsut) that the naming is valid if the husband provides any customary gift/honour, otherwise mahr al-mithl. Then state the opposing view of al-Walwalji and al-Muhit that the naming is fasid from the start due to jahl.
The disagreement is intra-Hanafi, not between madhhabs.
2
Understand the legal reasoning
Analyse the role of jahl (ignorance) in each view. The opposing view holds that jahl in the benefit (gift/honour) is greater than jahl in mahr al-mithl, so mahr al-mithl is more appropriate. The first view says jahl is removed by subsequent fulfillment.
Fulfillment can be minimal, e.g., any act customarily counted as honour.
3
Analyse the effect of divorce before consummation
If divorce occurs before consummation, both views agree that she gets half the specified dower only, not mahr al-mithl, because mahr al-mithl is not halved. The reasoning from al-Bada'i' is that the condition (vague promise) fails, and only the specified dower remains, which is halved.
This is a key point of reconciliation.
4
Reconcile the views
The text reconciles by adopting the position of al-Hidayah, al-Mabsut, and al-Bada'i': if the husband gives something, the naming is sahih; if not, it is fasid and mahr al-mithl is due. But for pre-consumption divorce, only half the specified dower is given because mahr al-mithl does not apply.
The reconciled view is the mufta bihi.
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling
Given a marriage contract with 1000 dirhams and a condition of 'a gift', if the husband gives a small gift, she gets the 1000 if no divorce, or 500 if divorced before consummation. If he gives nothing, she gets mahr al-mithl (if no divorce) or 500 (if divorce before consummation).
The amount of mahr al-mithl must be determined separately.

إذا لم يكرمها ولم يهد لها هدية كما حمل في المبسوط كلام محمد عليه فيوافق ما في الهداية والمبسوط والبدائع. لكن بقي هنا شيء وهو أنه ذكر المسألة في الاختيار شرح المختار بلفظ : ولو تزوجها على ألف وكرامتها قبل الدخول، فإذا كانت متعتها أكثر منه وجبت المتعة فهو نظير ما سيأتي فيما لو تزوجها على هذا العبد أو هذا العبد وأحدهما أوكس فإنه يحكم مهر المثل. وقد قال في الهداية : إن الواجب في الطلاق قبل الدخول في Then know that the author of al-Hidayah mentioned that this issue, i.e., the issue of stipulating a benefit with the specified dower, covers cases where he stipulates honour and a gift with the thousand. Its apparent meaning is that if he fulfills, she gets the specified dower, otherwise she gets mahr al-mithl, as stated in Ghayat al-Bayan regarding the case where one of the two slaves turns out to be free, even though the gift and honour are unknown and fulfilling the unknown is impossible. And it appears that they are not included in this issue. It falls short of his statement: 'And it appears that they are not included.' He said in al-Nahr: I saw in al-Mabsut what supports what is in al-Hidayah, namely that after mentioning Muhammad's statement: 'If he marries her for a thousand and her honour, or that he gives her a gift, she gets her mahr al-mithl, not the thousand,' he said: 'This issue has two aspects: either he honours her or gives her a gift, or he does not honour her nor give her a gift. If he honours her or gives her a gift, then it is fine and she gets the specified dower; otherwise she gets her mahr al-mithl.' This, as you see, is beneficial for absoluteness, and it appears that the least thing that counts as honour or gift is sufficient. And al-Maqdisi in al-Ramz reconciled by saying: It can be said that it is carried on the case where the stipulated gift is specific and the honour is specific, like giving her a servant. Then the naming is invalid, so mahr al-mithl is obligatory. For this reason, al-Walwalji in his Fatawa and the author of al-Muhit said: 'If he marries her for a thousand and her honour, or that he gives her a gift, she gets her mahr al-mithl not less than the thousand, because the honour and gift are unknown in amount, and this ignorance is greater than the ignorance of mahr al-mithl, so recourse is to mahr al-mithl. Then if he divorces her before consummation, she gets half the thousand because what exceeds the thousand is established on the basis of mahr al-mithl, and mahr al-mithl is not halved.' And it is restricted to when he stipulates a benefit for her and does not stipulate something in return. So if he marries her for a thousand and on condition that he divorces his wife so-and-so, and on condition that she returns a slave to him, then she has given the vulva and the slave as a slave-girl. In short, he mentioned what qualifies as dower, and what is in al-Muhit about the unknown is denied. I said: But in al-Bada'i', in the section on what causes half the dower to fall, it is explicit that the unknown is denied, where he said: 'And if he stipulates with the specified dower something that is not property, such as marrying her for a thousand dirhams and on condition that he divorces his other wife, or that he does not take her out of her town, then divorces her before consummation, she gets half the specified dower and the condition falls. Because if he does not fulfill it, complete mahr al-mithl is obligatory, and mahr al-mithl is not established in divorce before consummation, so its consideration falls, leaving only the specified dower, so it is halved. Similarly, if he stipulates with the specified dower something unknown, such as marrying her for a thousand dirhams and that he gives her a gift, then divorces her before consummation, she gets half the specified dower, because if he does not fulfill the honour and gift, complete mahr al-mithl is obligatory, and mahr al-mithl has no role in divorce before consummation, so the consideration of this condition falls.' This also supports what is in al-Hidayah. And his statement 'something unknown' contradicts carrying it on something specific. Rather, it becomes necessary to carry what is in al-Walwalji and al-Muhit on the case where he does not honour her and does not give her a gift, as carried in al-Mabsut regarding Muhammad's statement, thus agreeing with what is in al-Hidayah, al-Mabsut, and al-Bada'i'. But there remains something: He mentioned the issue in al-Ikhtiyar Sharh al-Mukhtar with the wording: 'If he marries her for a thousand and her honour, she gets mahr al-mithl not less than a thousand because he consented to her; and if he divorces her before consummation, she gets half the thousand because it is more than the mut'a.' This shows that what is obliged by divorce before consummation is obliged by virtue of mut'a due to invalidity of the naming, but she only gets half the thousand because when he named the thousand, he consented to an increase over mut'a in the customary amount more than it. Its implication is that if mut'a were more than half the specified dower, mut'a would be obligatory, because the woman did not consent to only the thousand but with something additional, so she is not content with half of it at divorce before consummation. If her mut'a is more than that, then mut'a is obligatory. It is analogous to what will come regarding the case where he marries her for this slave or that slave and one of them is inferior: he is judged by mahr al-mithl. And he said in al-Hidayah: 'What is obligatory in divorce before consummation in such a case is mut'a, and half the inferior exceeds it customarily, so it is obligatory because he admitted the increase.' This indicates the invalidity of the naming, so mahr al-mithl is obligatory before divorce and mut'a after divorce before consummation. By this it appears that what is in al-Walwalji and al-Muhit is another opinion. And it may be said that there is no impediment to saying the naming is invalid on the assumption of no gift and honour, and it is elevated on the assumption of presence of gift and honour because ignorance is removed, as suggested by the statement of al-Mabsut which explained Muhammad's statement. And by divorce before consummation, ignorance is confirmed, so only half the known specified dower is required and the unknown is void, so it is not increased by virtue of naming, because before divorce it was possible to increase over the specified thousand when there was no gift and honour if mahr al-mithl was more than it, considering mahr al-mithl, and mahr al-mithl is not halved by divorce before consummation, so the halving of the thousand is determined.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute over the ruling when the stipulated benefit is vague, such as a gift (هدية) or honour (كرامة) of unspecified value. The author of al-Hidayah holds that if the husband fulfills by giving any gift or honour, the specified dower stands; otherwise, she gets mahr al-mithl. However, scholars like al-Walwalji and the author of al-Muhit argue that such vagueness makes the naming invalid (fasid), so mahr al-mithl is obligatory from the start, and she gets no less than the specified thousand. The discussion intensifies regarding divorce before consummation (qabl al-dukhul). The author reconciles by citing al-Bada'i': if the husband does not fulfill the vague promise, then mahr al-mithl is due but is not halved before consummation; instead, she gets half the specified dower only. This is because mahr al-mithl has no role before consummation, so only the known part of the specified dower is halved. The passage also draws an analogy with the case where one of two slaves named as dower is inferior, leading to mahr al-mithl. Ultimately, the text synthesizes the views: the naming is invalid (fasid) if the husband fails to provide the vague benefit, but upon divorce before consummation, she gets half the specified dower (not mahr al-mithl). If the husband does provide a token gift, the naming becomes valid and she gets the specified dower.

Key Terms
جهالة (jahl): Vagueness or ignorance regarding the amount or nature of the stipulated benefit.
هدية (hadiyya): Gift; in this context, an unspecified gift promised as part of the dower.
متعة (mut'a): Consolatory gift given to a divorced woman before consummation when no mahr was specified or when the dower is fasid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man marries a woman on the condition of giving her a gift (هدية) but does not specify the gift, and then divorces her before consummation, what is she entitled to according to the reconciled view?
A) Half the specified dower only
B) Full specified dower
C) Mahr al-mithl
D) Mut'a

Key Takeaway
Vague stipulations in mahr are not automatically void; fulfillment can cure, but failure triggers mahr al-mithl, except before consummation where only half the specified dower is due.

Invalid Dower with Unknown Additions
Ruling with proof and reconciliation of intra-Hanafi texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on invalid dower specification due to an unknown addition and apply the rule that upon pre-consummation divorce, only the known named amount is halved.

Core Idea
An unknown addition invalidates dower specification, triggering proper dower, but only the known named amount is halved upon divorce before consummation.

In this passage, the author of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a common scenario in marriage contracts: the dower is named but includes an additional condition of undefined value, such as 'honoring the wife' or giving a gift. The ruling is that this specification is invalid, and the wife is entitled to the proper dower (mahr al-mithl). However, if divorce occurs before consummation, the calculation changes. The author also reconciles apparent differences among leading Hanafi texts, providing a nuanced understanding of how the timing of divorce and fulfillment of the condition affect the outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Invalid Specification
Determine that the dower includes a named amount plus an unknown element (e.g., 'honor' or 'gift'). This makes the tasmiya (specification) invalid because the unknown element introduces excessive uncertainty (jahalah).
The unknown element is not property or has unknown value.
2
Apply the Proper Dower Rule
When the specification is invalid, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (proper dower) instead of the named amount, regardless of whether the named amount is less or more.
The proper dower is determined by the dower of women similar to her (e.g., father's sister).
3
Consider Pre-Consummation Divorce
If the husband divorces her before consummation, the proper dower is not halved. Instead, only the known named amount (the specified numeric part) is halved, because the unknown part is void and the proper dower is not established at this stage.
Exception: if the mut'ah (consolatory gift) would be larger than half the named amount, she gets mut'ah instead.
4
Reconcile Conflicting Texts
Some Hanafi sources (al-Walwalji, al-Muhit) appear to say that mahr al-mithl is given even upon pre-consummation divorce, but the author reconciles by noting these sources assume the condition (e.g., gift) was not fulfilled. If the condition was fulfilled, the specification may be valid.
The key distinction is whether the unknown addition was actually provided or not.
5
Analyze the Taxonomy of Scenarios
The passage ends with a comprehensive classification of 288 possible cases based on: nature of condition (beneficial/harmful/neutral), fulfillment by marriage or husband's act, comparison of mahr al-mithl to named amount, timing (before/after consummation), permissibility of benefit, counter-condition, and actual fulfillment.
This demonstrates the depth of Hanafi legal analysis and the principle that rulings are case-specific.

والزوج بذل الألف وشرط الطلاق فينقسم الألف على مهر مثلها وعلى قيمة العبد، فإذا كانا سواء صار نصف الألف ثمناً للعبد ونصفها صداقاً لها، فإذا طلقها قبل أن يدخل بها فلها نصف ذلك، وإن دخل بها نظر إن كان مهر مثلها خمسمائة أو أقل فليس لها إلا ذلك، وإن كان أكثر ، فإن وفى بالشرط فليس لها إلا الخمسمائة وإن أبى أن يطلق فلها كمال المثل، وتمامه في المحيط والمبسوط . وقد علم أن وجوب مهر المثل إنما هو عند الدخول، أما إن طلقها قبله فلها نصف المسمى وبطل شرط المنفعة لها ولذا قال في المبسوط : يجوز أن يصار إلى مهر المثل قبل الطلاق ولا يصار إلى المنفعة بعد الطلاق كما إذا تزوجها على ألف وكرامتها ا هـ. وقد يقال : إن هذه المسألة على وجوه ثلاثة لأن الشرط إما أن يكون نافعاً لها أو لأجنبي أو ضاراً، وكل منها إما أن يكون الوفاء حاصلاً بمجرد النكاح أو متوقفاً على فعل الزوج فهي ستة، وكل من الستة إما أن يكون مهر المثل أكثر من المسمى أو أقل أو مساوياً، وكل من الثمانية عشر إما أن يكون قبل الدخول أو بعده، وكل من الستة والثلاثين إما أن يباح الانتفاع بالشرط أو لا، وكل من الاثنين والسبعين إما أن يشترط عليها رد شيء إليه أو لا، وكل من المائة والأربعة والأربعين إما أن يحصل الوفاء بالشرط أو لا فهي مائتان وثمانية وثمانون فليتأمل.
And only the specification is invalid, so the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) is obligatory. That is why al-Walwalji said in his Fatawa and the author of al-Muhit: If he marries her for one thousand and her honor (karamataha) or for him to give her a gift, then she gets her proper dower not less than one thousand because the honor and gift are of unknown amount, and this ignorance is greater than the ignorance of the proper dower, so one resorts to the proper dower. If he divorces her before consummation, she gets half of the thousand because what is added to the thousand is established based on the proper dower, and the proper dower is not halved. End quote. And it is restricted to the condition being for her benefit and nothing is required from her in return. So if he marries her for one thousand and on condition that he divorce his wife so-and-so, and that she return a slave to him, then she has given her vulva and the slave is a slave woman. In summary, it mentioned what is valid as dower, and what is in al-Muhit regarding the unknown indefinite noun. End quote. I said: But al-Bada'i' mentioned in explaining what cancels half of the dower something explicit that the indefinite noun is unknown, where he said: If he stipulates with the named amount that is property something that is not property, such as marrying her for one thousand dirhams and on condition that he divorce his other wife, or that he not take her out of her town, then he divorces her before consummation, she gets half of the named amount and the condition falls away, because if he does not fulfill it, the entire proper dower is obligatory, and the proper dower is not established in divorce before consummation, so its consideration falls away, leaving only the named amount, so it is halved. Likewise, if he stipulates with the named amount something unknown, like if he marries her for one thousand dirhams and that he give her a gift, then he divorces her before consummation, she gets half of the named amount, because if he does not fulfill the honor and gift, the entire proper dower is obligatory, and the proper dower has no entry in divorce before consummation, so the consideration of this condition falls away. End quote. This also supports what is in al-Hidayah. And his saying 'something unknown' contradicts carrying it to definite; rather, what is in al-Walwalji and al-Muhit must be carried to the case where he did not honor her and did not give her the gift, as is carried in al-Mabsut from Muhammad's statement, so it agrees with al-Hidayah, al-Mabsut, and al-Bada'i'. But something remains here: he mentioned the issue in al-Ikhtiyar Sharh al-Mukhtar with the wording: If he marries her for one thousand and her honor, she gets the proper dower not less than one thousand because he agreed to it, and if he divorces her before consummation, she gets half of the thousand because it is more than the consolatory gift (mut'a). End quote. This indicates that what is obliged by divorce before consummation is obliged by the rule of mut'a due to the invalidity of the specification, but she only gets half of the thousand because when he named the thousand, he agreed to an increase over mut'a that is usually more than it. Its implication is that if mut'a were more than half of the named, mut'a would be obligatory because the woman did not consent only to the thousand but with something extra, so she was not satisfied with half of it by divorce before consummation. So if her mut'a is more than that, mut'a is obligatory. This is analogous to what will come regarding if he marries her on this slave or this slave, one of which is inferior, then proper dower is judged. And al-Hidayah said: The obligatory in divorce before consummation in such a case is mut'a, and half of the inferior is usually more than it, so it is obliged due to his acknowledgment of the increase. End quote. This teaches that the specification is invalid, so proper dower is obligatory before divorce and mut'a after it before consummation. And by this it becomes clear that what is in al-Walwalji and al-Muhit is another statement. And it may be said: There is no obstacle to saying the specification is invalid on the assumption of no gift and no honor, and it is valid on the assumption of existence of gift and honor due to removal of ignorance, as is implied by the statement of al-Mabsut explaining Muhammad's words, and by divorce before consummation the ignorance is established, so only the known half of the named amount is due, and the unknown is void, so no increase on it by virtue of the specification, because before divorce it was possible to increase beyond the named thousand when there was no gift or honor if the proper dower was more than it, by considering proper dower, and proper dower is not halved by divorce before consummation, so the halving of the thousand is determined because the husband paid the thousand and stipulated the divorce, so the thousand is divided between her proper dower and the value of the slave. If they are equal, half of the thousand becomes the price of the slave and half becomes dower for her. If he divorces her before consummation, she gets half of that. If he consummates, consider: if her proper dower is five hundred or less, she gets only that; if it is more, and he fulfills the condition, she only gets five hundred; if he refuses to divorce, she gets the full proper dower. Its completion is in al-Muhit and al-Mabsut. It is known that the obligation of proper dower is only at consummation. As for if he divorces her before it, she gets half of the named amount, and the condition of benefit for her becomes void. That is why al-Mabsut said: It is permissible to resort to proper dower before divorce, but not to resort to the benefit after divorce, as in the case of marriage for one thousand and her honor. End quote. And it may be said: This issue has three categories because the condition is either beneficial to her, to a stranger, or harmful, and each of these is either fulfilled by the mere marriage or dependent on the husband's action, so they are six. Each of the six is either that the proper dower is more than the named, less, or equal, so they are eighteen. Each of the eighteen is either before consummation or after, so they are thirty-six. Each of the thirty-six is either that the use of the condition is permissible or not, so they are seventy-two. Each of the seventy-two is either that a return of something is stipulated from her or not, so they are one hundred forty-four. Each of the one hundred forty-four is either that fulfillment of the condition occurs or not, so they are two hundred eighty-eight. So let it be pondered.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-explanation from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the chapter of dower. It addresses the scenario where the dower is specified (al-tasmiya) but with an unknown or invalid addition, such as a condition of 'honoring her' or giving a gift. The ruling: the specification is invalid (fasida), so the proper dower (mahr al-mithl) becomes obligatory. The author reconciles divergent statements from various Hanafi authorities. The key point: if the husband divorces before consummation (qabl al-dukhul), the wife gets half of the named amount (the one thousand) because the proper dower is not halved—only the known part is. However, if the mut'ah (consolatory gift) would be more than half of the named amount, she gets the mut'ah instead. The passage also introduces a thorough taxonomy of 288 possible scenarios based on the nature of the condition, fulfillment, and consummation, showing the depth of Hanafi legal analysis.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower determined by considering the dower of similar women (e.g., father's sister, etc.)
تسمية (tasmiya): Specification of the dower amount in the marriage contract
متعة (mut'ah): A consolatory gift given to the wife upon divorce before consummation when no dower was specified

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man marries a woman for 1000 dirhams and 'her honor' (a undefined addition), then divorces her before consummation, what does she receive?
A) Half of the proper dower (mahr al-mithl)
B) Half of 1000 dirhams only
C) The full proper dower
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
When a dower specification includes an unknown addition, the specification is invalid, and the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl; however, upon pre-consummation divorce, only the known named amount is halved, not the proper dower.

Conditional Dower: Three Hanafi Views
Second issue: dower conditional on future events, with three Hanafi views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Sahibayn, and Zufar on conditional dower, and apply the qiyas to ijarah to determine the dower amount in a given scenario.

Core Idea
Conditional dower divides Hanafi imams: first condition valid, second invalid (Abu Hanifa) vs. both valid (Sahibayn) vs. both invalid (Zufar).

When a marriage contract specifies different dower amounts depending on future events, the Hanafi school sees a genuine ikhtilaf. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the second issue of the chapter: the dower conditional on events like staying with her, not taking a concubine, etc. Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and Zufar each derive a different ruling by analogizing to a similar dispute in ijarah (hiring contracts). Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to trace how qiyas and textual interpretation generate divergent positions within the same madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
From the passage, extract the ruling of each imam on the validity of the two conditions (first: staying; second: taking out). State clearly what each imam says about the dower amount.
Abu Hanifa: first valid, second invalid; Sahibayn: both valid; Zufar: both invalid.
2
Map the analogy to ijarah
The passage says 'the origin of the issue is in ijarah.' Read the ijarah case: pay 1 dirham if sewn today, ½ dirham if sewn tomorrow. Understand how each imam's view in ijarah corresponds to their view in marriage.
In ijarah, the dispute is whether the second condition (tomorrow) is valid or invalid; this maps directly to the dower conditions.
3
Trace the illa (effective cause)
Identify the illa each imam uses to distinguish valid from invalid conditions. For Abu Hanifa, the second condition introduces uncertainty? For Sahibayn, both are valid because they set clear alternative amounts? For Zufar, both are uncertain?
Qiyas panel in the toolbox can help.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Apply each view to a concrete scenario: husband marries on condition 'if I stay, you get 1000; if I take you out, you get 2000'. He then takes her out. What does she get under each imam?
Abu Hanifa: proper dower between 1000 and 2000 (since second condition invalid). Sahibayn: 2000 (condition satisfied). Zufar: proper dower without bounds.
5
Note the tarjih (if any)
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq does not give tarjih here. Reflect on which view is relied upon in later Hanafi fatwa. This is an exposé of ikhtilaf, not a resolution.
Later authorities may prefer the view of Sahibayn or Abu Hanifa depending on context.

Source Text

الثانية حاصلها أن لها مهراً على تقدير وآخر على تقدير آخر كأن يسمي يتزوجها على ألف إن أقام بها أو إن لا يتسرى أو أن يطلق ضرتها أو إن كانت مولاة أو إن كانت أعجمية أو ثيباً وعلى ألفين إن كان أضدادها، فإن وفى بالشرط أو كانت أعجمية ونحوه فلها الألف وإلا فمهر المثل لا يزاد على ألفين ولا ينقص عن الألف عند أبي حنيفة، وكذا إن قدم شرط الألفين يصح المذكور عنده ، فحاصله أن الشرط الأول صحيح عنده، والثاني فاسد. وقالا : الشرطان جائزان حتى كان لها الألف إن أقام بها والألفان إن أخرجها . وقال زفر الشرطان جميعاً فاسدان وأصل المسألة في الإجارات في قوله «إن خطته درهم وإن خطته غداً فلك نصف درهم فعند الإمام اليوم للتعجيل والغد للإضافة، وعندهما اليوم للتوقيت والغد للإضافة، وعند زفر اليوم للتعجيل والغد للترفيه اليوم فلك
The second (issue) – its summary is that she has a dower on one condition and another on another condition, like if he names: 'I marry her for one thousand if he stays with her, or if he does not take a concubine, or if he divorces her co-wife, or if she is a client (mawla), or if she is a non-Arab, or a virgin, and for two thousand if the opposite of those.' If he fulfills the condition or she is a non-Arab and the like, she gets one thousand; otherwise, the proper dower is not increased beyond two thousand nor decreased below one thousand according to Abu Hanifa. Likewise, if he presents the condition of two thousand, the mentioned condition is valid according to him. So the outcome is that the first condition is valid according to him, and the second is invalid. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: both conditions are valid, so she gets one thousand if he stays with her, and two thousand if he takes her out. And Zufar said: both conditions are invalid. The origin of the issue is in ijarah in his statement: 'If I sew it today, you get one dirham; if I sew it tomorrow, you get half a dirham.' According to the Imam (Abu Hanifa), 'today' is for promptness and 'tomorrow' for deferment; according to the two (Sahibayn), 'today' is for timing and 'tomorrow' for deferment; according to Zufar, 'today' is for promptness and 'tomorrow' for ease. Today, you get...

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about conditional dower (mahr) where the amount depends on a future condition (e.g., staying with her, not taking a concubine, etc.). It summarizes the second issue (الثانية) of the chapter. The rulings: According to Abu Hanifa, the first condition (e.g., staying) is valid and the second (e.g., taking her out) is invalid; so if he fulfills the first, she gets the named amount, otherwise she gets proper dower between the two named amounts. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold both conditions valid, so she gets the amount corresponding to the satisfied condition. Zufar holds both conditions invalid, meaning the dower is unspecified and proper dower applies. The passage analogizes to a case in ijarah (hiring) where payment differs based on when the work is done, showing the qiyas (analogical reasoning) underlying the dispute. The text cuts off mid-sentence, but the legal positions are fully stated.

Key Terms
تقدير (taqdir): A conditional estimation or specification of the dower based on a future event
إجارة (ijarah): Hiring contract; the analogy is drawn to a case where payment varies by completion time

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a man marries a woman on condition that if he stays with her she gets 1000, and if he takes her out she gets 2000, what happens if he takes her out?
A) She gets 2000
B) She gets 1000
C) She gets proper dower not less than 1000 nor more than 2000
D) The marriage is invalid

Key Takeaway
Conditional dower is permissible in the Hanafi school, but the imams differ on whether both alternative amounts are enforceable; this is a classic example of intra-madhhab ikhtilaf resolved by qiyas on ijarah.

Conditional Dowers and Intra-Hanafi Disputes
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conditional dower validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and Zufar on conditional dowers, and evaluate the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf) of each view.

Core Idea
Conditional dowers: Abu Hanifa validates only the immediate condition; Sahibayn validate both; Zufar invalidates both.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute over the validity of dower specifications that depend on the husband's future actions (e.g., staying with the wife or taking her out). The disagreement hinges on the presence of risk (gharar) and the interpretation of an analogy from hire contracts. Understanding this dispute refines our grasp of how conditions in marriage contracts are treated in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Recognize that the dower is specified in two alternative amounts, one conditional on a future event (e.g., 'on a thousand if he stays, on two thousand if he takes her out'). The question is: which, if any, of these specifications is valid?
The condition involves the husband's volitional act, introducing uncertainty.
2
State each imam's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the first (immediate) condition is valid, the second (deferred) is invalid. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold both are valid. Zufar holds both are invalid. Memorize these three positions.
3
Examine the analogy from hire contracts
The text cites the hire case: 'If I sew it today, you get a dirham; if tomorrow, half a dirham.' Abu Hanifa interprets 'today' as immediacy (ta'jil) and 'tomorrow' as deferment (idafah), so only one valid condition. The Sahibayn interpret 'today' as timing (tawqit) allowing both. Understand how this analogy grounds the dispute.
The choice of interpretive lens (ta'jil vs. tawqit) determines the outcome.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Work out the practical dower entitlement under each view in a specific scenario (e.g., husband takes her out). Under Abu Hanifa: mahr al-mithl capped between the two named amounts. Under Sahibayn: if condition met, higher amount; otherwise lower. Under Zufar: always mahr al-mithl.
The difference is significant in practice, especially when dower amounts vary widely.

الجهالة فيه يسيرة
And the husband paid the thousand and stipulated divorce, so the thousand is divided between her mahr al-mithl and the value of the slave. If they are equal, half the thousand becomes the price of the slave and half becomes dower for her. If he divorces her before consummation, she gets half of that. If he consummates, then if her mahr al-mithl is five hundred or less, she has nothing beyond that; if it is more, then if he fulfills the condition, she only has the five hundred; if he refuses to divorce, she gets the full mahr al-mithl. Its completion is in al-Muhit and al-Mabsut. It is known that the obligation of mahr al-mithl is only upon consummation; if he divorces her before, she gets half the named dower and the condition of benefit for her becomes void. Hence he said in al-Mabsut: It is permissible to resort to mahr al-mithl before divorce, but not to benefit after divorce, as when he marries her for a thousand and her honor. It may be said: This issue has three aspects because the condition is either beneficial to her, to a stranger, or harmful. Each of these is either fulfilled simply by marriage or dependent on the husband's action, making six. Each of the six either has mahr al-mithl more than the named, less, or equal, making eighteen. Each of the eighteen either before or after consummation, making thirty-six. Each of the thirty-six either permissible to benefit from the condition or not, making seventy-two. Each of the seventy-two either stipulates a return to him or not, making one hundred forty-four. Each of the one hundred forty-four either has fulfillment of the condition or not, making two hundred eighty-eight. So reflect. The second: Its summary is that she has a dower on one estimation and another on another estimation, such as marrying her on a thousand if he stays with her, or if he does not take a concubine, or divorces her co-wife, or if she is a slave, or non-Arab, or non-virgin, and on two thousand if the opposites. If he fulfills the condition or she is non-Arab etc., she gets the thousand; otherwise, mahr al-mithl, not exceeding two thousand nor less than one thousand according to Abu Hanifa. Similarly, if he presents the condition of two thousand, the mentioned is valid according to him. So his conclusion is that the first condition is valid according to him, and the second is invalid. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Both conditions are permissible, so she gets the thousand if he stays with her, and the two thousand if he takes her out. Zufar said: Both conditions are invalid. The origin of the issue is in hire contracts in his statement: 'If I sew it today, you get a dirham; if I sew it tomorrow, you get half a dirham.' According to the Imam (Abu Hanifa), 'today' is for immediacy and 'tomorrow' for deferment; according to them (the two), 'today' is for timing and 'tomorrow' for deferment; according to Zufar, 'today' is for immediacy and 'tomorrow' for ease. Today you get by virtue of naming; but if the mut'ah is more than that, it is increased due to mut'ah because it is obligatory when the naming is invalid. With this explanation, the statements of al-Mabsut, al-Hidayah, and al-Bada'i align with those of al-Walwaljiyya and al-Muhit. And by this the answer appears to a branch that will come from al-Khaniyya, which the author mentions at the statement of the matn: 'on a garment, wine, or pig, etc.' The branch is his statement in al-Khaniyya: 'If he marries her on ten dirhams and a garment without describing it, she gets ten dirhams; if he divorces her before consummation, she gets five dirhams unless her mut'ah is more than that.' The garment is of unknown type, mentioned with a known named amount, so it is like marrying her on a thousand and that he gives her a gift, for the gift is also of unknown type. So the statement of al-Khaniyya that she gets ten dirhams is interpreted as when the ten is her mahr al-mithl and he did not give her a garment. Book of Nikah, Chapter of Mahr, and al-Taysir. Its completion is in al-Muhit from hire contracts. Know that their statement here about the validity of only the first naming, based on it being immediate, is only valid in his statement 'on a thousand if he stays.' As for something like 'on a thousand if he divorces her co-wife and on two thousand if he does not,' it is the opposite because the immediate now is not divorcing, so the first should be invalid and the second valid. As for something like 'if she is a slave,' it is not known which is immediate from the conditional. The summary of his proof here is that one of the two namings is immediate and the other conditional, so two namings cannot coexist at once. If he takes her out, they have coexisted, so both are invalid. This is because the conditional does not exist before its condition, and the immediate does not cease to exist by the existence of the conditional. So coexistence occurs at the existence of the condition, not before. An objection was raised requesting a distinction between this and the case where he marries her on a thousand if she is ugly and on two thousand if she is beautiful, where both conditions are valid by agreement. He distinguished between them in the goal, saying that risk in the book's issue enters upon the second naming because the husband does not know whether he will take her out or not, and there is no risk in that issue because the woman is of one description but the husband does not know it, and his ignorance does not entail risk. It was refuted in al-Tibyan that it is objected that if he marries her on two thousand if she is free-born, and on a thousand if she is a slave, or on two thousand if he has a wife, and on a thousand if he does not have a wife, there is no risk here but ignorance of the situation. It was approved in Fath al-Qadir, then he said: The better view is to treat the issue of ugly and beautiful as subject to dispute, for it is explicitly stated in Nawadir Ibn Sami'ah from Muhammad that there is dispute in it. This narration was taken from al-Mujtaba. It may be said in the distinction: Although the woman is of one description in all cases, ignorance is strong in [the case of] free descent and its absence and the like because it is not a visible matter; rather, if dispute arises, it needs proof, so there is risk in effect, unlike beauty and ugliness, for they are visible matters, so ignorance of them is slight because it is removed without difficulty. Hence Abu Hanifa validated both namings, as reported by Imam al-Dabusi and the author of Manzilat al-'adm. Therefore, invalidity is established and mahr al-mithl is obligatory, which is ten, and with divorce before consummation, mut'ah is obligatory, consistent with what we have presented. If the statement of al-Khaniyya were interpreted as the author will later interpret it, that mentioning the garment is canceled due to ignorance, so only ten is obligatory, then the consideration of mut'ah upon divorce before consummation would be problematic, considering that ignorance of the gift is greater than ignorance of the garment, for the garment includes linen, silk, cotton, etc., while the gift includes types of clothing, goods, real estate, cash, measured and weighed items. So if mentioning the gift is not canceled, then mentioning the garment should not be canceled a fortiori. So what we said is determined. And Allah knows best. His statement (it may be said in the distinction etc.) is refuted after this by the case: if he marries her on two thousand if he has a wife, and on a thousand if he does not have a wife, for it is also disputed, even though marriage is established by hearsay and does not require proof in case of dispute, so validity would be expected, and that ignorance is slight is contrary to the principle. Thus in al-Nahr, and in it that perhaps he has a wife in another town or absent, unknown to this woman, and there is no doubt about the distinction between this and ugliness and beauty, for the second is a visible matter hidden from no one, unlike his having a wife, which not everyone knows, and ignorance therein is slight.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a critical refinement of rulings on conditional dowers (mahr mu'allaq). It presents intra-Hanafi disputes between Imam Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and Zufar. The discussion begins with a scenario where a husband pays a thousand and stipulates divorce, dividing the sum between dower and a slave's price. The text then enumerates 288 possible logical permutations, demonstrating the complexity. The core issue: a dower conditional on a future event (e.g., staying, not taking a concubine, divorcing a co-wife). Abu Hanifa rules that only the first condition (the immediate one) is valid; the second is invalid. The Sahibayn permit both. Zufar invalidates both. The analogy from hire contracts is cited to explain the reasoning. The text also addresses an objection: why is a conditional dower based on ugliness/beauty valid by agreement, while other conditionals are disputed? The response distinguishes visible vs. non-visible conditions. The passage refines the understanding of gharar (risk) and jahalah (ignorance) in dower conditions. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated here, but the commentary aligns with the later Hanafi preference for the view of the Sahibayn in many cases.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower equivalent to what is customary for women of similar status; used when the named dower is invalid or condition fails.
تسمية (tasmiyah): The act of naming or specifying the dower amount in the marriage contract.
منفعة (manfa'ah): Benefit or advantage stipulated in the marriage contract, e.g., that the husband gives a gift or performs an act.
خطر (khatar): Risk or uncertainty (gharar) that may invalidate a condition in the dower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a man marries a woman on the condition that he will stay with her (1000) or take her out (2000), and he takes her out, what dower is she entitled to if consummation occurred?
A) 1000 (the first condition)
B) 2000 (the second condition)
C) Mahr al-mithl, not exceeding 2000 nor less than 1000
D) Mahr al-mithl with no cap

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on conditional dowers: the validity of a second condition depends on whether it introduces excessive risk (gharar); later practice often follows the Sahibayn for practicality.

Nikah — Marriage
advanced
12 min
Conditional Alternative Dowers: Invalidity of Both Upon Condition
Analysis of dower when one amount is conditional and another is immediate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional alternative dowers and explain why both designations become invalid upon the condition's fulfillment.

Core Idea
When a conditional dower coexists with an immediate one, both invalidate upon the condition's occurrence, triggering mahr al-mithl.

In a marriage contract, the dower (mahr) must be specified. When two alternative amounts are stipulated—one immediate and one conditional—a complex situation arises. The Hanafi school provides a detailed ruling to ensure certainty and avoid risk (khatar). This lesson examines the case where the condition eventually occurs, causing both designations to invalidate and making mahr al-mithl obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the specification of dower (tasmiyah) in a marriage contract with two amounts: one immediate and one conditional. The ruling is that upon the condition's occurrence, both tasmiyas become invalid, and mahr al-mithl becomes wajib.
This is the mufta bihi position of Abu Hanifa.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof lies in the principle that two designations cannot coexist at the same time. The immediate one exists at contract; the conditional one exists only after the condition. When the condition occurs, both are present simultaneously, causing conflict and invalidity due to the prohibition of jahalah (uncertainty).
This is a qiyas (analogical) reasoning, classified as qiyas khafi (subtle analogy).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal reasoning)
The immediate designation is valid at the time of contract. The conditional designation becomes effective only upon fulfillment of its condition. When the condition occurs, both are simultaneously applicable, which is impossible because the dower must be a single, definite amount at any given time. Hence, both are void.
Risk (khatar) arises from the uncertainty of whether the condition will occur, invalidating the second designation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (dispute) on the beauty case
An objection is raised: why is this different from marrying on a thousand if she is ugly and two thousand if beautiful, where both conditions are valid? The response is that beauty is perceptible, so ignorance is slight and quickly resolved, whereas divorce is a future event uncertain to occur, introducing risk.
Some narrations from Muhammad al-Shaybani indicate ikhtilaf on this beauty case, but the stronger view favors validity per Abu Hanifa.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that both tasmiyas are invalid upon the condition's occurrence, and mahr al-mithl is wajib. This is supported by the majority of Hanafi scholars and recorded in al-Muhit and Ghayat al-Bayan.
The intra-madhhab ikhtilaf from Nawadir Ibn Sama'ah is considered weak.
