لم يكن له امرأة لأنه لا مخاطرة هنا ولكن جهل الحال. وارتضاه في فتح القدير ثم قال : والأولى أن تجعل مسألة القبيحة والجميلة على الخلاف فقد نص في نوادر ابن سماعة عن محمد على الخلاف فيها ا.هـ. وقد أخذ هذه الرواية من المجتبى. وقد يقال في الفرق: إن المرأة وإن كانت في الكل على صفة واحدة لكن الجهالة قوية في الحرية أصالة وعدمها ونحوها لأنها ليست أمراً مشاهداً بل إذا وقع فيه التنازع احتاج إلى الإثبات فكان فيه مخاطرة معنى بخلاف الجمال والقبح فإنه أمر مشاهد فيها فجهالته يسيرة لزوالها بلا مشقة فنزلت صحح أبو حنيفة التسميتين كما نقله الإمام الدبوسي رحمه الله وصاحب منزلة العدم، فلذا فيتقرر الفساد ويجب مهر المثل وهو العشرة وبالطلاق قبل الدخول تجب المتعة فيوافق ما قدمناه . ولو حمل كلام الخانية على ما حمله عليه المؤلف فيما سيأتي من أنه يلغو ذكر الثوب لجهالته فتجب العشرة فقط أشكل عليه اعتبار المتعة بالطلاق قبل الدخول على أن جهالة الهدية أفحش من جهالة الثوب فإن الثوب تحته الكتان والحرير والقطن ونحوهما والهدية تحتها أجناس الثياب والعروض والعقار والنقود والمكيل والموزون، فإذا لم يلغ ذكر الهدية يلزم أن لا يلغو ذكر الثوب بالأولى فتعين ما قلنا والله تعالى أعلم قوله (وقد يقال في الفرق الخ يرد بعد هذا ما إذا تزوجها على ألفين إن كان له امرأة وعلى ألف إن لم يكن له امرأة فإنها خلافية أيضاً مع أن النكاح مما يثبت بالتسامع فلا يحتاج إلى إثبات عند المنازعة فكان ينبغي الصحة وكون الجهالة يسيرة خلاف الأصل. كذا في النهر. من المحيط، وكذا ذكر الاتفاق الإمام الولوالجي في فتاواه وغيره وارتضاه في غاية البيان، فما في نوادر ابن سماعة من الخلاف ضعيف. ثم اعلم أن دليل الإمام المذكور هنا لا يشمل ما ذكره أن طلق ضرتها ونحوه كما لا يخفى. وقوله وإلا فمهر المثل عائد إلى المسألتين أي إن لم يوف بما شرط لها في المسألة الأولى ولم يقم بها في الثانية فالواجب مهر المثل. لكن قد علمت أنه في الثانية لا يزاد على التسمية الثانية لرضاها بها، ولا ينقص عن التسمية الأولى لرضاه بها. وأشار بوجوب مهر المثل إلى أنه لو طلقها قبل الدخول فلها نصف المسمى أولاً، سواء وفى بشرطه أو لا، لأن مهر المثل لا يتنصف.
And ease, and its completion in al-Muhit from the book of Ijarat. Know that their statement here about the validity of only the first designation is based on it being immediate, but this is not complete except in his statement 'on a thousand if he stays'. As for cases like 'on a thousand if he divorces her co-wife' and 'on two thousand if he does not divorce', it is the opposite because the immediate now is the absence of divorce, so the first should be invalid and the second valid. As for cases like 'if she is a mawlah', it is not known which is immediate and which is conditional. The sum of his proof here is that one of the two designations is immediate and the other conditional, so two designations do not coexist at the same time. When he divorces her, they both coexist and become invalid. Because the conditional does not exist before its condition, and the immediate does not cease to exist by the existence of the conditional, so coexistence occurs at the existence of the condition, not before. The objection was raised to seek a distinction between this and the case where he marries her on a thousand if she is ugly and two thousand if she is beautiful, where both conditions are valid by agreement. So he distinguished between them in the result by saying that risk in the issue of the book entered upon the second designation because the husband does not know whether he will divorce her or not, and there is no risk in that issue because the woman is of one quality but the husband does not know that, and his ignorance does not cause risk. This was refuted in al-Tabyin by saying that it is refuted by the case where he marries her on two thousand if she was originally free and one thousand if she is a mawlah, or on two thousand if he has a wife and one thousand if he does not have a wife, because there is no risk here but ignorance of the situation. Al-Fath al-Qadir approved this and then said: The better approach is to make the issue of ugly and beautiful based on ikhtilaf, as it is stated in Nawadir Ibn Sama'ah from Muhammad that there is ikhtilaf on it. And he took this narration from al-Mujtaba. It may be said in the distinction: Even though the woman is in all cases of one quality, yet ignorance is strong regarding original freedom and its absence and similar because it is not a perceptible matter; rather, when dispute occurs, it requires proof, so there is risk in meaning, unlike beauty and ugliness because it is a perceptible matter in her, so ignorance of it is slight because it is removed without hardship. Therefore, Abu Hanifa validated both designations as transmitted by Imam al-Dabusi and the author of Manzilat al-'Adam, so the invalidity is established and mahr al-mithl is obligatory, which is ten, and by divorce before consummation, mut'ah is obligatory, agreeing with what we have presented. If the statement of al-Khaniyah is interpreted as the author later does that the mention of cloth is void due to ignorance, so only ten is obligatory, then the consideration of mut'ah at divorce before consummation becomes problematic, whereas ignorance of a gift is more gross than ignorance of cloth, because cloth includes linen, silk, cotton, etc., while a gift includes types of garments, goods, real estate, coins, measured and weighed items. So if the mention of a gift is not void, then the mention of cloth should not be void a fortiori, so what we said is established, and Allah knows best. The statement 'It may be said in the distinction' etc. is refuted by this: the case where he marries her on two thousand if he has a wife and one thousand if he does not have a wife is also a matter of ikhtilaf, even though marriage is established by reputation and does not require proof in case of dispute, so validity should be assumed, and slight ignorance is against the principle. Thus in al-Nahr. From al-Muhit, and similarly Imam al-Walwaliji mentioned agreement in his Fatawa and others, and it was approved in Ghayat al-Bayan, so what is in Nawadir Ibn Sama'ah of ikhtilaf is weak. Then know that the proof of the Imam mentioned here does not include what he mentioned about divorcing her co-wife etc., as is not hidden. And his statement 'otherwise mahr al-mithl' refers back to the two issues: i.e., if he does not fulfill what he stipulated for her in the first issue and does not make it happen in the second, then the obligatory is mahr al-mithl. But you have known that in the second, no more than the second designation is given due to her consent to it, and no less than the first designation is given due to his consent to it. He indicated by the obligation of mahr al-mithl that if he divorces her before consummation, she gets half of the named dower first, whether he fulfills the condition or not, because mahr al-mithl is not halved.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion on the ruling of dower when specified as two alternative amounts, one conditional and one immediate. The author begins by explaining the base ruling from the matn: if a woman is married on a conditional dower (e.g., 'on a thousand if he divorces her co-wife' and 'on two thousand if he does not'), the immediate designation is the opposite of what one might assume. The key principle is that only one designation can be effective at the time of the contract; if both are present, the immediate one prevails. However, when the condition occurs, both designations coexist and both become invalid because they cannot be simultaneously valid. This leads to the obligation of mahr al-mithl. The author then discusses an objection: why is this not the same as the case of marrying on a thousand if she is ugly and two thousand if she is beautiful, where both conditions are agreed to be valid? The initial response distinguishes based on risk: in the marring case, the husband knows he may divorce her, introducing risk into the second designation, while in the beauty case, there is no risk because the woman is one entity and the husband's ignorance is not considered risk. This response is refuted by comparing to cases involving freedom or existence of a wife, where there is no risk but only ignorance. Fath al-Qadir suggests that the beauty case should be treated as a matter of ikhtilaf, citing a narration from Nawadir Ibn Sama'ah that Abu Hanifa's follower Muhammad al-Shaybani differed. The author then offers his own distinction: ignorance about freedom requires proof in case of dispute and thus constitutes risk in meaning, while beauty is perceptible and ignorance is quickly resolved, so Abu Hanifa validated both designations in the beauty case. Consequently, the invalidity of the dower is established, and mahr al-mithl is wajib. The author further clarifies that if divorce occurs before consummation, the woman gets half of the named dower (the immediate amount) and mut'ah, not half of mahr al-mithl, because mahr al-mithl is not divided. The passage ends by addressing an objection from al-Khaniyah regarding the voiding of the dower due to ignorance of the object.

Key Terms
التسمية (tasmiyah): The specification or naming of the dower amount in the marriage contract.
المهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower of a woman of similar status to the bride, used when the specified dower is invalid or unspecified.
الخطر (khatar): Risk or uncertainty in the dower specification that renders it invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a man marries a woman on a conditional dower (e.g., 1000 if he divorces her co-wife, 2000 if not) and he does NOT divorce her, what is the ruling on the dower?
A) The first designation (1000) is valid and wajib.
B) The second designation (2000) is valid and wajib.
C) Both designations are invalid and mahr al-mithl is wajib.
D) The lower amount is wajib per the Sahibayn.

Key Takeaway
In conditional alternative dowers, the immediate designation at contract is the valid one until the condition occurs; thereafter both invalidate, making mahr al-mithl wajib.
